📝 한글
**번역:**

문제: Gottlieb의 표준화된 양식에서 제시된 책임제한 조항이 계약의 일부였는지 여부

법원은 어떤 규칙을 사용하여 이 문제를 판단할까요?
**UCC 2-207** (UCC는 Uniform Commercial Code의 약자로, 상업 거래에 관한 통일법규를 의미합니다. 여기서 CL 대신 UCC를 사용하는 이유는 거래가 상품의 매매와 관련이 있기 때문입니다.)

판매되는 것은 무엇인가요? 상품인가요? 이동 가능하고 물리적인 물건인가요?
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether the limitation of liability clause from Gottlieb’s standardized form was part of the contract
What Rule does the court use to decide the issue?
UCC 2-207. Why are we using the UCC here instead of the CL?
What is being sold? Is it a good? A movable and tangible thing?
Paul Gottlieb v. Alps South Corp.slide 89
📝 한글
법원은 양식에 기재된 계약을 인정했습니다. 그러나 고틀리브의 수락서에는 계약에 (추가 조항: 계약 당사자 간에 미리 합의되지 않은 새로운 조건) "추가적인" 조항이 포함되어 있어 그로 인해 어떠한 간접 손해에 대한 책임도 면제되는 내용이 있었습니다. subsection (2)에 따르면, 수락서에 있는 ("추가적인" 조항: 계약 당사자 간에 미리 합의되지 않은 새로운 조건) "추가적인" 조항은 계약의 본질적인 내용을 변경할 경우 계약의 일부가 되지 않습니다. 따라서 주요 쟁점은 다음과 같습니다: "고틀리브의 양식에 기재된 손해 제한 조항이 (추가 조항) 계약의 본질적인 내용을 변경했는지 여부"
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The court found a contract on the forms. Gottlieb’s acceptance, however, contained an “additional” term that excluded any liability for consequential damages. Under subsection (2), an “additional” term on an acceptance will not be part of the contract if it materially alters it.
The main issue is therefore: “Whether the limitation of damages clause [on Gottlieb’s form], as an additional term, materially altered the contract”
Paul Gottlieb v. Alps South Corp.slide 90
📝 한글
법원은 다음 규칙을 사용하여 책임 조항의 중요성 여부를 판단합니다:
- **Alps (중요 조항)** 배제를 청구하는 당사자는 그 중요성을 입증해야 합니다.
- Alps는 ** surprise (예상치 못한 조항)** 을 입증해야 합니다: “상황상 합리적인 상인이 추가 조항에 동의했을 것이라고 추정할 수 없음”
- Alps는 이 surprise가 ** hardship (어려움)** 을 초래했다는 것을 입증해야 합니다: “비동의 당사자에게 실질적인 경제적 어려움”
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The court uses the following Rules to determine if the liability term is material:
The party seeking exclusion of the material term (Alps) has the burden of proving its materiality
Alps must show surprise— “that, under the circumstances, it cannot be presumed that a reasonable merchant would have consented to the additional term”
Alps must show that this surprise caused hardship. “substantial economic hardship on the non-consenting party”
Paul Gottlieb v. Alps South Corp.slide 91
📝 한글
알프스는 이 용어가 포함된 여섯 개의 계약서를 전혀 읽지 않았기 때문에 놀랐다고 주장합니다. (알프스는 해당 용어가 포함된 계약서들을 전혀 검토하지 않았기 때문에 놀랐다고 주장합니다.)

이것은 적절한 종류의 놀라움이 아닙니다! (이는 법적으로 인정되는 '예상치 못한 상황'의 요건을 충족하지 못합니다.) 해당 용어가 이례적이거나 이례적이라는 점을 입증해야 합니다.

이러한 종류의 놀라움에 대한 증거가 없습니다. 고틀리브는 알프스가 어떠한 간접적 손해도 입지 않을 것이라고 믿을 이유가 없었으며, 알프스가 어떠한 배상금을 지불할 것이라고 믿게 할 어떠한 행동도 취하지 않았습니다.
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Alps argues that it was surprised because it never read the six contracts containing this term.
This is not the right kind of surprise! Need to show that the term is unexpected in the sense that it is unusual or strange
No evidence of this kind of surprise. Gottlieb had no reason to believe that Alps would suffer any consequential damages and did nothing to lead Gottlieb to believe that it would pay any.
Paul Gottlieb v. Alps South Corp.slide 92
📝 한글
판결: Gottlieb의 책임을 제한하는 조항은 핵심 조항이 아니었다. 따라서 (2)에 따라 계약의 일부이며, Gottlieb은 간접적 손해에 대한 책임을 지지 않는다.

(핵심 조항: 핵심적인 내용이나 조건을 결정하는 중요한 조항을 의미합니다. 간접적 손해: 계약 당사자가 예측 가능한 범위를 벗어난 손해를 의미합니다.)
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Holding: The term limiting Gottlieb’s liability was not a material term. It is thus part of the contract under (2), and Gottlieb cannot be liable for consequential damages.
Paul Gottlieb v. Alps South Corp.slide 93
📝 한글
알프스가 제시해야 했던 증거는 무엇인가?
(증거: 사건 해결에 필요한 사실 확인 자료)
일반적으로, 관습과 관행을 통해 놀라움이 입증된다.
(놀람: 예상치 못한 상황이나 조건으로 인한 당사자의 불만)
정상적인 상인이 이러한 조건에 이의 없이 동의했을 것인가?
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What evidence should Alps have presented?
Surprise is generally proven by reference to custom and usage. Would a normal merchant have consented to these terms without objection?
Layered and Electronic Contractingslide 94
📝 한글
문제는 제품 포장 내부 또는 웹사이트에 기재된 "Terms and Conditions" (계약 조건)이 계약의 일부인지 여부입니다. 이는 상호 동의의 문제입니다. (계약 당사자 간의 합의) 이 문제는 상품이나 서비스의 판매 상황에서 발생할 수 있습니다.
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The issue is whether the “Terms and Conditions” found inside the packaging of a product or on a website are part of the contract.
This is an issue of mutual assent. It could arise in the sale of goods or services.
Shrinkwrapslide 95
📝 한글
포장 내부에 약관이 기재되어 있습니다. (약관: 계약서에 명시된 규정 사항) 구매자는 제품을 개봉하고 보관함으로써 약관에 동의하는 것으로 간주됩니까?
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The terms and conditions are found inside the packaging.
Does the buyer agree to the terms and conditions by opening and keeping the product?
Majority Approachslide 96
📝 한글
판매자는 제안자로 간주됩니다. 제안 조건은 고객(수락자)이 제품을 보관함으로써만 수락할 수 있음을 명시합니다. 고객이 포장을 개봉하기 전까지는 조건을 확인하지 못하더라도, 제안은 고객이 제품을 반환함으로써 조건을 거부할 수 있음을 명시합니다. 이를 "다층 계약"이라고 하며, 계약 성립이 여러 단계를 거쳐 이루어집니다.

(Layered contracting: 여러 단계를 거치며 계약 조건이 점진적으로 제시되는 방식)
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The Seller is viewed as the offeror. The offer provides that the customer (offeree) can only accept by keeping the product.
Although the customer does not see the terms until she opens the package, the offer states that the customer can reject the terms by returning the good.
This is called “layered” contracting because formation occurs over several steps
Majority Approachslide 97
📝 한글
판매자는 다음을 명확히 해야 합니다:

* **(Terms and Conditions: 계약 조건)** 고객의 제품 수령은 계약 조건 수용을 의미하며,
* 고객은 제품 반환을 통해 계약 조건을 거부할 수 있습니다.
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Seller must show that its terms and conditions make it clear that:
Customer’s acceptance of the product is also an acceptance of the terms and conditions; and
Customer can reject the terms and conditions by returning the product
Majority Approachslide 98
📝 한글
이유: 실질적 고려사항: 그렇지 않으면 현금수취인은 판매 전에 모든 약관을 읽고 고객의 동의를 받아야 하며, 이는 당사자 중 한 명이 상인이 아닌 경우 2-207조에 따른 추가 약관이 계약의 일부가 될 수 없기 때문입니다. (*약관: 계약 내용을 규정하는 세부 조항들, *상인: 상업 활동을 주로 하는 개인이나 기업을 의미하며, 법적 보호와 책임의 범위가 일반 소비자보다 넓음)
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rationale: Practical considerations: otherwise the cashier would need to read all terms and conditions before sale and get customer to agree to them, because additional terms are never part of the K under 2-207 when one party isn’t a merchant
Minority Approachslide 99
📝 한글
고객은 구매 제안을 하며, Shrinkwrap 내의 조건은 추가 약관입니다. UCC의 '형식 간의 전투' 규정에 따라, 고객이 상인이 아니므로 추가 약관은 명시적 동의 없이 계약의 일부가 아닙니다. (Shrinkwrap: 제품 포장 내에 포함된 사용 설명서나 약관, UCC: 미국 통일상법전)
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The customer offers to purchase, and the terms and conditions in the shrinkwrap are additional terms. Applying the UCC Battle of the Forms, the additional terms are not part of the contract unless the customer explicitly agrees to them because the customer is not a merchant.
DeFontes v. Dellslide 100
📝 한글
사실관계:
다수의 소비자들이 전화 및 인터넷을 통해 컴퓨터를 구매하였습니다.
원고들은 Dell을 결함 제품으로 인해 소송을 제기하고 있으며, Dell은 이 사건을 중재로 이관하려고 합니다.
컴퓨터 박스 안에 포함된 서류상의 중재 조항
문제점: 중재 조항의 적용 여부
조약 체결 시점은 언제로 볼 것인가? Dell이 결제를 받고 물품을 발송한 시점인가, 아니면 고객이 물품을 수령한 시점인가?

(중재 조항: 분쟁 해결을 위해 중재 기관을 통한 비공개 협상을 요구하는 계약 조항)
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts:
Several consumers bought computers: one over phone, the others over internet.
The Plaintiffs file a lawsuit against Dell based on defective products, and Dell seeks to force the case into arbitration.
The Arbitration provision on paperwork that is in the cardboard box with the computers
Issue: whether arbitration provision applies
When did formation occur? When Dell took payment and shipped goods? Or when customer kept the goods?
DeFontes v. Dellslide 101
📝 한글
컴퓨터 시스템의 인도를 수락함으로써, **(고객)** 은 다음 조건에 동의하고 이를 준수하기로 약속합니다. (Terms and Conditions)
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
“By accepting delivery of the computer systems, . . . You (‘Customer’) agree to be bound by and accept these terms and conditions”
Holdingslide 102
📝 한글
델은 제안자로서 행동을 통한 수락 초대가 가능하며, 그 행동이 수락과 동등한 제한을 가할 수 있습니다. (제안자는 행동을 통해 수락을 유도할 수 있으며, 이 행동은 수락의 범위를 제한할 수 있습니다.) 즉, Shrinkwrap 조건은 제안의 일부이며, 고객의 수락은 조건을 거부할 합리적인 기회가 없을 때까지 완전하지 않습니다.

그러나 판매자는 다음을 명확히 해야 합니다:
(1) 제품을 수락하는 것은 조건 및 약관을 수락하는 것을 의미합니다. (수락 시 약관 동의 포함)
(2) 소비자는 제품을 반환함으로써 조건 및 약관을 거부할 수 있습니다. (반품을 통한 거부 가능)

**DeFontes v. Dell**
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Dell, as the offeror, can invite acceptance by conduct and put limitations on conduct that equals acceptance
In other words, the shrinkwrap terms are part of the offer, and customer’s acceptance isn’t complete until she has a reasonable chance to refuse the terms.
However, the Seller must show that its terms and conditions make clear that:
(1) accepting product meant accepting the terms and conditions
(2) consumer could reject the terms and conditions by returning the product
DeFontes v. Dell
Application:slide 103
📝 한글
델의 양식에 따르면, 배송 수락을 통해 소비자는 약관을 수락하는 것으로 간주됩니다. (Dell의 양식에 따라 배송 수령은 약관 동의로 간주됩니다.)

그러나 양식은 상품을 보유하는 것이 약관 수락임을 명확히 하지 않습니다. (명확한 반환 기간이 명시되지 않아 소비자는 포장 개봉이 약관 동의로 오해할 수 있습니다.)

또한 양식은 소비자가 상품 반환을 통해 약관을 거부할 수 있음을 명시하지 않습니다. (양식은 상품 반환이 가능하다고만 언급하고 있어, 이는 약관 거부를 의미하지 않습니다.)
반품이 약관 거부를 의미한다는 내용이 명시되어야 합니다.

DeFontes v. Dell
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Dell’s form says that, by accepting delivery, the consumer accepts the terms
However, the form doesn’t clearly say that keeping the goods is acceptance of terms. This is not clear, because it doesn’t give a time period in which to return – consumer may think that opening package is acceptance of terms
The form also doesn’t say consumer can reject terms by returning the goods. Its says that the goods can be returned, but this is not the same thing. It must say that returning the goods is a rejection of the terms.
DeFontes v. Dell
Browserwrapslide 104
📝 한글
고객은 웹페이지 이용을 통해 (Terms of Service: 서비스 이용 약관) 약관에 동의하시나요?
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Does the customer agree to the terms and conditions by using the webpage?
Terms of Service
Clickwrapslide 105
📝 한글
웹사이트는 (웹사이트: 인터넷을 통해 정보를 제공하는 플랫폼) 귀하가 동의를 표시하는 버튼을 클릭하도록 강제합니다. (동의: 특정 조건이나 약관에 대한 수락)
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The website forces you to click on a button showing your agreement
Majority Approach: Browser and Click Wrapslide 106
📝 한글
"이용약관"은 사용자가 실제 또는 추정상의 지식을 갖게 되었을 때에만 계약의 일부가 됩니다. 따라서 이용약관은 합리적인 고객이 실제로 볼 수 있는 위치에 있어야 합니다. (이용약관: 웹사이트 이용과 관련된 규정 (Terms and Conditions)) 웹사이트를 구축한 당사자는 증명 책임이 있습니다.
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The “Terms and Conditions” will become part of the contract only if the user has actual or constructive knowledge
The terms and conditions thus must be located in a place where a reasonable customer will actually see them.
Party who built the website has the burden of proof
Clickwrapslide 107
📝 한글
클릭워랩은 고객이 약관에 동의하기 전에 진행을 강제하기 때문에 브라우저워랩보다 규정 준수 가능성이 훨씬 높습니다. (클릭워랩: 사용자가 특정 조건에 동의하지 않으면 진행이 불가능한 방식 (클릭으로 동의를 완료), 브라우저워랩: 웹 브라우저를 통해 자동으로 약관에 동의하게 되는 방식)
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Because clickwrap forces the customer to agree to the terms and conditions before moving on, it is much more likely to meet the rule than browserwrap
4
Promissory Estoppel
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Promissory Estoppel이 뭐냐면... 계약이 아니야. Consideration도 없어. 그런데도 법원이 약속을 강제하는 경우가 있어 — 상대방이 그 약속을 믿고 행동했고, 강제하지 않으면 불공평하면. 3가지 요건: ① 약속(Promise) ② 약속자가 합리적으로 예견할 수 있는 수준의 상대방 의존(Reasonable Reliance) ③ 약속을 강제하지 않으면 불공평한 결과(Injustice). 셋 다 있어야 해. 왜 중요하냐면... 손해배상 범위가 달라. Contract 위반이면 기대이익(Expectation Damages) 청구 가능. Promissory Estoppel은 보통 Reliance Damages(믿고 지출한 비용)만 인정돼.
판례 — Harvey v. Dow: Harvey는 부모 Dow 씨 부부가 자기에게 땅을 줄 거라고 믿었어. 아버지가 "나중에 줄게"라고 막연하게 말했어. Harvey는 그 믿음으로 건축 준비까지 했어. 법원은 구체적인 약속도 없고, 그 약속이 구체적 행동을 유발할 만큼 충분하지 않았다고 봤어 — Promissory Estoppel 실패. 약속이 충분히 명확하고 구체적이어야 해.
Charitable Subscriptions: 자선 기부 약속은 특별히 Consideration 없어도 일부 법원에서 PE로 집행해 — 공익 목적이라는 정책적 이유.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Contract law concerns itself with three types of “binding obligations”slide 108
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Contract
Promissory Estoppel
Restitution
Manifestation of mutual assent, bargain in exchange & consideration
Promise plus detrimental reliance
No promise but confers a benefit that is accepted
Promissory Estoppelslide 109
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) Contracts § 90(1)
A promise which the promisor should reasonably expect to induce action or forbearance on the part of the promisee or a third person and which does induce such action or forbearance is binding if injustice can be avoided only by enforcement of the promise. The remedy granted for breach may be limited as justice requires.
Promissory Estoppelslide 110
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Elements:
Promise
Reasonable Reliance
Injustice can be avoided only by enforcement of the promise.
Promissory Estoppel
Importanceslide 111
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The distinction between contract liability and liability in promissory estoppel matters when we get to damages.
Exampleslide 112
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Plaintiff is a widow who lives with her three children. Plaintiff owns a home. Defendant, her brother-in-law tells plaintiff that he will give her a place to live and land to cultivate if she will move near him. Plaintiff sold her home and moved to live with Defendant. Defendant gave Plaintiff a house to live in and land to farm. After two years, however, Defendant evicted Plaintiff. Can Plaintiff recover from Defendant under promissory estoppel?
Harvey v. Dowslide 113
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Harvey is the daughter of the Dows
Dows had a general, non-specific plan to give land to Harvey at some time on their homestead
Harvey built a home on the Dows’ property, with their permission. The Dows helped Harvey get a permit.
Dows helped Harvey build the home
Relationship between Harvey and the Dows deteriorates, and the Dows refuse to give Harvey a deed
Issue: Whether the doctrine of promissory estoppel applies to the Dows’ promise to give land to Harvey
Harvey v. Dowslide 114
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
PE Rule:
Restatement § 90(1): PE applies to (1) promise (2) reasonable reliance; and (3) injustice can be avoided only by enforcement of the promise.
Do we have a “promise”?
The Dows contend there is no promise because they did not make an express promise to convey any specific parcel of land
Harvey v. Dowslide 115
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Do we have a “promise”?
Rule: A promise is a “manifestation of intention to act in a specified way.” “The promise relied on by the promisee need not be express but may be implied from a party’s conduct”
Application: a promise . . . to convey that specific parcel could be implied from his conduct, including “the Dows’ acquiescence, support, and encouragement of Teresa’s construction of a house upon the property”
Harvey v. Dowslide 116
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement § 90(1): (1) promise (2) reasonable reliance; and (3) injustice can be avoided only by enforcement of the promise.
(2) She relied by building the house. This was reasonable because Dow promised to convey land, approved and acquiesced in building the home, assisted in construction, obtained a building permit, etc., Dow should have reasonably expected Harvey to build.
Harvey v. Dowslide 117
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
PE Rule: Restatement § 90(1): PE applies to (1) promise (2) reasonable to expect reliance; (3) reliance; and (4) injustice can be avoided only by enforcement of the promise.
(3) Injustice only be avoided by enforcing the promise. Without enforcement, Harvey would lose a house worth $200,000. Harvey relied on the promise to her detriment
Hypotheticalslide 118
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if Teresa had merely put a mobile home on the property, and mobile home remained mobile at the time of the lawsuit?
Teresa would not have relied to her detriment, so no PE
Hypotheticalslide 119
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if the Dows did not live on the property, did not help with construction of the home, and were unaware of Teresa’s conduct?
Then there would be no implied promise to convey the land.
This doesn’t necessarily mean that the parents get to keep the house for free though!
Harvey v. Dowslide 120
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if, instead of Teresa’s parents, the Dows were acquaintances?
Now the reliance may not be reasonable or foreseeable
Harvey v. Dowslide 121
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if Teresa were a real estate attorney?
Even though she would not have been reasonable in thinking the implied promise was enforceable, because of the family relationship she may have been reasonable in thinking that her parents would voluntarily perform.
Commercial Promisesslide 122
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Up to this point, we have looked at promissory estoppel in cases involving promises between family members and to charities. Promissory estoppel can also be available in commercial settings.
Katz v. Danny Dare, Inc.slide 123
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material facts:
Katz worked for DD for 25 years
The president of DD was Katz’s brother-in-law
Katz was injured on the job, after which time his performance was unacceptable
DD therefore offered Katz a pension if he would retire
Katz initially refused, but eventually agreed.
DD passed a resolution stating that it will pay Katz $13,000 per year for the rest of his life, and Katz retires
Katz would not have retired without the pension, but DD would have fired Katz if he had not accepted the pension
DD then stops paying the pension when Katz is 70 years old
Katz v. Danny Dare, Inc.slide 124
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether Dare’s promise to provide Katz a pension is enforceable under Promissory Estoppel
Element #1:
Promise = manifestation of intent to act or refrain from acting so that the Promisee knows that a commitment has been made.
Application: Danny Dare made a commitment to Katz to pay the pension
Katz v. Danny Dare, Inc.slide 125
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Element #3: Did the promise to pay Katz induce reasonable reliance by Katz?
Dare contends that Katz didn’t rely on the promise, because he did not give up anything he was legally entitled to receive. If Katz had not agreed to retire, he would have been fired. Moreover, Katz was free to work elsewhere
Court holds that Katz need not show that he gave up anything to which he was legally entitled. Instead, “reliance” is present if the promise induced Katz to take any action that he was not required to undertake
Katz relied on the promise by retiring, when he did not have to retire. The facts show that, even though Dare was legally entitled to fire Katz at will, it was reluctant to do so
This case shows us that any change in position = reliance. Expenditures are not needed!
Katz v. Danny Dare, Inc.slide 126
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Element #3: Can injustice only be avoided by enforcement?
Yes, Katz received payments until he was 70. At that point, he could not work.
Hypothetical 1slide 127
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith worked as a loyal employee at Big Corp. for 30 years. Due to poor economic conditions, Big Corp. decides to lay off a number of employees, including Smith. However, Big Corp. tells Smith that he will receive half of his former compensation as a pension for the remainder of his life. Four years later, Big Corp. stops paying Smith. Does Smith have a valid promissory estoppel claim against Big Corp.?
Yes, because Smith relied on Big Corp.’s promise by retiring
Yes, because Smith and Big Corp. had a contract
No, because Smith did not rely on Big Corp.’s promise
No, because Big Corp. did not make a valid promise

Yes, because Smith relied on Big Corp.’s promise by retiring

Yes, because Smith gave consideration
No, because Smith did not rely on Big Corp.’s promise

Aceves v. U.S. Bankslide 131
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
During the financial crisis, Aceves gets into debt and stops paying her mortgage. She has a mortgage with US Bank. Aceves goes into bankruptcy, which automatically freezes all of her assets so that creditors cannot seize them. Aceves agrees to lift the stay in bankruptcy after US Bank promises to negotiate with her to modify and reinstate the loan. After the stay is lifted, however, US Bank only gives her days to get current on her mortgage and pay all fees and interest charges. When she cannot pay, US Bank sells the house in foreclosure. Aceves sues under Promissory Estoppel.
Aceves v. U.S. Bankslide 132
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Element #1: Promise
US Bank promised to work with Aceves to try to modify the loan
US Bank says that no results were promised, and the promise is too unclear to enforce
Court holds that, to be enforceable, a promise need only be definite enough so the court can determine scope of the duty and a rational basis for damages
Aceves v. U.S. Bankslide 133
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Element #2: Reasonable Reliance
Aceves relied by deciding not to use the bankruptcy laws to save her house. Reliance was reasonable because the bankruptcy court could not change the term of the loan or the interest rate, but US Bank could through a loan modification
Element #3: Would injustice result if the promise is not enforced?
US Bank argued that it was possible that Aceves would never reached an agreement to modify the mortgage. In others, injury was speculative or uncertain.
Court holds that it is enough that she could have saved her house in Bankruptcy
Aceves v. U.S. Bankslide 134
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if, instead of promising to negotiate to modify the loan, a U.S. Bank representative had promised to look into whether the Bank might give the Aceves more time to become current on the loan. The representative, however, refused to put anything into writing or “make any guarantees.” Further assume that the representative did not look into the issue.
Aceves v. U.S. Bankslide 135
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if, instead of promising to negotiate to modify the loan, a U.S. Bank representative had promised to look into whether the Bank might give the Aceves more time to become current on the loan. The representative, however, refused to put anything into writing or “make any guarantees.” Further assume that the representative did not look into the issue.
Here, US Bank broke its promise, but reliance probably was not reasonable or foreseeable
Drennan v. Star Paving Co.slide 136
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Drennan is a general contractor that is soliciting bids from subcontractors for a project. Star Paving submits the lowest bid for the paving work, and Drennan uses this bid in calculating its bid for the overall project. Drennan is awarded the contract, but Star says that it cannot honor its quote because it made a mistake in calculating the cost of the paving work.
Drennan v. Star Paving Co.slide 137
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether Star is liable under PE
Defendant subcontractor revoked his offer before Plaintiff general contractor accepted it
No option contract was formed, so the offer was revocable
Drennan v. Star Paving Co.slide 138
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Promise
Court implies a promise. It finds that Star’s offer constituted a promise to perform on the condition that Drennan was awarded the general contract.
This is true even though Star never explicitly made such a promise!
Drennan v. Star Paving Co.slide 139
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rationale: The court says the promise can be implied from the facts or “annexed thereto by operation of law.”
In other words, this promise is implied in law
The court is saying that, even though no actual promise was made, the court will act as if a promise was made because otherwise the result will be unfair
Drennan v. Star Paving Co.slide 140
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if Drennan had received 5 bids: 4 bids for about $15,000, and Star’s bid was for $2,000?
Drennan v. Star Paving Co.slide 141
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if Drennan had received 5 bids: 4 bids for about $15,000, and Star’s bid was for $2,000?

Pop’s Cones v. Resorts International Hotelslide 142
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Pop’s is a franchisee of TCBY frozen yogurt
Resorts leases prime retail space
Pop’s has a number of conversations with Phoenix, an executive at Resorts about relocating
Pop’s makes a proposal to Resorts to lease space, tells Phoenix he wants an answer because its other lease needs to be renewed
Phoenix responds that “we are 95% there” and that they just need an executive’s signature. Phoenix assures Pop’s that the deal will go through. Phoenix advises Pop’s not to renew its current lease
Pop’s notifies its landlord that it will not renew
Resorts then withdraws from the deal.
Pop’s Cones v. Resort International Hotelslide 143
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether there is a question of fact as to whether Pop’s has a cause of action under PE
Rule: (1) Promise; (2) Reasonable reliance; (3) Injustice can be avoided only by enforcement of the promise.
Pop’s Cones v. Resort International Hotelslide 144
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Promise
Phoenix (executive director of business development and sales for Resorts) promised to lease a space to Pop’s.
Resorts argues that the promise is not clear enough for PE, because they did not agree on a lease term or amount
Court holds that the promise is clear enough for PE because we can tell that it was breached, and we can fashion a remedy
Pop’s Cones v. Resort International Hotelslide 145
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
2. Reliance was reasonable and foreseeable.
Pops did not renew its lease based on this assurances. This was reasonable because Mr. Phoenix instructed him not to renew his lease and said that they were 95% there. All that was left was for John Belisle to sign. Phoenix also said he had recommended the deal to Belisle and that Belisle would follow that recommendation.
The fact that Pop’s is an unsophisticated small business owner matters!
Pop’s Cones v. Resort International Hotelslide 146
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
3. Injustice: This led to costs of moving/relocating.
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 87slide 147
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
(2) An offer which the offeror should reasonably expect to induce action or forbearance of a substantial character on the part of the offeree before acceptance and which does induce such action or forbearance is binding as an option contract to the extent necessary to avoid injustice.
Recall option contracts. We said you needed consideration for an option contract. However, even if there is no consideration, there could be liability if a party relied on an offer! In other words, reliance substitutes for consideration and can make revoking an offer prior to acceptance a problem
Practice Essay #2slide 148
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Kyla lives in downtown Chicago, but she has always loved the outdoors.  Sick of living in the city all year, she buys a cabin in the woods near Baldwin, Michigan. Baldwin is a small town with a population of about 1,200 people. However, Baldwin has a number of seasonal cabins and tourism due to its excellent salmon and steelhead fishing. Kyla’s cabin is relatively rustic, and the only source of heat is a wood-burning furnace. Although the cabin had a large pile of wood on the property when she purchased it, she notices that she will run out of wood very soon.  When shopping at the Save A Lot grocery store, she sees the following flier taped to the wall:
“Frank’s Firewood and Supplies: We will deliver a cord of seasoned firewood to your property each month for one year at the low price of $100 per month.  Individual cords of wood can be purchased for $150 per cord.”
After reading the ad, Kyla picks up her phone and calls Frank’s. When no one picks up, Kyla leaves a message on the answering machine. In her message, she says that she saw Franks’ flier and that she would like a cord of firewood delivered to her cabin the next day.  She says she will be home all day, and she will pay the $100 in cash. The next day, Frank delivers the firewood and Kyla pays him $100 in cash. Although Kyla does not speak to Frank again for the next month, Frank delivers another cord of firewood a month later, and Kyla pays him $100.slide 149
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Kyla loves her cabin so much that she convinces Larry, her good friend, to buy the property neighboring her cabin.  Larry plans to put a camper on the property and stay periodically when he has time off work. However, Larry’s property is covered in trees, so he needs to clear an area for his camper.  When Kyla learns about this, she asks if Larry would mind giving her some of the wood that he will have from cutting down the trees on his property. Larry says: “Sure, I would be happy to fill up your shed with firewood.  I have a favor to ask though. Would you mind if I stay at your cabin while I clear my land?”  In response, Kyla says: “Of course, you are always welcome to stay at my cabin!  Coincidentally, I need to go back to Chicago for a few weeks for my job, so you will have the place to yourself.”
Knowing that she has a new source of firewood, Kyla calls Frank and tells him that she doesn’t want any more deliveries.  Frank, however, tells Kyla that they have a contract for ten more months of deliveries.
Fully evaluate:slide 150
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Whether Kyla and Frank have a contract, and, if so, whether it requires Kyla to pay for ten more months of deliveries; and
Whether Larry and Kyla have a contract.  In answering this question, please discuss only consideration. You may assume that Kyla accepted Larry’s offer.
Practice Essay #2slide 151
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The UCC will apply to the contract between Frank and Kyla.  The UCC applies to the sale of goods, and firewood is a good because it is a moveable and tangible thing.
Contract formation requires mutual assent and consideration.  Under the UCC, mutual assent can be established through offer and acceptance or any other objective evidence of intent to be bound.
Frank’s advertisement is not an offer.  An offer is a manifestation of intent to enter into a deal that would justify a reasonable person in thinking her assent would conclude the deal. The law presumes that advertisements are not offers because a reasonable person would know that there could be a limited supply, i.e, the problem of overacceptance.  Here, Frank’s ad is not an offer because the problem of overacceptance applies to this deal. Frank could sell out of firewood, and Frank has no control over the demand for firewood. Moreover, Frank uses no words of assurance that he will have the goods in stock.
Kyla’s phone call is thus the offer. A reasonable person in Frank’s position would think his acceptance would conclude the deal because Kyla gave a specific quantity, price, and time for delivery. In other words, all of the material terms were included.
Frank accepts Kyla’s offer by delivering the goods and accepting payment. An acceptance must be an unqualified and unequivocal agreement to the terms of the offer, and it can be in the form of a promise or performance. Here, Frank’s delivery unambiguously showed that he accepted Kyla’s offer because he delivered according to the time, price, and quantity specified in the offer. The parties thus formed a contract for the first two shipments of firewood.slide 152
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The next issue is whether the contract includes ten additional months of deliveries. A court could find that, because Frank’s ad was not the offer, the terms of the advertisement are not part of the deal. Because the yearlong commitment was only in the ad, it may not be part of the contract.
However, the parties probably implicitly agreed to a yearlong contract. A reasonable person could conclude that Kyla’s offer implicitly included the terms of the grocery store flier because she referenced the flier in her offer and offered to buy the firewood at the same price that was specified in the flier.  Moreover, the fact that Kyla accepted the second delivery without question and called Larry to cancel any further deliveries are strong evidence that she thought the contract included additional deliveries. Moreover, the parties here are relatively unsophisticated, the parties had no prior dealings, and the price of the contract is relatively low. It is thus reasonable in our case to think that the parties implicitly agreed to the long-term contract without any explicit agreement.  In other words, a reasonable person viewing the parties’ words and conduct would probably conclude that they intended to be bound to a yearlong deal.
The next issue is whether the contract between Larry and Kyla was supported by consideration. Because this contract involves an interest in real estate and a possible sale of goods, it may be governed by the common law. However, the UCC does not define consideration, so the choice of law issue need not be resolved to answer the question.slide 153
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Consideration has two elements: (1) benefit to the promisor or detriment to the promise; and (2) a bargain/mutual inducement. Here, the first element is easily met. Each party makes a promise, and each promise entails a benefit to the promisor. Kyla promises to let Larry stay at her cabin, and she will benefit when Larry gives her the firewood and cares for the cabin. Larry promises to care for the cabin and deliver the firewood, and he benefits by getting a place to stay.
The second element of consideration, however, is lacking. Consideration is bargained for only if the promises are mutually inducing. Here, Kyla’s promise to let Larry stay at the cabin was not induced by Larry’s promise to give her the firewood. We know this because Kyla says that Larry is “always welcome” to stay at her cabin. Because Larry is always welcome, Kyla is saying that Larry can stay even if he does not give her the firewood.  Because the bargain element is missing, Kyla’s promise is a promise to make an executory gift, which is not enforceable in contract law.
UDSL 슬라이드 원문 — Class 3 — Restitution, SOF & Interpretation
1
Restitution & Quasi-Contract
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Restitution이 뭐냐면... "계약도 없고, 약속도 없는데 남이 내 덕에 이득을 봤다면?" 법원이 그 이득을 돌려주라고 할 수 있어. 이게 Unjust Enrichment / Quasi-Contract야. 핵심 공식: ① 상대방이 이익(Benefit)을 받았고 ② 그 이익을 유지하는 게 불공평할 때(Unjust) → 반환해야 해. Officious Intermeddler 금지: 상대방이 원하지도 않는데 내 마음대로 뭔가 해주고 돈 달라고 하면 안 돼. 예: 남의 집 마당을 주인 허락 없이 청소해주고 청소비 요구 → No. Emergency Exception: 의식 잃은 환자에게 응급 의료를 제공했다면? 동의를 받을 수 없는 상황이었으므로 Restitution 가능 — 합리적인 가치(Reasonable Value) 기준.
Cotnam v. Wisdom: 갑자기 쓰러진 사람을 의사가 응급 치료했어. 환자는 결국 숨졌어. 유족이 "계약 없으니 돈 안 줘도 돼"라고 했어. 법원은 Quasi-Contract 인정 — 의사의 치료 서비스는 Benefit이고, 그걸 공짜로 누리는 건 Unjust. 의사는 합리적인 치료비 받을 자격 있어.
Restitution vs. Contract: 계약 위반 후 손해배상 대신 Restitution을 선택할 수도 있어 — 계약 가격이 시장 가격보다 낮았다면 Restitution이 더 유리할 수 있어.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Agendaslide 1
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문

Interpretation
Contract law concerns itself with three types of “binding obligations”slide 2
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Contract
Promissory Estoppel
Restitution
Manifestation of mutual assent, bargain in exchange & consideration
Promise plus detrimental reliance
No promise but confers a benefit that is accepted
Restatement of Restitution § 1slide 3
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A person who has been unjustly enriched at the expense of another is required to make restitution to the other.
Liability in restitution is also called “quasi contract” or “implied in law contract”
Unjust Enrichment
Restatement of Restitution § 1 cmt. aslide 4
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A person is enriched if he has received a benefit.
A person is unjustly enriched if the retention of the benefit would be unjust
A person obtains restitution when he is restored to the position he formerly occupied either by the return of something which he formerly had or by the receipt of its equivalent in money. . . .
Unjust Enrichment
Restatement of Restitution § 1 cmt bslide 5
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A person confers a benefit upon another if he gives to the other possession of or some other interest in money, land, chattels, or chose in action, performs services beneficial to or at the request of the other, satisfies a debt or a duty of the other, or in any way adds to the other’s security or advantage.
He confers a benefit not only where he adds to the property of another, but also where he saves the other from expense or loss.
The word “benefit,” therefore, denotes any form of advantage. . . .
Unjust Enrichment
Restatement (First) of Restitution § 2slide 6
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A person who officiously confers a benefit upon another is not entitled to restitution therefor.
Restatement (First) of Restitution § 2 cmt a
Officiousness means interference in the affairs of others not justified by the circumstances under which the interference takes place.
A person is not required to deal with another unless he so desires and, ordinarily, a person should not be required to become an obligor unless he so desires.
Unjust Enrichment
Restitutionslide 7
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Benefit Conferred
Unjust to keep benefit without paying
Not officious intermeddler. Benefit not forced on defendant
-> Not unjust benefit >> No restitution
>>> Restitution
We often see Restitution in two situations:slide 8
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rescue of a person
Restatement (First) of Restitution § 116
Rescue of property
Restatement (First) of Restitution § 117
Restitution
Credit Bureau Enterprises, Inc. v. Peloslide 9
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Pelo is taken to the hospital after making threats of self harm
Magistrate finds probable cause that Pelo is mentally impaired and thus enters hospitalization order
Pelo does not want to stay at the hospital and refuses to sign a release form agreeing to pay the bill
Pelo is later found to not require further hospitalization
Hospital sought payment of the medical bill against Pelo
Credit Bureau Enterprises, Inc. v. Peloslide 10
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Holding: Pelo owes the hospital for the medical services under restitution
Reasoning:
Hospital benefits Pelo by providing treatment
It would be unjust for Pelo to get the treatment without paying for it
Hospital acted with intent to charge
Treatment was reasonable/unofficious
Impossible for donee to give consent because of medical impairment
Services were necessary to prevent serious bodily harm or pain to done
Donor had no reason to know donee would not consent, if mentally competent, to receiving things/services
Credit Bureau Enterprises, Inc. v. Peloslide 11
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
This is an implied-in-law contract
Once we are in implied-in-law contract, we do not need to meet the formal elements of contract formation for a binding obligation to be created.
Credit Bureau Enterprises, Inc. v. Peloslide 12
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Pelo’s arguments:
Argument 1
Pelo suffers from bipolar disorder.
Pelo does not dispute that the $2,775.79 was a reasonable cost of services provided.
Pelo argues that he did not need the services (and thus did not get a benefit) based upon the referee’s finding that further hospitalization was not authorized.
Does the court agree?
No. Because the referee’s finding does not mean that he did not need the services at the time they were given, this argument fails.
Court also finds that the hospitalization was of medical benefit to Pelo.
Credit Bureau Enterprises, Inc. v. Peloslide 13
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Pelo’s arguments:
Argument 2
Pelo argues he shouldn’t have to pay because he did not ask for the services
The Court rejects this argument. Pelo’s opinion as to whether he needed or consented to medical services is irrelevant.
Because the emergency hospitalization order establishes that Pelo lacked sufficient judgment to make responsible decisions concerning hospitalization and lacked the ability to consent to treatment.
Credit Bureau Enterprises, Inc. v. Peloslide 14
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What is the policy behind the rule announced in this case? Why make patients like Pelo pay for services they did not request?
Restatement (First) of Restitution § 116 cmt. a
The rule stated in this Section exists in order that a person needing help in an emergency and not able to ask for it should obtain it, the attainment of such a result being aided by the assuring compensation to the person rendering the aid if the other is solvent
Judge Posner: Transaction costs are prohibitive

Jason mows his neighbor’s lawn and demands payment when they return a week later. Is Jason entitled to restitution?

Contract Law and Restitutionslide 25
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A valid contract defines the obligations of the parties as to matters within its scope, displacing to that extent any inquiry into unjust enrichment
Restatement (Third) § 2
Exampleslide 26
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Mechanic overhauls the motor of Owner's speedboat for an agreed-on price of $2500. The following season, Owner complains to Mechanic that the motor does not run as well as Mechanic had promised it would. To achieve the results previously warranted, Mechanic finds it necessary to perform extensive additional work on the motor, replacing a variety of related parts not foreseen in Mechanic's original estimate. By the time the job is finished, Mechanic has performed additional work that has a reasonable value of $5000, increasing the value of Owner's boat by a like amount.
Mechanic cannot recover the $5,000 in restitution
Exampleslide 27
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Now suppose that Mechanic can assert a valid defense to the contract. (For example, mutual mistake).
Mechanic can recover the $5,000 in restitution
Exampleslide 28
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Producer pays Actor $500 to perform a show at a concert hall. Unbeknownst to Actor, Producer records the show, posts it online, and obtains approximately $1,000 in advertising revenue.
Actor can recover the advertising revenue in restitution, because the contract did not cover recordings.
Performance of Another's Dutyslide 29
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A person who performs another's duty to a third person or to the public is entitled to restitution from the other as necessary to prevent unjust enrichment, if the circumstances justify the decision to intervene without request.
Restatement (Third) § 22
Performance of Another's Dutyslide 30
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Typically, the following are required:
Urgency;
Unable to reach agreement prior to conferral of benefit; and
the claimant is a proper party to intervene (typically a family member).
Restatement (Third) § 22Comment b
Example 1slide 31
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Son meets Father a restaurant. Father has already eaten and lays money on the table to pay his bill. Son notices that Father did not leave a tip, so Son puts his own money on the table while Father is not looking.
Restitution is not available. There is no urgency, and Son could have reached an agreement with Father.
Example 2slide 32
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Son pays the expenses of Father's final illness and his reasonable funeral expenses, intending to seek reimbursement from Father's Estate but acting before an administrator has been appointed.
Son is entitled to restitution of these expenditures from Estate
Example 3slide 33
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Now suppose that Son buys the most expensive casket and mausoleum available. Father’s estate, however, is worth only $75,000, and the costs exceed that amount.
Son is not entitled to restitution for unreasonable expenditures
Restatement (Second) § 86slide 34
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A promise made in recognition of a benefit previously received by the promisor from the promisee is binding to the extent necessary to prevent injustice.
A promise is not binding under Subsection (1):
(a) if the promisee conferred the benefit as a gift or for other reasons the promisor has not been unjustly enriched; or
(b) to the extent that its value is disproportionate to the benefit
Restatement (Second) § 86Comment bslide 35
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
restitution is denied in many cases in order to protect persons who have had benefits thrust upon them. In other cases restitution is denied by virtue of rules designed to guard against false claims, stale claims, claims already litigated, and the like.
…
a subsequent promise to make restitution removes the reason for the denial of relief, and the policy against unjust enrichment then prevails.
…
Facts such as the definite and substantial character of the benefit received, formality in the making of the promise, part performance of the promise, reliance on the promise or the probability of such reliance may be relevant to show that no imposition results from enforcement.
Mills v. Wymanslide 36
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts
Defendant’s son was sick after voyage at sea. The Plaintiff cared for him—nursed him and gave him board until he died. The Defendant (father) then wrote a letter promising to pay for services.
Mills v. Wymanslide 37
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
No contract was formed, because past or moral consideration is not valid
No recovery under restitution, because the father received no benefit (the son was an adult)
Mills v. Wymanslide 38
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if the plaintiff had contacted the defendant before his son’s death, and the defendant had made the same promise while the plaintiff was caring for him?
Then we would have consideration
Exceptionsslide 39
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Remember, satisfaction of a moral duty is consideration if the moral duty were once a legal one
Promises made after bankruptcy, infancy, or statute of limitations
There was actual consideration—but public policy makes the K unenforceable—and court is reviving the legal duty
Here, there was never consideration, and implying consideration would turn every equitable duty into a legal duty
Webb v. McGowinslide 40
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts:
Plaintiff was crippled while saving McGowin at work.
McGowin promised to pay plaintiff in consideration for having saved his life
McGowin paid for 9 years until he died
Plaintiff filed suit against McGowin’s estate for unpaid balance since payments were stopped
Webb v. McGowinslide 41
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
No liability under Restitution as a rescue case:
Plaintiff acted out of moral reasons, not because he expected the defendant to pay him. Gratuitous benefit
Rescuers are only presumed to act with intent to charge when they are professionals
Rule: a material and pecuniary benefit substitutes for consideration, thus making the promise enforceable (even if there was no duty to pay before the promise)
Exampleslide 42
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A and B are neighbors. When A’s dog runs away, B finds the dog and keeps it in his backyard until A gets home later that day. After B returns the dog, A promises to pay B $10,000.
A does not have a legal duty to pay B the $1,000, because the promise is disproportionate to the value of the services
Quasi Contractslide 43
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The defendant has knowledge of the benefit
The plaintiff has conferred a benefit on the defendant
The defendant has accepted or retained the benefit conferred and
The circumstances are such that it would be inequitable for the defendant to retain the benefit without paying fair value for it
“A person who has been unjustly enriched at the expense of another is required to make restitution to the other.”
Commerce Partnershipslide 44
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Commerce hired World as a general contractor to perform improvements
World hired Equity as a subcontractor
Equity performs stucco work as a subcontractor
World does not pay Equity
Equity files suit against Commerce, claiming unjust enrichment
Commerce Partnershipslide 45
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether a subcontractor can recover under the restitution theory from the owner of the property when the general contract has not paid the subcontractor
There would be no implied in fact contract here. Contracts implied in fact involve an implied promise to pay for services. Usually, the services were requested, and the promise to pay is implied. Here, Commerce did not ask Equity to do the work. No implied promise to pay Equity. Instead, Commerce was to pay the general contractor.
.slide 46
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Quasi-Contract Rule
What does a subcontractor need to show to recover from the owner?
The plaintiff has conferred a benefit on the defendant
The defendant has knowledge of the benefit
The defendant has accepted or retained the benefit conferred and
The circumstances are such that it would be inequitable for the defendant to retain the benefit without paying fair value for it
.slide 47
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Quasi-Contract Rule
What does a subcontractor need to show to recover from the owner?
The plaintiff has conferred a benefit on the defendant
Subcontractor did work that improved the owner’s property
The defendant has knowledge of the benefit
Owner knows the subcontractor did the work
The defendant has accepted or retained the benefit conferred and
Owner accepted the subcontractor’s work
The circumstances are such that it would be inequitable for the defendant to retain the benefit without paying fair value for it
Subcontractor cannot recover from the general contractor and the owner had not given consideration to any person for the improvements furnished by the subcontractor.
.slide 48
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Quasi-Contract Rule
How does this apply here?
Subcontractor did work that improved the owner’s property
Owner knows the subcontractor did the work
Owner accepted the subcontractor’s work
Subcontractor cannot recover from the general contractor and the owner had not given consideration to any person for the improvements furnished by the subcontractor.
.slide 49
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Quasi-Contract Rule
What does a subcontractor need to show to recover from the owner?
Subcontractor did work that improved the owner’s property
Equity did work that improved Commerce’s property by putting up stucco at value of $17,100
Owner knows the subcontractor did the work
Commerce knows the Equity did the work, because it inspected the job weekly
Owner accepted the subcontractor’s work
Commerce accepted Equity’s work because it did not object to Equity putting up the stucco
Subcontractor cannot recover from the general contractor and the owner had not given consideration to any person for the improvements furnished by the subcontractor.
Equity was not paid by the general contractor, which went bankrupt.
BUT, Equity has no evidence regarding whether Commerce paid any party for the stucco work
Commerce Partnershipslide 50
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
So who wins?
In this case, Equity did not prove at trial that Commerce had not made payment to any party for the benefits conferred on the property by Equity.
Because we need to know if Commerce paid anyone for the benefits conferred by Equity, the case is remanded to the trial court to take relevant evidence.
Equity has the burden of proof, because the plaintiff must prove each required element of its cause of action.
Commerce Partnershipslide 51
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if, on remand, the parties cannot prove whether Commerce paid the general contractor?
Equity has the burden of proof, because the plaintiff must prove each required element of its cause of action.
Commerce Partnershipslide 52
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if Commerce can prove that it paid the general contractor?
Then Equity loses. No injustice if Commerce doesn’t pay

Rescue:
Unable to give consent

Knowledge and acceptance of benefit

Hypothetical 2slide 57
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Phil and Sarah are dating. They have a child. Phil tells Sarah that, if she will move in with him and take care of the family, he will always provide for her. Sarah quits her job and moves in with Phil. The couple lives together for 10 years without getting married. Sarah takes care of the home and helps Phil at his business about 10 hours per week. Phil and Sarah then separate, and Phil takes all of the couple’s assets. Sarah sues Phil for breach of contract, promissory estoppel, and restitution. Will she recover against Phil?
Yes, under breach of contract
Yes, under promissory estoppel
Yes, under restitution
Yes, under all of the above
Yes, under promissory estoppel and restitution
Hypothetical 2slide 58
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Phil and Sarah are dating. They have a child. Phil tells Sarah that, if she will move in with him and take care of the family, he will always provide for her. Sarah quits her job and moves in with Phil. The couple lives together for 10 years without getting married. Sarah takes care of the home and helps Phil at his business about 10 hours per week. Phil and Sarah then separate, and Phil takes all of the couple’s assets. Sarah sues Phil for breach of contract, promissory estoppel, and restitution. Will she recover against Phil?
Yes, under breach of contract
Yes, under promissory estoppel
Yes, under restitution
Yes, under all of the above
Yes, under promissory estoppel and restitution
Hypothetical 2slide 59
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Implied in fact contract: Phil makes an offer to take care of her, and she accepts the offer through her performance. However, the terms are probably too open and uncertain for contract liability.
Promissory estoppel: Phil promised to take care of her, and she relied by quitting her job and taking care of the house. Even though the promise is not specific, the court can see that Phil breached and can award a remedy
Restitution. Sarah conferred a benefit, and Phil knew of the benefit and accepted at the time it was conferred. It would be unjust for Phil to refuse to pay because she intended to be compensated in the event of a divorce. He should not be able to keep all of the couple’s assets

Son promises that he will pay. After he pays the bill for two months, however, Son abruptly stops paying. If Son does not pay, Mother will be forced to go to a nursing home. Does Mother have a legal claim against Son?
Yes, under promissory estoppel

Statute of Frauds
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Statute of Frauds가 뭐냐면... 특정 계약은 구두로만 하면 법원이 강제 못 해 — 반드시 서면(Writing)이 있어야 해. 사기 방지용이야. 어떤 계약이 서면 필요하냐면 (MY LEGS): - Marriage — 결혼 약속(결혼 자체가 아닌, 결혼을 조건으로 한 약속) - Year — 1년 안에 이행 불가능한 계약 - Land — 토지 관련 계약 - Executor — 유언집행인이 유산에서 채무 갚겠다는 약속 - Goods — UCC: $500 이상의 물건 판매 - Surety — 타인의 빚을 보증하는 계약 서면 요건: 반드시 정식 계약서일 필요 없어. 이메일, 문자, 영수증, 편지 — 뭐든 핵심 조건과 당사자 서명이 있으면 돼.
예시 — "1년 룰": 4월 1일에 "내년 3월 31일까지 일해줘"라고 구두 합의. 1년 안에 이행 가능? 딱 364일이면 가능하네 → 서면 불필요. 근데 "내년 4월 1일까지" 라면? → 정확히 1년 = 1년 안에 완료 불가 → 서면 필요. 이 경계가 시험에 자주 나와.
예외 — Part Performance (토지): 구두 계약만 있어도 ① 점유 + ② 대금 지불 + ③ 개량공사(improvements) 세 가지 있으면 법원이 집행해줄 수 있어.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Statute of Fraudsslide 63
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Form of the Contract
Does the contract need to be in writing?
What does the statute of frauds do?slide 64
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
It stops the courts from enforcing a contract.
Thus it is a defense to contract enforcement.
We will discuss defenses to contract formation later.
Statute of Frauds
This says nothing about whether there is/is not a contract.
A statute of frauds issue involve at least two sub-issues:slide 65
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Does the statute of frauds apply to this contract?
Has the statute been satisfied?
Statute of Frauds
Policy Justifications:slide 66
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Prevents people from engaging in fraud
This is a social policy decision where the legislature has determined that failing to enforce certain otherwise valid contracts is a reasonable price to pay to avoid enforcing fraudulent contracts.
Like consideration, it forces people to appreciate the significance of the contract
Statute of Frauds
Statute of Fraudsslide 67
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The following classes of contracts are not enforceable unless there is a written memorandum or an applicable exception:
Marriage: A contract made upon consideration of marriage (the marriage provision)
Year: (A contract that is not to be performed within one year from the making thereof (the one-year provision)
Land: A contract for the sale of an interest in land (the land contract provision)
Executor: A contract of an executor or administrator to answer for a duty of his decedent (the executor-administrator provision).
Goods over $500
Surety: A contract to answer for a duty of another (the suretyship provision)
M
Y
L
E
G
S
Why these types of contracts?slide 68
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
These contracts are very important and/or likely to be subject to fraud/confusion.
History: An act for prevention of frauds and perjuries (English parliament 1677) set out the following circumstances under which the parties are required to reduce their agreement to a writing:
1. A promise by an executor to pay the decedent’s debts out of the executor’s funds;
2. A promise to answer for the debt of another;
3. A promise made in consideration of marriage;
4. A promise to convey an interest in land; and
An agreement that cannot be performed within a year of its making.
Sale of goods worth ten pounds sterling or upwards
Statute of Frauds
Executorslide 69
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The key point here is that a contract for an executor or administrator of an estate to pay a debt of the estate out of the executor’s or administrator’s own funds must be evidenced by a writing sufficient to satisfy the statute of frauds or it will not be enforceable.
Statute of Frauds
Executor
Not evidenced by writing
Executorslide 70
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The key point here is that a contract for an executor or administrator of an estate to pay a debt of the estate out of the executor’s or administrator’s own funds must be evidenced by a writing sufficient to satisfy the statute of frauds or it will not be enforceable.
Statute of Frauds
Executor
Evidenced by writing
What is a suretyship?slide 71
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Suretyship is a contractual relationship resulting from an agreement whereby one person,
the surety,
engages to be answerable for the debt or default of another
the principal.
The surety promises to assume the responsibility for payment of a debt incurred by the principal if the principal fails to repay the creditor.
i.e., a cosignor
Statute of Frauds
The statute of frauds typically requires that contracts for more than one year be in writing.slide 72
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The courts interpret this loosely asking whether the whole process could have taken place within a year.
If it could have (even if it is unlikely or improbable), then the court will not void the contract.
At the same time, the courts distinguish between contracts that may be terminated within a year and those that can be performed within one year.
So, a contract for a definite duration (like five years) is subject to the statute of frauds even though it might be terminated within one year because of breach by one party or because of some excusing event, such as impossibility of performance.
One Year

HBO enters into a contract to pay George R.R. Martin to write an additional Game of Thrones Book. Martin has a deadline of 2 years from the date the contract was formed, but HBO has an option to cancel the contract at any time if ratings for its Game of Thrones TV show decrease by a specified amount. The agreement is unenforceable because Martin did not sign it

On December 1, 2020, Sandy and Beatrice form an oral contract under which Beatrice is to decorate Sandy's house for Christmas day, 2021 and then after Christmas take the decorations down. Which of the following is correct?

A statute of frauds issue involve at least two sub-issues:slide 83
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Does the statute of frauds apply to this contract?
Has the statute been satisfied?
Statute of Frauds
Has the statute been satisfied?slide 84
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract within the Statute of Frauds is enforceable only if it is evidenced by any writing that:
is signed by or on behalf of the party to be charged (the defendant in a breach of contract action);
reasonably identifies the subject matter of the contract;
Indicates a contract has been formed; and
States the key terms of the contract with reasonable certainty
Has the statute been satisfied?slide 85
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
There is NO requirement that the writing:
Be all in one document or piece of paper. Multiple documents can be pieced together so long as the defendant has agreed to their contents;
Be made with the intent to formalize the contract; or
Was delivered to the plaintiff
Was signed at the time of formation (it can be signed earlier or later)
Exist at the time of trial (it could have been destroyed)
Material Facts:slide 86
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Crabtree had a contract with Arden to work for the defendant for two years
A memorandum prepared by Arden’s secretary stated the length of employment and salary, but was not signed
A payroll form noted the same, and was signed by an employee
A second payroll form, signed by the comptroller, stated that the terms had been agreed to by Arden
After one year, Crabtree is not paid the salary specified in the contract, and he brings suit
Crabtree v. Elizabeth Arden Sales Corp.
Step 1: does the statute of frauds apply?slide 87
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract that is not to be performed within a year must be memorialized in writing
The contract here was for a term of 2 years of services.
Crabtree v. Elizabeth Arden Sales Corp.
Step #2: Has the statute been satisfied?slide 88
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What is the writing?
There are three writings in this case: the office memo, the payroll change card initialed by the general manager, and the payroll change card signed by the comptroller.
Crabtree v. Elizabeth Arden Sales Corp.
The memo was not signed, but the payroll documents were signedslide 89
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The payroll documents were not signed with the intent to evidence the contract. Also, they were signed after formation. However, they still count for purposes of the statute of frauds.
Documents created after contract formation count
The document does not need to be signed with the intent of satisfying the rule and making an enforceable contract
The document must only be signed with the intent to agree that the document states the terms of the contract
Crabtree v. Elizabeth Arden Sales Corp.
The signed payroll documents, however, do not contain all of the key terms!slide 90
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
They do not say that he will be employed for 2 years. Only the memo, which is not signed, says this.
Crabtree v. Elizabeth Arden Sales Corp.
However, a writing may be pieced together out of separate writings, connected with one another either expressly or by implication.slide 91
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
If at least one document is signed, the others do not need to be signed so long as the documents refer to the same contract and there is evidence that the defendant agreed to the documents.
Crabtree v. Elizabeth Arden Sales Corp.
Application: Can these documents be pieced together? Why or why not?slide 92
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Yes. It is apparent that all three refer on their face to the same transaction. Although Arden did not sign the memo, it was written by her secretary, so we know that she agreed to it. There is little risk of fraud.
So, has the statute of frauds been satisfied?
Yes. Together, these writings contain all of the essential terms of the contract.
Crabtree v. Elizabeth Arden Sales Corp.

Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 129. Action in Reliance; Specific Performanceslide 95
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract for the transfer of an interest in land may be specifically enforced notwithstanding failure to comply with the Statute of Frauds if it is established that the party seeking enforcement, in reasonable reliance on the contract and on the continuing assent of the party against whom enforcement is sought, has so changed his position that injustice can be avoided only by specific enforcement
Courts have held that such reliance must be “unequivocally referable” to an agreement to sell the land. This is usually shown by the buyer:
Taking possession of the property; and/or
Making valuable, permanent, and substantial improvements to the property
Part Performance Exception
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 129. Action in Reliance; Specific Performanceslide 96
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Cmt c: the present rule is limited to equitable relief, and does not make available an ordinary action for damages for breach of contract. The remedy of restitution is not ordinarily affected by the Statute of Frauds. Where a contract is specifically enforceable under the rule of this Section, damages or other relief may be awarded if specific performance is prevented by the intervention of an innocent purchase for value, by condemnation of the land, or by other circumstances. Or monetary relief may be granted on the basis of fraud, estoppel, or other doctrines.
Part Performance Exception
Plaintiff is an employee of Defendant.slide 97
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Plaintiff promises to buy land from Defendant, and Defendant promises to sell the land.
Plaintiff then puts a mobile home on the property and spends $85,000 on improvements like plumbing, landscaping, and concrete around the home.
Sellers applied to the local government for permission to put the mobile home on the property; sought legal advice re sale; and allowed Buyers to stay on land for years
3 years later, Plaintiff stops working for Defendant, the relationship deteriorates, and Defendant tries to evict Plaintiff.
The parties never signed a contract.
Beaver. BrumLow
Step 1: does the statute of frauds apply?slide 98
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Yes, because this a contract for the sale of land
Step 2: is the statute of frauds satisfied?
No, because there is no signed writing
Beaver. BrumLow
Court applies the part performance exceptionslide 99
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract for the transfer of an interest in land may be specifically enforced notwithstanding failure to comply with the Statute of Frauds if it is established that the party seeking enforcement, in reasonable reliance on the contract and on the continuing assent of the party against whom enforcement is sought, has so changed his position that injustice can be avoided only by specific enforcement
Such reliance must be “unequivocally referable” to an agreement to sell the land. This is usually shown by the buyer:
Taking possession of the property; and/or
Making valuable, permanent, and substantial improvements to the property
Beaver. BrumLow
Application:slide 100
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Here, the contract was performed to such an extent as to make it inequitable to deny effect because:
Buyers spent $85,000 developing property (cashed in 401k, bought and moved mobile home, skirted home, landscaped, etc.)
Sellers applied for permission to put the mobile home on the property; sought legal advice re sale; and allowed Buyers to stay on land for years
Beaver. BrumLow
Seller argues that part performance exception is no good if there is any other plausible explanation. Here, he argues that the conduct is not “unequivocally referable” to a K for sale – equally consistent with Seller simply allowing Buyer to live on his property.slide 101
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Court rejects this and says conduct must “naturally and reasonably” lead outsider to think oral K was formed.
“an outsider, knowing all of the circumstances of a case except for the claimed oral agreement, would naturally and reasonably conclude that a contract existed regarding the land, of the same general nature as that alleged by the claimant”
Beaver. BrumLow
Seller further argues that there is no contract because no meeting of the minds since the price term was never agreed upon.slide 102
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Court holds that lower court has equitable power to make a remedy. Court looks to equitable factors: degree of reliance by Buyer, Buyer’s assumption that the price would be fair market value, and Seller’s repeated assurances to work something out.
Beaver. BrumLow

Some courts have held that reliance by a promisee can turn a promise that would otherwise be unenforceable under the statute of frauds into an enforceable promise. In these cases, courts state that the promisee’s reliance is an effective substitute for the writingslide 105
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
R 2d K § 139 cmt b. “Like § 90 this Section states a flexible principle, but the requirement of consideration is more easily displaced than the requirement of a writing.”

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Court holds that the statute of frauds is not a complete defense to a promissory estoppel action
Court explains that the purpose of Statute of Frauds is to prevent fraud, not enable people to avoid their promises
But, the court will require stronger proof of the promise
The reliance should show the existence of the promise
Alaska Democratic Party v. Rice

The Party reasonably should have expected to induce Rice to quit her job and move

This reliance is good evidence that a promise was made, because there is no other reasonable explanation for her move

Reliance not reasonable, and therefore no recovery under PE
Quitting her job and selling her home is not strong evidence that a promise was made
The general rule is that a party who refuses to continue performing a contract that is unenforceable by reason of the Statute of Frauds, after having derived a benefit from a part performance by the other party, must pay for or return what he has received from the other party under the contract.slide 114
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The Statute of Frauds was never intended to be used to permit one relying on it to enrich oneself at the expense of another or to aid in defrauding such other person.
To permit a party to an oral contract to accept the benefits of such a contract and then invoke the Statute of Frauds to avoid payment would be using the Statute to perpetrate a fraud.
Restitution to avoid the Statute of Frauds

Interpretation
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Interpretation이 뭐냐면... 계약서 언어가 모호할 때 "무슨 뜻이었나?"를 법원이 해석하는 과정이야. 양쪽 다 자기 해석이 옳다고 하면 누구 말 들어? Restatement § 201 — 3가지 시나리오: ① 양쪽이 같은 의미로 썼다 → 그 의미로 해석 (당연) ② 한 쪽은 A 의미, 다른 쪽은 B 의미 — 근데 한 쪽이 상대방 의미를 알았거나 알 수 있었다면 → 모르는 쪽의 의미로 해석 ③ 양쪽 다 진짜로 달리 이해했고 둘 다 상대방 의미 몰랐다면 → 계약 성립 자체가 안 될 수 있어(no mutual assent) 해석 원칙: 애매한 부분은 작성한 쪽(drafter)에게 불리하게 해석. 서면보다 필기(handwritten)가 우선. 특정 규정이 일반 규정보다 우선.
판례 — Joyner v. Adams: 계약서에 "부지를 개발(develop)하라"고 적혔어. Joyner는 "건물 완공"이라고 이해했고, Adams는 "건축 준비(land preparation)"라고 이해했어. 법원: 각자 진심으로 다르게 이해한 경우. 만약 Adams가 Joyner의 이해를 알았다면 → Joyner 이기. Adams가 몰랐다면 → Raffles v. Wichelhaus처럼 계약 자체가 무효. 정보를 가진 쪽이 불리해.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Interpretationslide 119
📝 한글
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 201slide 120
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Sometimes the parties to an agreement may attach different meaning to the term, clause, or agreement.
I say “blue” by which I mean:
You say “blue” by which you mean:
Why might that happen?
Innocent mistake.
Purposeful deceit on one party’s part.
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 201slide 121
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
If both parties innocently attach different meanings to the term, clause, agreement, what should we do?
Whose meaning should we use?
I’d like the blue paint.
Blue paint it is.
She meansslide 122
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
But I mean
Hee, Hee, I’ll trick her!
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 201
Compare that to the situation where one party attaches a meaning to a term, the other party knows that, but that party attaches a different meaning to the term.
Whose meaning should we use?
I’d like the blue paint.
“Blue” paint it is.
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 201slide 123
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
(1) Where the parties have attached the same meaning to a promise or agreement or a term thereof, it is interpreted in accordance with that meaning.
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 201slide 124
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
(2) Where the parties have attached different meanings to a promise or agreement or a term thereof, it is interpreted in accordance with the meaning attached by one of them if at the time the agreement was made
that party did not know of any different meaning attached by the other, and the other knew the meaning attached by the first party; or
that party had no reason to know of any different meaning attached by the other, and the other had reason to know the meaning attached by the first party
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 201slide 125
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
(3) Except as stated in this Section, neither party is bound by the meaning attached by the other, even though the result may be a failure of mutual assent.
