Hypothetical 2
Joyner v. Adamsslide 132
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Joyner enters into a contract with Adams to have Adams lease and develop Joyner’s property
Adams was required to develop all lots by Sept 30, 1980
If Adams failed to develop by that date, he would owe a penalty
On Sept 30, Adams had prepared the last lot, but had not yet begun construction of the building
Joyner v. Adamsslide 133
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Interpretation issue: Does development mean construction or preparing the lot for construction?
Procedural History:
Trial court found that Joyner honestly thought the contract required the buildings to be finished by Sept. 30th, whereas Adams honestly thought it required only that the land be prepared for construction
Suppose Adams knew that Joyner was new to the industry and thought she might be confused as to what “develop” meant in the industry. Who should win?
Adams
Joyner
The contract should fail for lack of consideration
Joyner v. Adamsslide 134
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Interpretation issue: Does development mean construction or preparing the lot for construction?
Procedural History:
Trial court found that Joyner honestly thought the contract required the buildings to be finished by Sept. 30th, whereas Adams honestly thought it required only that the land be prepared for construction
Suppose Adams knew that Joyner was new to the industry and thought she might be confused as to what “develop” meant in the industry. Who should win?
Adams
Joyner
The contract should fail for lack of consideration
This would make sense, because we want the party with superior information to share that information with the other party so they can reach a fair and informed deal.
Maxims of Interpretationslide 135
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A “maxim” is a generalized rule that exists in the common law.
It is like a proverbial saying in that they sometimes conflict:
He who hesitates is lost.
Good things come to those who wait.
In essence, they are rules of thumb, which, if relied upon can be helpful to argue a position.
The better ones are strongly linked to the outcomes they suppose.
Maximsslide 136
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
1. Noscitur a sociis. “Is known by friends.”
Read words in context. So if a word is in a series, look at the other words in the series to help interpret the word in question. If a word is in a sentence, list, paragraph, look at the words in that grouping to help interpret the word in question.
Ejusdem generis. “Same kind”
A general term joined with a specific one will be deemed to include only things that are like the specific one.
Expressiou unius exclusio alterius. “Listing of one excludes the other”
If one or more specific items are listed, without any more general or inclusive terms, other items although similar in kind are excluded.
Maximsslide 137
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Ut magis valeat quam pereat. “To have an effect rather than no effect.”
An interpretation that makes the contract valid is preferred to one that makes it invalid.
Omnia praesumuntur contra proferentum. “All presumed against the speaker.”
It a written contract contains a word or phrase which is capable of two reasonable meanings, one of which favors one party and the other which favors the other, that interpretation will be preferred which is less favorable to the one by whom the contract was drafted. (Interpret against the drafter)
Interpret the contract as a whole.
A writing or writings that form part of the same transaction should be interpreted together as a whole, that is, every terms should be interpreted as part of the whole and not as if isolated from it.
Maximsslide 138
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Purpose of the parties.
The principal apparent purpose of the parties is given great weight in determining the meaning to be given manifestations of intention or to any part thereof.
8. Plain meaning.
Give the text its “plain meaning”: what a reasonable person reading would think the words meant.
Specific provision is exception to general one.
If two provisions of a contract are inconsistent with each other and if one is “general” enough to include the specific situation to which the other is confined, the specific provision will be deemed to qualify the more general one, that is, to state an exception to it. (Specific provisions have more weight than general ones).
Maximsslide 139
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Handwritten or typed provisions control printed provisions.
Handwritten or typed provisions are presumed to be more recent and reliable statements of intent
Public interest preferred.
If a public interest is affected by a contract that interpretation or construction is preferred which favors the public interest.
Material Facts:slide 140
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Contract for the sale of chicken
The ambiguous term is “chicken.” Plaintiff and defendant disagree in a fundamental way about what “chicken” means.
Plaintiff says “chicken” means a young chicken suitable for broiling and frying.
Defendant says “chicken” means any bird of that genus that meets contract specifications on weight and quality, including “stewing chicken” and “fowl.”
Defendant delivers stewing chicken or “fowl,” not young chicken suitable for broiling and frying.
Frigaliment Importing Co. v. B.N.S. International Sales Corp.
The terms of the contracts:slide 141
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Contract 1 (May 2, 1957): defendant confirmed the sale to plaintiff of U.S. Fresh Frozen Chicken, Grade A, Government Inspected, Eviscerated 2 ½ - 3 lbs.. and 1 1/2 -2 lbs. each
75,000 lbs. 2 ½ - 3 lbs.. @ 33.00
25,000 lbs.. 1 ½ - 2 lbs.. @36.50
The second contract (also May 2, 1957) was identical save that the 50,000 lbs.. of the heavier “chicken” were called for, the price of the smaller birds was $37 per 100 lbs., and shipment was scheduled for May 40.
Frigaliment Importing Co. v. B.N.S. International Sales Corp.
Can we use the language of the contract?slide 142
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Defendant says that the contract called for “U.S. Fresh Frozen Chicken, Grade A, Government Inspected”
It therefore incorporated by reference the Dept. of Agriculture’s regulations.
The court accepts this argument and ends up using this as a “dictionary.”
Frigaliment Importing Co. v. B.N.S. International Sales Corp.
The USDA regulation divides “chicken” into the following classes:slide 143
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
(a) Broiler or fryer
(b) Roster
(c) Capon (CAY PIN)
(d) Stag
(e) Hen or stewing chicken or fowl
(f) Cock or old rooster
The contract incorporated the USDA regulations by reference.
This list stands in as a “dictionary” for understanding what counts as “chicken.”)
Frigaliment Importing Co. v. B.N.S. International Sales Corp.
Trade Usage Rule:slide 144
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
When a party to a contract is not a trade member, to establish that the party used a term in its trade sense, the other party must prove that (1) the first party had actual knowledge of the usage or (2) that the usage is so generally known in the community that his actual individual knowledge of it may be inferred.
To prove (2), you must show that the usage is of long continuance, well established, notorious, universal and reasonable in itself.
Frigaliment Importing Co. v. B.N.S. International Sales Corp.
Application of Trade Usage:slide 145
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Plaintiff contends there is a definite trade usage that “chicken” meant “young chicken.”
Defendant was only beginning in trade, so need to establish that the usage is of such long continuance, well established, notorious, universal that the Defendant should be presumed to know it.
The evidence was in conflict as to this conclusion
Frigaliment Importing Co. v. B.N.S. International Sales Corp.
The argument relating to “profit”slide 146
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Defendant argues that assuming Plaintiff’s view of “chicken,” Defendant would not have been able to make a profit in the deal.
Further Plaintiff would have known of this impossibility.
This implies Defendant’s view should prevail.
Frigaliment Importing Co. v. B.N.S. International Sales Corp.
Conclusionslide 147
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Court holds that, because there is subjective evidence that defendant believed it was providing “chicken” as defined in the contract and there are objective definitions of chicken consistent with defendant’s interpretation (dictionary, department of agriculture regulations, some usage in trade, realities of market, and what plaintiff’s spokesperson said), Plaintiff has failed to meet its burden of showing that “chicken” was used in its (narrower) sense.
Plaintiff has the burden of proof to show a breach!
Frigaliment Importing Co. v. B.N.S. International Sales Corp.
Hypotheticalslide 148
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Builder builds homes in planned communities that have strict requirements for landscaping through a homeowners’ association. Builder enters into a contract that requires Chuck to provide and install all landscaping on the homes that Builder constructs for $5,000 per house. Builder knows that Chuck has just started working in the landscaping field and is unfamiliar with the industry. Moreover, Builder is surprised that Chuck has offered a price that is significantly lower than his competitors. In fact, Chuck’s price seems to be equivalent to the cost of the supplies without any labor or transportation costs. After Builder completes a home, Chuck lays down sod. Builder calls Chuck and asks when he will complete the landscaping by planting trees and shrubbery. Chuck replies that he thought “landscaping” under the contract meant only the laying of sod (grass). Builder says that “landscaping” in the construction industry means laying sod and planting trees and bushes. If Chuck refuses to plant the trees and bushes and Builder files suit for breach of contract, which of the following is most likely if the common law governs the case?
Builder will lose, because the contract failed for lack of mutual assent
Builder will lose, because the Court will use Chuck’s meaning of the term “landscaping”
Builder will win, because the court will use Builder’s meaning of the term “landscaping”
Builder will win, because the court will use the meaning of the term “landscaping” used by the construction industry

UDSL 슬라이드 원문 — Class 4 — Parol Evidence Rule
1
Parol Evidence Rule — Common Law
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Parol Evidence Rule이 뭐냐면... 계약서를 최종적으로 서면으로 작성했으면, 그 이전에 했던 구두·서면 합의로 계약서 내용을 추가하거나 변경하는 건 안 돼. 법원은 "서면이 최종"이라고 봐. Integrated vs. Not: - Totally Integrated: "이 계약서가 전부야(merger clause)" → 추가도 변경도 안 됨 - Partially Integrated: 일부만 최종 → 추가는 안 되지만, 완전히 다른 별개 사항은 가능 PER이 막는 것: ① 계약서 내용을 변경하는 선행 증거 ② 계약서에 새 조건을 추가하는 선행 증거 PER이 못 막는 것(예외): ① 계약 성립 이후 변경(Modification) — 나중 합의는 괜찮아 ② 사기(Fraud), 강박(Duress), 착오(Mistake) 입증 ③ 계약 효력 자체를 다투는 것 (선행 조건, 조건부 효력) ④ 계약서 언어 해석 (Trade usage, Course of dealing)
예시 — 집 계약서에 Merger Clause 있음. 계약 전 구두로 "외벽 페인트칠 해줄게" 약속. 계약 성립 후 안 해줌. 법원: PER 때문에 이 구두 약속은 증거 제출 불가 — 계약서가 총체적 통합(Totally Integrated). 처음부터 그 조건을 계약서에 넣었어야 했어.
4 Corners vs. Contextual 접근: 고전적 접근은 계약서만 봄. 현대(Corbin/UCC)는 언어 해석 위해 외부 증거 허용.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Agendaslide 1
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Parol Evidence Rule
Parol Evidence Rule: What are the express terms?slide 2
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Interpretation of Explicit Terms
Contractual Meaning
Implied Terms (Good Faith; Warranties)
Modification
Parol Evidence Ruleslide 3
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Governs the effect of a written agreement on any prior oral or written agreements between the parties.
Not a rule of evidence or interpretation
Instead, it is a rule of substantive contract law
It governs the terms of the contract
Parol Evidence Rule (PER)slide 4
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
When the rule applies, it prevents parties from using evidence to add new terms to the writing or contradict the terms of the writing
PER Terminologyslide 5
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Integration
Partially integrated
Totally integrated
Consistent additional terms
Contradictory terms
Collateral contract
Integrationslide 6
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
An integrated agreement is a writing or writings constituting a final expression of one or more terms of an agreement.
When an agreement is integrated, no evidence of contradictory terms will be admitted.
Integrationslide 7
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Total or complete integration – intended to be a final and complete statement of the parties’ agreement.
No evidence of additional or contradictory terms will be admitted
Partial integration – intended to constitute a final expression of one or more terms
Evidence of consistent additional terms is allowed, but no evidence of contradictory terms will be admitted.
Evidence of the following is always admissible:slide 8
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Evidence used to interpret the terms in the writing
Evidence that agreement to the writing was obtained by fraud
Evidence of a separate contract that has separate consideration (collateral contract)
Evidence of a condition precedent
Exceptions
Additional Termsslide 9
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Writing
Oral Terms
Price: $1,000
Price: $1,000
Details of Work
Details of Work
Time of Work
Time of Work
All disputes subject to arbitration
Additional term

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문

Oral Terms

Price: $1,000
Details of Work
Details of Work

Time of Work
All disputes subject to arbitration
This is allowed with a partial integration, but no evidence of this term will be admitted if it is a total integration

Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 209slide 22
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
(2) Whether there is an integrated agreement is to be determined by the court as a question preliminary to determination of a question of interpretation or to application of the parol evidence rule.
Step 1slide 23
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Determine the purpose of the extrinsic evidence
Add a consistent additional term
Add an inconsistent term
Interpret the agreement
Prove fraud
Prove the existence of a collateral agreement
Prove existence of a condition
Step 2
Determine if writing is fully or partially integrated
Step 3
Apply Parol Evidence rule:
Consistent additional term + partial integration = admit evidence
Consistent additional term + total integration = exclude evidence
Inconsistent term + integration (partial or total) = exclude evidence
Interpretation/fraud/collateral agreement/condition = evidence is admissible
Applying the PERslide 24
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
But how does the court determine the purpose of the evidence and the level of integration?
Four corners approach (classic approach, but still used in some jurisdictions)
Modern approach
Key Questionslide 25
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Is the party trying to interpret the language of the writing, or is the party instead trying to contradict the writing?
Was the plaintiff in Frigaliment interpreting the word “chicken” or advancing an meaning that was inconsistent with the writing?
The Classical Approachslide 26
📝 한글
Thompson v. Libbyslide 27
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Parties enter into contract to sell logs. They sign the following:
“I have this day sold top R.C. Libby . . . All of my logs marked “H.C.A.” cut in the winters of 1882 and 1883, for ten dollars a thousand feet, boom scale at Minneapolis, Minnesota. Payments case as fast as scale bills are produced.”
Defendant claims the contract contained a warranty on the logs. Defendant attempts to introduce oral evidence of such a warranty.
Thompson v. Libbyslide 28
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether the trial court erred by admitting oral testimony to prove the warranty allegedly made at the time of formation
Thompson v. Libbyslide 29
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Purpose of the PER: Injustice would result if writing could be controlled by “slippery memory”
Step 1: Purpose of the evidence is to add a consistent additional term
Step 2: Is the contract totally integrated?
Thompson v. Libbyslide 30
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Four corners rule
The judge (the court) determines the completeness of the writing by looking solely at the writing.
The writing must appear to the judge (the court) to be complete on its face.
Rationale: If oral evidence is admitted to prove partial integration, the purpose of the rule is frustrated – we have gone in a circle.
Thompson v. Libbyslide 31
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application: “The language of the contract ‘imports a legal obligation, without any uncertainty as to its object or the extent of the engagement.’”
“I have this day sold top R.C. Libby . . . All of my logs marked “H.C.A.” cut in the winters of 1882 and 1883, for ten dollars a thousand feet, boom scale at Minneapolis, Minnesota. Payments case as fast as scale bills are produced.”
Thompson v. Libbyslide 32
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Is it really possible to tell from the writing that it is a complete representation of the parties’ agreement?
This approach is losing favor; although it is still followed by a fair number of jurisdictions
The Four Corners Ruleslide 33
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule 1
If the writing contains a merger clause, then, unless the writing is obviously incomplete or the merger clause was included by mistake/fraud, the writing is conclusively held to be a total integration.
Merger clause = a provision in the contract that says the writing is an integrated agreement (“This writing is a complete and accurate statement of the parties’ agreement and supersedes all prior oral statements.”)
The Four Corners Ruleslide 34
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule 2
If there is no merger clause, then:
If the writing is obviously incomplete on its face, it is a partial integration (evidence of consistent additional terms may be introduced).
If the writing appears complete on its face and the writing expresses the undertaking of one party (e.g., in the case of a deed, note), then it is a partial integration.
The Four Corners Ruleslide 35
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule 3
If the writing appears to be a complete writing and it expresses the rights/obligations of both parties, then the writing is a total integration.
The Modern Approachslide 36
📝 한글
What may be considered when determining if the writing is integratedslide 37
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 210.
(3) Whether an agreement is completely or partially integrated is to be determined by the court as a question preliminary to determination of a question of interpretation or to application of the parol evidence rule.
Comment b: Proof of complete integration. That a writing was or was not adopted as a completely integrated agreement may be proved by any relevant evidence. A document in the form of a written contract, signed by both parties and apparently complete on its face, may be decisive of the issue in the absence of credible contrary evidence. But a writing cannot of itself prove its own completeness, and wide latitude must be allowed for inquiry into circumstances bearing on the intention of the parties.
Evidence of an inconsistent term or interpretation of a term in the writing?slide 38
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 215 cmt b.Whether there is contradiction depends . . . on whether the two [agreements] are consistent or inconsistent.
This is a question which often cannot be determined from the face of the writing
the writing must first be applied to its subject matter and placed in context.
Where . . . the evidence if [reasonably] believed could lead a reasonable person to interpret the writing as claimed by the proponent of the evidence, [we have a question of fact]
But the asserted meaning must be one to which the language of the writing, read in context, is reasonably susceptible.
If no other meaning is reasonable, the court should rule as a matter of law that the meaning is established.
Partial Integration or Complete Integration?slide 39
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 216(1) Evidence of a consistent additional term is admissible to supplement an integrated agreement unless the court finds that the agreement was completely integrated.(2) An agreement is not completely integrated if the writing omits a consistent additional agreed term which is
(a) agreed to for separate consideration, or
(b) such a term as in the circumstances might naturally be omitted from the writing.
Modern Approachslide 40
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The judge considers all evidence to determine if the agreement is integrated and to determine the purpose of the evidence. (Steps 1 and 2)
The judge thus always sees the extrinsic evidence
The jury sees the extrinsic evidence only after the application of the parol evidence rule (Step 3)
The jury thus does not always see the extrinsic evidence
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 41
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Taylor is involved in an auto accident
Taylor is sued by Ring, and jury awards Ring $2.5 in excess of Taylor’s insurance
Taylor files a claim against State Farm, his insurer, claiming State Farm failed to settle with Ring in bad faith
State Farm moves to dismiss, claiming that Taylor released all claims against State Farm when he agreed to accept $15,000 in uninsured motorist benefits
Lower court denies motion, and jury awards $2.4 million to Taylor
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 42
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: whether parol evidence will be admitted to prove the meaning of the release
Procedural History:
The trial court ruled that the provision was ambiguous, meaning parol evidence could be admitted
The Court of Appeals ruled that the provision was not ambiguous, meaning parol evidence could not be admitted
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 43
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Holding:
A judge must first consider the offered/extrinsic evidence and, if he or she finds that the contract language is "reasonably susceptible" to the interpretation asserted by its proponent, the extrinsic evidence is admissible to determine the meaning intended by the parties.
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 44
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
How does this case differ from the approach of Thompson v. Libby?
The majority here uses the modern approach to the parol evidence rule, i.e., the court considers parol evidence to determine if the agreement is integrated or “reasonably susceptible” to the proffered interpretation
Here, the court should give effect to the parties’ intent, even if they give the language a special meaning
After determining if it is integrated or reasonably susceptible, the court will apply the parol evidence rule to exclude only the evidence that contradicts or varies the meaning the K
Under the classical approach, the judge determines the completeness of the writing by looking solely at the writing. Extrinsic evidence is allowed in only if the writing is ambiguous on its face.
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 45
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Taylor released “all contractual rights, claims, and causes of action he had or may have against State Farm under the policy of insurance in connection with the collision and all subsequent matters.”
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 46
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
The contract releases “all contractual” claims against State Farm
Taylor claims this did not release the bad faith claim, which sounds in tort law
Court admits parol evidence to determine if the contract is “reasonably susceptible” to Taylor’s proffered meaning
Considering all the evidence (parties never mentioned bad faith, both parties aware of potentially large liability), the Court determines that the contract was reasonably susceptible to that interpretation
The parol evidence was therefore properly submitted to the jury, which interpreted the contract
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 47
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Suppose the agreement released: “all rights, claims, and causes of action Taylor had or may have against State Farm in connection with the collision and all subsequent matters.”
Court will look at all the evidence, but Taylor’s evidence probably wont go to the jury. He could try to show that “all” doesn’t mean all. Most likely, this is attempting to contradict the writing, which you can’t do. In other words, the term “all rights, claims and causes of action” is not reasonably susceptible to waiving only contract claims.
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 48
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Suppose the agreement released: “all uninsured motorist claims Taylor had or may have against State Farm in connection with the collision and all subsequent matters.” State Farm then seeks to admit evidence that the parties orally agreed at the time of signing that the bad faith claim would also be released.
Same – not “reasonably susceptible” to State Farm’s meaning of bad faith claims.
Taylor v. State Farm Auto Insurance Co.slide 49
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
But could state Farm seek to admit evidence that the parties intended to settle the bad faith claim as an additional term?
Modern view looks at all extrinsic evidence to see if the writing is integrated. Then admits consistent additional terms if “such a term as in the circumstances might naturally be omitted from the writing.”
Here, the bad faith claim would not naturally be admitted. Liability under the bad faith claim was very significant. Because it was so important, the parties would have put it in writing
Step 1slide 50
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Determine if the evidence is being used to add a consistent additional term, add an inconsistent term, interpret the agreement, or prove fraud
If the term is ambiguous/”reasonably susceptible” to the proffered meaning, the evidence is being admitted to interpret the terms
If the term is not ambiguous/reasonably susceptible, the evidence is of an additional or inconsistent term
Step 2
Determine if writing is fully or partially integrated
Step 3
Apply Parol Evidence rule:
Consistent additional term + partial integration = admit evidence
Consistent additional term + total integration = exclude evidence
Inconsistent term + integration (partial or total) = exclude evidence
Interpretation = admit evidence (assuming the term is ambiguous/”reasonably susceptible” to the proffered meaning)
Fraud = evidence is admissible
Classical Approachslide 51
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
(Thompson)
Modern Approach
(Taylor)
Step 1
Court looks only at the 4 corners of the document to determine if the term is a consistent additional term because the contract is ambiguous.
Court looks at 4 corners and all extrinsic evidence to determine if the term is a consistent additional term because the contract is ambiguous
Step 2
Court looks only at the 4 corners of the document to determine if K is integrated
Court looks at 4 corners and all extrinsic evidence to determine if K is integrated. Partial integration if, under the circumstances, the term “might naturally be omitted from the writing”
Step 3
No difference between the approaches
Riverisland Cold Storage, Inc. v. Fresno-Madera Production Credit Associationslide 52
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts
Plaintiffs sign an agreement with Credit Association to restructure their debt. Writing gives Plaintiffs 4 months before any payments are due and lists 8 parcels of land as collateral. Plaintiffs did not read the K. They say a representative for the Credit Association told them they would have 2 years before payment was due and post collateral of 2 ranches.
Plaintiffs file action seeking damages for fraud and rescission of the agreement
Credit Assoc moved for summary judgment, claiming this evidence of fraud inadmissible
Riverisland Cold Storage, Inc. v. Fresno-Madera Production Credit Associationslide 53
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule: Parol Evidence Rule (PER) does not apply to evidence of fraud
Rationale: PER doesn’t apply to arguments that go to the validity of the agreement itself; instead, it only applies to evidence regarding the terms of the agreement. If contract is not valid, then the writing has no legal effect
Riverisland Cold Storage, Inc. v. Fresno-Madera Production Credit Associationslide 54
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Credit Association’s motion for summary judgment should be denied. Plaintiffs can admit extrinsic evidence to show that the Credit Association lied about the contents of the writing.
2
UCC Parol Evidence & Interpretation
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
UCC Parol Evidence Rule이 뭐냐면... Common Law PER보다 훨씬 유연해. UCC에서는 계약서 언어를 설명하거나 보충하는 외부 증거를 훨씬 더 쉽게 받아줘. UCC가 허용하는 3가지 외부 증거: ① Course of Performance: 이 계약에서 실제로 어떻게 행동해왔나? (가장 강력한 증거) ② Course of Dealing: 이전 거래에서 어떻게 했나? ③ Trade Usage: 업계에서 통상적으로 어떻게 하나? (가장 약한 증거) 우선순위: Course of Performance > Course of Dealing > Trade Usage. 충돌하면 앞선 게 이겨. UCC Gap Fillers: 계약서에 조건이 빠졌을 때 UCC가 채워줘 — 가격 미정이면 합리적 가격, 인도 장소 미정이면 판매자 영업소, 인도 시기 미정이면 합리적 기간.
예시 — Wavelaster v. Wetailers: 계약서엔 불량품만 반품 가능이라고 적혔어. 근데 거래 중 3년간 정상품 125개를 반품받아줬어. 이 "행동(Course of Performance)"을 증거로 제출 가능? → YES. UCC에서 계약 이행 중 실제 행동은 최우선 해석 근거야.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
UCC Parol Evidence Rule and Interpretationslide 55
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-202
Essentially adopts the modern view of the parol evidence rule
States that the agreement can be explained or supplemented by course of performance, course of dealing, or usage of trade
UCC Parol Evidence and Interpretationslide 56
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-202
Terms with respect to which the confirmatory memoranda of the parties agree or which are otherwise set forth in a writing intended by the parties as a final expression of their agreement with respect to such terms as are included therein may not be contradicted by evidence of any prior agreement or of a contemporaneous oral agreement but may be explained or supplemented
(a) by course of performance, course of dealing, or usage of trade (Section 1-303); and
(b) by evidence of consistent additional terms unless the court finds the writing to have been intended also as a complete and exclusive statement of the terms of the agreement.
UCC Parol Evidence Ruleslide 57
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
§ 1-303. Course of Performance, Course of Dealing, and Usage of Trade.(a) A “course of performance” is a sequence of conduct between the parties to a particular transaction that exists if:
(1) the agreement of the parties with respect to the transaction involves repeated occasions for performance by a party; and
(2) the other party, with knowledge of the nature of the performance and opportunity for objection to it, accepts the performance or acquiesces in it without objection.
(b) A “course of dealing” is a sequence of conduct concerning previous transactions between the parties to a particular transaction that is fairly to be regarded as establishing a common basis of understanding for interpreting their expressions and other conduct.
UCC Parol Evidence Ruleslide 58
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
§ 1-303. Course of Performance, Course of Dealing, and Usage of Trade.(c) A “usage of trade” is any practice or method of dealing having such regularity of observance in a place, vocation, or trade as to justify an expectation that it will be observed with respect to the transaction in question. The existence and scope of such a usage must be proved as facts. If it is established that such a usage is embodied in a trade code or similar record, the interpretation of the record is a question of law.
More UCC Gap Fillersslide 59
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
§ 1-303. Course of Performance, Course of Dealing, and Usage of Trade.(e) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (f), the express terms of an agreement and any applicable course of performance, course of dealing, or usage of trade must be construed whenever reasonable as consistent with each other. If such a construction is unreasonable:
(1) express terms prevail over course of performance, course of dealing, and usage of trade;
(2) course of performance prevails over course of dealing and usage of trade; and
(3) course of dealing prevails over usage of trade.
Agreed upon termsslide 60
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What the parties have done in this contract
What the parties have done in other contracts
What other parties have done in other contracts
Nanakuli Paving & Rock Co. v. Shell Oil Co.slide 61
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts:
Shell and Nanakuli have a contract for the sale of asphalt materials. The contract says that the price shall be “Shell’s Posted Price at time of delivery.” When the price of oil rises, Shell increases the price in the contract. Shell does not give Nanakuli any warning, and thus Nanakuli is forced to buy the materials at a much higher price than it had anticipated. Because Nanakuli had already bid on several government projects using the lower prices, Nanakuli loses a significant amount of money.
Nanakuli Paving & Rock Co. v. Shell Oil Co.slide 62
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts:
In the paving industry in Hawaii, sellers generally engage in price protection, meaning that the seller will only change the price for new projects. The seller will continue to honor the old price for existing construction projects. This is because the state of Hawaii will not alter the price it pays for the work when the price of materials fluctuates.
Nanakuli argues that its contract with Shell requires price protection
Nanakuli Paving & Rock Co. v. Shell Oil Co.slide 63
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule: Course of performance, course of dealing, and usage of trade are always considered by judge; but if judge determines that they cannot be reconciled with express terms of the writing they are excluded from the jury.
Nanakuli Paving & Rock Co. v. Shell Oil Co.slide 64
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Usage of trade: suppliers in the asphalt industry in Hawaii always offer price protection
Course of performance:
Shell price protected Nanakuli twice under this contract in the past
Shell argues these were mere waivers, not course of performance
These were the only 2 instances where price protection as an issue
In first instance, Shell used language suggesting that Nanakuli was entitled to protection – Shell official wrote of need to “bargain” with Nanakuli
Court considers a change in management at Shell, which explains why Shell changed practices and why the earlier price protections are evidence of the parties’ understanding of the agreement rather than waivers
Nanakuli Paving & Rock Co. v. Shell Oil Co.slide 65
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Looking at this evidence, the court finds that price protection is a consistent additional term
In other words, the course of performance and usage of trade show that price protection is not inconsistent with the terms of the writing
Price protection is an exception to the written term, which is that prices are set by Shell. Because it is a limited exception, it is not a total negation.
Nanakuli Paving & Rock Co. v. Shell Oil Co.slide 66
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Conclusion
Under the UCC, the contract is virtually always partially integrated with respect to course of performance, course of dealing, and usage of trade. In other words, the evidence of these things goes to the jury so long as it is consistent with the writing.
The evidence of price protection thus goes to the jury
UDSL 슬라이드 원문 — Class 5 — Implied Terms, Breach & Damages
1
Implied Terms & Good Faith
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Implied Terms가 뭐냐면... 계약서에 명시되지 않았지만 법원이 "당연히 있는 걸로" 읽어넣는 조건이야. Implied in Fact(당사자 의도로 추론)와 Implied in Law(정책적 이유로 삽입) 두 가지. Good Faith & Fair Dealing: 모든 계약에는 묵시적으로 "성실하고 공정하게 이행해야 한다"는 의무가 있어. 계약 조건을 악용해서 상대방을 함정에 빠뜨리면 안 돼. Wood v. Lucy, Lady Duff-Gordon: Wood가 유명 디자이너 Duff-Gordon과 독점 계약을 맺었어. Wood가 제품 배치를 해주면 이익을 나누는 계약. 근데 "Wood가 배치하겠다"는 명시적 약속이 없어 — Illusory Promise 아냐?
판례 스토리 — Cardozo 판사는 이렇게 봤어: Wood는 배치를 독점적으로 할 권한을 받았고, 계약 구조 전체가 그가 최선을 다해(best efforts) 이익을 창출할 거라는 전제로 되어 있어. Best efforts 의무가 묵시적으로 포함돼 있으니 Illusory Promise가 아니야. Consideration 있고 계약 유효. → UCC § 2-306도 같은 원칙: Output/Requirements 계약에는 Best Efforts 의무 묵시적 포함.
Satisfaction Clauses: "내가 만족하면 지불"이라는 조건은 Illusory 아냐 — 단, 불만족이 진심이어야 해(Good Faith). 취향 문제면 주관적 기준, 기술적 문제면 합리적 기준 적용.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Agendaslide 1
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Implied Terms
Good faith

Parol Evidence Rule: What are the express terms?slide 2
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Interpretation of Explicit Terms
Contractual Meaning
Implied Terms (Good Faith; Warranties)
Modification
Common Law Implied Termsslide 3
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
An implied term is a term that is not actually in the contract.
There are two types of implied terms:
Implied in fact: Is founded upon a meeting of minds, which, although not embodied in an express contract, is inferred, as a fact, from conduct of the parties showing, in the light of the surrounding circumstances, their tacit understanding.
Implied in law: Is a legal fiction under which the term is imputed into the contract regardless of whether the parties actually intended to include that term.
Wood v. Lucy, Lady Duff-Gordonslide 4
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Duff-Gordon is a popular fashion designer
She enters into a contract with Wood, giving him the exclusive right to place her endorsements on the designs of others
Duff-Gordon would have half of all money Wood made under the contract by placing her endorsements
Duff-Gordon placed her design on clothing without paying Wood
Wood filed suit for breach of contract
Wood v. Lucy, Lady Duff-Gordonslide 5
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Was there sufficient consideration to support formation of a contract?
Why is this the issue?
Because if Wood’s promise was illusory, then, as an offer it will not stand as consideration for the contract and there would be no contract for Lady Duff-Gordon to breach.
Wood v. Lucy, Lady Duff-Gordonslide 6
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Review: what is an illusory promise?
An illusory promise appears to be a promise but on closer examination reveals that the promisor has not promised to do anything.
“Words in promissory form that promise nothing; they do not purport to put any limitation on the freedom of the alleged promisor, but leave his future action subject to his own future will, just as it would have been had he said no words at all.” Marshall Durbin Food Corp. v. Baker
Wood v. Lucy, Lady Duff-Gordonslide 7
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rules:
Interpretation of the terms of an agreement is not limited to the explicit words.
If an agreement, in its entirety, implies the existence of a term not explicitly in it, then such term is part of the contract.
A term is implied if the agreement cannot be understood to effect the parties’ purposes without that term.
Wood v. Lucy, Lady Duff-Gordonslide 8
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
The contract contains an implied promise that Wood would use reasonable efforts to sell Lady Duff-Gordon’s name/products.
Without such an implied term, the contract would lack business efficacy.
The parties thus had a valid contract.
Implied Terms under the U.C.C.slide 9
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The U.C.C. contains a number of rules about implied in law terms (they are called “gap fillers” in the UCC) which define a term in case a contract fails to explicitly define that term.
Gap Fillers under the U.C.C.
UCC Gap Fillersslide 10
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
2-305 Open price term
2-306 Output, Requirements and Exclusive Dealings
2-307 Delivery in Single Lot or Several Lots
2-308 Absence of Specified Place for Delivery
2-309 Absence of Specific Time Provisions; Notice of Termination
UCC Gap fillersslide 11
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-305. Open Price Term.
(1) The parties if they so intend can conclude a contract for sale even though the price is not settled. In such a case the price is a reasonable price at the time for delivery if
(a) nothing is said as to price; or
(b) the price is left to be agreed by the parties and they fail to agree; or
(c) the price is to be fixed in terms of some agreed market or other standard as set or recorded by a third person or agency and it is not so set or recorded.
UCC Gap fillersslide 12
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-305. Open Price Term.
(2) A price to be fixed by the seller or by the buyer means a price for him to fix in good faith.
(3) When a price left to be fixed otherwise than by agreement of the parties fails to be fixed through fault of one party the other may at his option treat the contract as cancelled or himself fix a reasonable price.
(4) Where, however, the parties intend not to be bound unless the price be fixed or agreed and it is not fixed or agreed there is no contract. In such a case the buyer must return any goods already received or if unable so to do must pay their reasonable value at the time of delivery and the seller must return any portion of the price paid on account.
UCC Gap fillersslide 13
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-306. Output, Requirements and Exclusive Dealings.
(1) A term which measures the quantity by the output of the seller or the requirements of the buyer means such actual output or requirements as may occur in good faith, except that no quantity unreasonably disproportionate to any stated estimate or in the absence of a stated estimate to any normal or otherwise comparable prior output or requirements may be tendered or demanded.
UCC Gap fillersslide 14
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-306. Output, Requirements and Exclusive Dealings.
(2) A lawful agreement by either the seller or the buyer for exclusive dealing in the kind of goods concerned imposes unless otherwise agreed an obligation by the seller to use best efforts to supply the goods and by the buyer to use best efforts to promote their sale.
UCC Gap fillersslide 15
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-307. Delivery in Single Lot or Several Lots.
Unless otherwise agreed all goods called for by a contract for sale must be tendered in a single delivery and payment is due only on such tender but where the circumstances give either party the right to make or demand delivery in lots the price if it can be apportioned may be demanded for each lot.
UCC Gap fillersslide 16
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-308. Absence of Specified Place for Delivery.Unless otherwise agreed
(a) the place for delivery of goods is the seller's place of business or if he has none his residence; but
(b) in a contract for sale of identified goods which to the knowledge of the parties at the time of contracting are in some other place, that place is the place for their delivery; and
UCC Gap fillersslide 17
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
U.C.C. § 2-309. Absence of Specific Time Provisions; Notice of Termination.
(1) The time for shipment or delivery or any other action under a contract if not provided in this Article or agreed upon shall be a reasonable time.
(2) Where the contract provides for successive performances but is indefinite in duration it is valid for a reasonable time but unless otherwise agreed may be terminated at any time by either party.
(3) Termination of a contract by one party except on the happening of an agreed event requires that reasonable notification be received by the other party and an agreement dispensing with notification is invalid if its operation would be unconscionable.
Leibel v. Raynor Manufacturing Co.slide 18
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Parties entered into an exclusive dealer-distributorship for Raynor Manufacturing Co. to sell and deliver to Leibel its garage doors, operators, and parts at the factory distributor price and Leibel to sell, install, and service Raynor products exclusively.
The agreement was for an indefinite time.
After two years, Raynor notified Leibel that as of that date (June 30, 1976), the relationship was terminated & that another distributor had been found.
Leibel v. Raynor Manufacturing Co.slide 19
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: should a reasonable notification of termination clause be read into an on-going distributorship contract?
Leibel v. Raynor Manufacturing Co.slide 20
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule: U.C.C. § 2-309.
(2) Where the contract provides for successive performances but is indefinite in duration it is valid for a reasonable time but unless otherwise agreed may be terminated at any time by either party.
(3) Termination of a contract by one party . . . requires that reasonable notification be received by the other party
Leibel v. Raynor Manufacturing Co.slide 21
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
The contract was for an on-going dealer/distributor relationship. Such a relationship, by its very nature, requires successive performances. The agreement did not specify a duration. As a result, the agreement could be terminated at any time by either party. U.C.C. § 2-309(2). At the same time, such termination of the agreement requires reasonable notification of the termination. U.C.C. § 2-309(3).
To determine what notification would be reasonable, the court considers two factors: need to sell off inventory and the need to recoup investment made in reliance on the K. Other possible factors: time needed to find a substitute arrangements; industry standards.
Implied Termsslide 22
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Why have implied terms?
Promote fairness
Represent probable intention of the parties
Promote economic efficiency
If most parties would agree on the implied terms, the parties will save expense by not having to negotiate around them. Good default rules make it easier to draft contracts.
Without implied terms, contracts would need all terms, making them much longer and more difficult to draft. Parties would need to plan for every possible contingency
Implied Duty of Good Faithslide 23
📝 한글
Examples of bad faith with related good faith requirementslide 24
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Form of bad faith conduct
Meaning of good faith
Seller concealing a defect in what he is selling
Fully disclosing material facts
Builder willfully failing to perform in full, though otherwise substantially performing
Substantially performing without knowingly deviating from specifications
Party openly abusing bargaining power to coerce an increase in the contract price
Refraining from abuse of bargaining power
Hiring a broker and then deliberately preventing him from consummating the deal
Acting cooperatively
Conscious lack of diligence in mitigating the other party’s damages
Acting diligently
Arbitrarily and capriciously exercising a power to terminate a contract
Action with some reason
Adopting an overreaching interpretation of contract language
Interpreting contract language fairly
Harassing the other party for repeated assurance of performance
Accepting adequate assurances
Seidenberg v. Summit Bankslide 25
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Seidenberg and Raymond owned a brokerage company bought out by Summit Bank.
Seidenberg and Raymond remained in the company.
Seidenberg and Raymond were eventually terminated.
Seidenberg and Raymond alleged that Summit did not perform its obligations in good faith because it did not really cooperate with Seidenberg and Raymond in building up the business once Summit bought it.
Seidenberg v. Summit Bankslide 26
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Procedural History:
The trial court granted a motion for summary judgment from Summit
The trial court held that Seidenberg and Raymond were not really alleging that there was a breach of the duty of good faith and fair dealing, but rather they were alleging a breach of an oral agreement outside the four corners of the purchase agreement.
Since this violates the parol evidence rule, case is dismissed for failure to state a claim upon which relief can be granted.
Seidenberg v. Summit Bankslide 27
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issues:
Does the Parol Evidence Rule bar reading the duty of good faith and fair dealing into a contract when it is not expressly contained in the contract?
What are the ways in which the duty of good faith and fair dealing have been applied?
Seidenberg v. Summit Bankslide 28
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #1: Does the Parol Evidence Rule bar reading the duty of good faith and fair dealing into a contract when it is not expressly contained in the contract?
No, the parol evidence rule cannot inhibit application of the implied covenant of good faith and fair dealing because the covenant is contained in all contracts by operation of law
The parol evidence rule bars “additional” terms only when the parties have a fully integrated agreement; here, the written K is not a full expression of the agreement, because the covenant of good faith and faith dealing is always implied into every K
Seidenberg v. Summit Bankslide 29
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #2: What are the ways in which the duty of good faith and fair dealing have been applied?
It imposes absent terms and conditions
So if a term is missing and it is necessary to give business efficacy to the contract, then we assume it is in the contract.
Allows redress for the bad faith performance of an agreement even when the defendant has not breached any express term.
Permits inquiry into a party’s exercise of discretion expressly granted by a contract’s terms.
Both 2 & 3 have been read to mean that while the duty of good faith and fair dealing cannot override an express term, it does require that a contracting party act in good faith when exercising either its discretion in performing its contractual obligations or its right to terminate.
Seidenberg v. Summit Bankslide 30
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Summit had the right to terminate plaintiffs, yet exercised that right in bad faith
Summit failed to put reasonable efforts into its discretionary activities, such as pursuing leads, marketing efforts, etc.
Seidenberg v. Summit Bankslide 31
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Ultimate result:
The trial court erred by misunderstanding the scope of the duty of good faith and fair dealing in relation to the parol evidence rule. It erred by granting the motion to dismiss, meaning plaintiffs should be allowed to pursue their claim.
Seidenberg v. Summit Bankslide 32
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Final points
The court also tells us “[t]o determine what is considered a good faith performance, the court must consider the expectations of the parties and the purpose for which the contract was made.”
Also, “[t]he guiding principle in the application of the implied covenant of good faith and fair dealing emanates from the fundamental notion that a party to a contract may not unreasonably frustrate its purpose.”
Requirements and Output Contractsslide 33
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Requirements Contract: Party A agrees to use the other party’s (Party B’s) goods or services to supply all of Party A’s requirements and Party B agrees to supply all of Party A’s requirements.
In a sense Party A says that it will use Party B exclusively for its needs.
For example, Jones makes “Jones Organic O’s” a breakfast cereal. Smith has an organic oats farm.
Jones agrees to buy all of the oats Jones requires from Smith & Smith agrees to sell Jones all of the oats Jones requires.
Requirements and Output Contractsslide 34
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Jones agrees to buy all of the oats Jones requires from Smith & Smith agrees to sell Jones all of the oats Jones requires.
How might Jones technically meet his obligations under a requirements contract but violate the duty of good faith and fair dealing?
Jones could “shut down” his business so that his requirements are less than he really needs, perhaps by creating a substitute business that makes “J’s Organic O’s” and that is not obligated under the requirements contract.
Requirements and Output Contractsslide 35
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Output Contract: Party A agrees to sell all of the goods/services Party A outputs to Party B and Party B agrees to buy all of that output from party A.
In a sense Party A says that it will sell exclusively to Party B.
For example, Jones makes “Jones Organic O’s” a breakfast cereal. Smith has an organic oats farm.
Smith agrees to sell all of her oats to Jones & Jones agrees to buy all of the oats Smith produces.
Requirements and Output Contractsslide 36
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith agrees to sell all of her oats to Jones & Jones agrees to buy all of the oats Smith produces.
How might someone technically meet their obligations under a output contract but violate the duty of good faith and fair dealing?
Smith might plant far fewer oats than she ordinarily does or no oats. She would then sell “all” of her crop, thereby meeting the condition.
Good Faith: Satisfaction Clausesslide 37
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: How should the court determine if a “satisfaction clause” has been met?
Two possible standards:
Whether a reasonable person would be satisfied
Whether the party was subjectively satisfied (in good faith)
Good Faith: Satisfaction Clausesslide 38
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rules:
The reasonable person standard is employed when the contract involves commercial quality, operative fitness, or mechanical utility which other knowledgeable persons can judge. Basically, if it is possible to determine whether a reasonable person would be satisfied, the courts use the reasonable person test
The standard of good faith (honest satisfaction) is employed when the contract involves personal aesthetics or fancy.
Morin Building Products Co. v. Baystone Construction, Inc.slide 39
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
GM hired Morin to construct the aluminum walls for an addition to a factory
The work was to be “mill finish”
Work was subject to the approval of GM’s agent
GM rejects the work, because it did not have a uniform finish
Held: GM breaches the duty of good faith. The reasonable person standard is used because this is a contract for the siding of a factory, and mill finish is not uniform. The contract is thus about practical utility rather than aesthetics. A reasonable person would have been satisfied with the finish.
Locke v. Warner Bros., Inc.slide 40
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Locke and Eastwood have a relationship and falling out
Locke and Warner enter into a contract where Locke would receive $250,000 per year for three years, and Locke would submit movie proposals to Warner
Eastwood had an agreement with Warner, where he would reimburse Warner if it did not develop a movie with Locke
Warner did not develop any proposals with Locke
Locke files suit, arguing that Warner never intended to work with her
Issue: Did Warner violate the covenant of good faith and fair dealing by exercising its discretionary power in bad faith?
Locke v. Warner Bros., Inc.slide 41
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rules:
Where a contract confers on one party a discretionary power affecting the rights of the other, a duty is imposed to exercise that discretion in good faith and in accordance with fair dealing.
In every contract there is an implied covenant that neither party shall do anything which will have the effect of destroying or injuring the right of the other party to receive the fruits of the contract.
Where the contract involves matters of fancy, taste or judgment, the promisor is the sole judge of his satisfaction.
Locke v. Warner Bros., Inc.slide 42
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Warner had a duty to consider Locke’s proposals in good faith, because this was the purpose of the contract for Locke
The subjective standard applies, because this is a contract for artistic taste or judgment
Locke has presented evidence that Warner did not honestly consider her proposals, thus failing to meet the subjective standard
Donahue v. Federal Express Corp.slide 43
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts
Donahue is an at-will employee at Fed-Ex. He reports that his boss is engaging in misconduct. Soon thereafter, he is fired.
Donahue argues that FedEx breached the implied duty of good faith and fair dealing by terminating him because he was not treated fairly in the company’s grievance procedures.
Donahue v. Federal Express Corp.slide 44
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule: Terminating an at-will employee cannot violate the duty of good faith and fair dealing
Rationale: Any other rule would turn at-will employment into for-cause termination
Donahue v. Federal Express Corp.slide 45
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Exceptions: According to the court the implied duty of good faith and fair dealing applies to an at-will employment contract with respect to:
Contractual terms other than termination
i.e., promise to pay employee commissions
Termination that results in the loss of previously-earned compensation
Manner of termination if the contract promises a certain type of evaluation
Donahue v. Federal Express Corp.slide 46
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application
Donahue was an at-will employee. He could be fired for any reason or no reason at all.
His firing violated no express right under the contract
Donahue was not owed a commission, and had no contractual right to any notice or grievance procedures
Conclusion: The duty of good faith and fair dealing did not apply to his termination
2
UCC Warranties
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
UCC Warranty가 뭐냐면... 물건 팔 때 따라오는 "품질 보장" 약속이야. 크게 셋이야. ① Express Warranty (명시적 보증): 판매자가 물건에 대해 사실(Fact)을 주장하거나, 샘플/설명(Description)을 보여주면 그게 보증이야. 단, 그냥 "이 차 최고야" 같은 의견(Puffery)은 보증 아님. ② Implied Warranty of Merchantability (묵시적 상품성 보증): Merchant가 파는 물건은 "그 종류의 물건으로 통상적으로 통용될 수 있어야 해(fit for ordinary purpose)." 빵을 샀는데 돌이 들어있으면 → 상품성 위반. ③ Implied Warranty of Fitness for a Particular Purpose (특수 목적 적합성 보증): 판매자가 구매자의 특수 목적을 알고, 전문가로서 적합한 물건을 추천했을 때. 구매자가 그 추천을 믿고 샀으면 → 목적에 안 맞으면 위반.
예시 — 차 딜러가 "이 차 150mph까지 나와"라고 했는데 실제론 안 나와 → Express Warranty 위반. 슈퍼마켓에서 산 오렌지 주스에서 유리조각 나왔어 → Implied Merchantability 위반. 캠핑 전문점이 "이 침낭이 당신 캠핑에 딱이에요"라고 추천했는데 아니었어 → Implied Fitness 위반.
Disclaimer: 보증 포기(As-Is 조항) 가능하지만, 반드시 눈에 잘 보이게(conspicuous) 써야 해.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
What is a warranty?slide 47
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
“Warranty” means an express or implied promise that something in furtherance of the contract is guaranteed by one of the contracting parties.
In essence, it is (1) an enforceable (2) promise (3) that something relating to the contract (4) will be a specific way.
Warranties
(1) Express warranties by the seller are created as follows:slide 48
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
(a) Any affirmation of fact or promise made by the seller to the buyer which relates to the goods and becomes part of the basis of the bargain creates an express warranty that the goods shall conform to the affirmation or promise.
(b) Any description of the goods which is made part of the basis of the bargain creates an express warranty that the goods shall conform to the description.
(c) Any sample or model which is made part of the basis of the bargain creates an express warranty that the whole of the goods shall conform to the sample or model.
U.C.C. § 2-2-313 Express Warranty
(2) It is not necessary to the creation of an express warranty that the seller use formal words such as “warrant” or “guarantee” or that he have a specific intention to make a warranty, but an affirmation merely of the value of the goods or a statement purporting to be merely the seller's opinion or commendation of the goods does not create a warranty.slide 49
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
If the seller is merely "puffing," or clearly expressing an opinion, he will not be held to have made a warranty.
U.C.C. § 2-2-313 Express Warranty
Elements:slide 50
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Affirmation of fact; description; OR sample
Basis of the bargain
U.C.C. § 2-2-313 Express Warranty
Hypothetical 1slide 51
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Car Dealer tells Buyer that a particular car will go up to 150 mph, and Buyer says "Oh, I'm never going to take it above 55.” Is there an express warranty?
Yes
No
Hypothetical 1slide 52
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Car Dealer tells Buyer that a particular car will go up to 150 mph, and Buyer says "Oh, I'm never going to take it above 55.” Is there an express warranty?
Buyer will probably not be able to claim breach of warranty if the car won't go above 120 mph, because the affirmation of fact was not part of the basis of the bargain
Hypothetical 2slide 53
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Seller states that his boat is the “best boat on the market.” Express warranty?
Yes
No
Hypothetical 2slide 54
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Seller states that his boat is the “best boat on the market.”
This is just an opinion. Mere puffing
Unless excluded or modified (Section 2-316), a warranty that the goods shall be merchantable is implied in a contract for their sale if the seller is a merchant with respect to goods of that kind.slide 55
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Goods are merchantable if they “pass without objection in the trade” and are “fit for the ordinary purposes for which such goods are used”
The seller thus usually makes a warranty of merchantability!
U.C.C. § 2-2-314 Implied Warranty of Merchantability
Where the seller at the time of contracting has reason to know any particular purpose for which the goods are required and that the buyer is relying on the seller's skill or judgment to select or furnish suitable goods, there is unless excluded or modified under the next section an implied warranty that the goods shall be fit for such purpose.slide 56
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Arises where seller has reason to know
At time of contracting
Any particular purpose for which goods are required and
That buyer is relying on seller’s skill/judgment to select or furnish suitable goods
U.C.C. § 2-2-315 Implied Warranty of Fitness for a Particular Purpose
UCC §2-316 Exclusion or Modification of Warrantiesslide 57
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Disclaimers of Express Warranties
The seller might give an express warranty, then attempt to disclaim it.
General Rule: If the scope of the dis­claimer is clear, and the scope of the alleged express warranty is not as clear, the court should construe the warranty narrowly, so that it will not conflict with this disclaimer.
But if there is no reasonable way to construe the two as consistent with each other, the disclaimer is ineffective.
Note: the best way for a seller to avoid liability for an express warranty is not to make it in the first place.
UCC §2-316 Exclusion or Modification of Warrantiesslide 58
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Disclaiming the Warranty of Merchantability
This disclaimer may be oral, but if it is writing, it must be “conspicuous.”
“Conspicuous” is defined in UCC § 1-201(10) as "so written ... that a reasonable person against which it is to operate ought to have noticed it."
In other words, the disclaimer cannot be buried in the fine print
UCC §2-316 Exclusion or Modification of Warrantiesslide 59
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Disclaiming Fitness for a Particular Purpose
A disclaimer of the warranty of fitness for a par­ticular purpose must:
(i) always be in writing, and
(ii) be conspicuous.
It does not have to use any particular words
§ 2-316(2) itself provides a sample clause which suffices to exclude all implied warranties of fitness for a particular purpose:
"THERE ARE NO WARRANTIES WHICH EXTEND BEYOND THE DESCRIPTION ON THE FACE HEREOF”
Hypothetical 1slide 60
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith is conducting an estate sale of his late father’s home. Jones comes to the estate sale and sees among the things for purchase is a vintage, all black, 1969 Dodge Charger, and Jones has to have it. When Jones approaches Smith about buying the car, he asks its condition. Smith says, “Well my father wasn’t able to drive it, so it has just been sitting in the garage gathering dust for years.” After giving it a cursory glance, Jones decides to buy it on the spot and drive it home. On the ride home, the car breaks down. The next day, Jones learns that the car’s transmission is blown and will cost $5,000 to repair. Jones sues Smith for breach of warranty. What result?
Jones will win, because a car that breaks down that quickly is not fit for its ordinary purpose.
Smith will win, because he is not a car merchant.
Jones will win, because Smith made a statement of fact that created an express warranty that was breached when the car broke down.
Jones will win, because the car was not fit for his particular purpose

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Now suppose the parties sign a written document stating that the car is being sold “AS IS, with no warranties beyond the description in this document.” Assume the document mentions nothing about towing capacity.
Yes, this is a valid disclaimer
Under the classic principle of caveat emptor (let the buyer beware) the seller bore no responsibility at all for the quality of the product he was selling unless he expressly guaranteed it or gave a “warranty” to the buyer.slide 70
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Modern courts have created warranties, such as the warranty of habitability, in limited circumstances like home construction
Common Law Warranties
3
Breach & Conditions
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Breach가 뭐냐면... 계약상 의무가 발생했는데 이행하지 않은 거야. 근데 모든 불이행이 다 같은 게 아니야 — Material이냐 Immaterial이냐가 핵심이야. Material Breach vs. Immaterial: - Material Breach: 상대방이 계약 전체를 해제(terminate)하고 손해배상 청구 가능 - Immaterial(Minor) Breach: 상대방은 계약을 계속 이행해야 하고, 손해만 청구 가능 Substantial Performance: 완벽하진 않아도 거의 다 이행했으면(substantial), 상대방도 의무를 이행해야 해. Jacob & Youngs v. Kent — 배관 브랜드가 달랐어도 실질적으로 이행 완료. Anticipatory Repudiation: 이행 기일 전에 "안 할 거야"라고 확실히 의사표시 하면, 상대방은 그 즉시 계약 해제 + 손해배상 청구 가능. 기다릴 필요 없어.
예시 — Otto가 Edward 거실을 $500에 2월 1일 페인트칠하기로 했어. Edward는 Otto가 칠하기 전에 먼저 돈을 줘야 해? No — 칠하는 게 먼저(Condition Precedent)이고, 그 다음 돈. Otto가 1월 15일에 "안 할 거야"라고 하면? → Anticipatory Repudiation → Edward는 즉시 다른 화가 고용하고 손해배상 청구 가능.
UCC Perfect Tender Rule: 물건 판매는 기본적으로 완벽한 이행 요구. 조금이라도 하자 있으면 거절(reject) 가능. 단, Installment Contract이면 Substantial Impairment 기준.

Implied Terms and Warranties
Breach
When two parties form a contract, they create duties/obligations to each other.slide 73
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Those duties usually are triggered by something,
I don’t have to pay you $500 until you paint my living room.
Breach occurs when one party’s duty to do something has arisen (you painted my living room) but the party with the duty did not do what they were obligated to do (I didn’t pay you).slide 74
📝 한글
Hypotheticalslide 75
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Otto and Edward enter into an agreement under which Otto will paint Edward’s living room for $500 on February 1st when Otto completes painting the living room.
Otto shows up on February 1st ready, willing and able to paint the room. Edward refuses to pay Otto before Otto begins to paint.
Edward has not breached. His duty to pay has not arisen yet.
Hypotheticalslide 76
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Otto and Edward enter into an agreement under which Otto will paint Edward’s living room for $500 on February 1st when Otto completes painting the living room.
Otto paints half of the room and then demands that Edward pay him half of the money. Edward refuses to pay Otto before Otto finishes the job.
Edward has not breached. His duty to pay has not arisen yet.
Hypotheticalslide 77
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Otto and Edward enter into an agreement under which Otto will paint Edward’s living room for $500 on February 1st when Otto completes painting the living room.
Otto paints the entire room and then asks Edward to pay him $500. Edward realizes he only has $499. He pays Otto that amount and promises to pay the rest tomorrow when he gets the ATM.
Edward has breached. He did not pay $500
Conditionsslide 78
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Some duties only become due after a condition is met.
Example: I will purchase your car, but only if I get a my promotion at work.
Hypothetical 1slide 80
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
On July 1, 2013, Paul promises to pay Bob $100 on July 15, 2013.
This promise is not conditional
There is no condition because the event (the arrival of July 15, 2013) is certain to happen.
Lapse of time is not treated as a condition because it is looked on as an event certain to occur.
Hypothetical 2slide 81
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
On July 1, 2013, Paul promises to pay Bob $100 on July 15, 2013 if it rains on July 2, 2013.
This promise is conditional.
There is an event (raining on July 2) that is not certain to occur, that must occur, that isn’t excused, before performance (paying Bob $100) is due.
Two systems of classificationslide 82
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Time when the conditioning event is to happen in relation to the promisor’s duty to perform a promise
Condition precedent: an act or event, other than a lapse of time, which must exist or occur before a duty to perform a promise arises.
Condition concurrent: the parties are to exchange performances at the same time
Condition subsequent: any event the existence of which, by agreement of the parties, discharges a duty of performance that has arisen.
Time class of conditionsslide 83
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A condition precedent forestalls creation of the duty
A condition concurrent makes creation of the duty simultaneous for both parties.
A condition subsequent discharges a duty that already exists.
Two systems of classificationslide 84
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Manner in which the condition arises
Constructive conditions: implied by law
Express conditions: created by parties.
Conditionsslide 85
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Time
Manner
Condition subsequent
Condition precedent
Condition concurrent
Express Condition
Constructive condition
Hypotheticalslide 86
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
John has an insurance policy that includes the clause “No claims will be paid unless the insured files a claim with the insurer within 10 calendar days of any loss.”
Express condition subsequent because it specifies how a duty that already exists (the duty to pay insured’s claims) may later be discharged without performing the duty.
Hypotheticalslide 87
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Sally agrees to sell her car to Jane for $5,000.
What type of condition is this?
In the absence of an agreement to the contrary, payment and delivery are constructive concurrent conditions.
Under the doctrine of constructive conditions, if Jane fails to tender the price ($5,000), Sally must make conditional tender of the car to show that tender is excused and to put Jane in default.
In essence, if payment and delivery are concurrent conditions and the other party doesn’t show up to pay, to get the other party for breach, you have to say “Hey, I am ready to deliver the car if you pay up.”
Hypotheticalslide 88
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Tom agrees to pay John $1,000 if a specified ship arrives in port before a certain date.
Condition precedent.
Tom’s duty to pay does not arise unless and until the ship arrives.
If the ship does not arrive by the date, then Tom has no duty to pay.
Hypotheticalslide 89
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith enters into a contract with Construction Co. for the construction of a new home for $200,000. A provision in the contract states that Smith’s obligation to pay the $200,000 will arise only if he can obtain financing for a mortgage. This provision is:
Not a condition
A constructive condition
A condition precedent
A condition subsequent
Hypotheticalslide 90
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith enters into a contract with Construction Co. for the construction of a new home for $200,000. A provision in the contract states that Smith’s obligation to pay the $200,000 will arise only if he can obtain financing for a mortgage. This provision is:
Not a condition
A constructive condition
A condition precedent
A condition subsequent
Conditions serve an important function because they allocate the risk between the parties that one of the parties will not perform.slide 91
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
If I agree to buy your house but make my offer to buy contingent on my getting a mortgage, then I have a condition precedent to my duty to buying your house.
This shifts the risk of my not getting the mortgage to you.
Distinction between a promise and a conditionslide 92
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A promise is a contractual undertaking, breach of which leads to liability for damages or equitable relief.
Failure to perform a promise, unless excused, is a breach.
A condition, is a fact, the occurrence or nonoccurrence of which determines when and if a party must perform.
Failure of a condition to be satisfied is not a breach.
Conditions
(condition precedent, condition subsequent)
Forfeitureslide 93
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 229. Excuse Of A Condition To Avoid Forfeiture
To the extent that the non-occurrence of a condition would cause disproportionate forfeiture, a court may excuse the non-occurrence of that condition unless its occurrence was a material part of the agreed exchange
Forfeitureslide 94
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A forfeiture occurs when a party relied on the bargain (as by preparing to perform or making part performance), and compliance with the condition would make that party lose its benefit from the deal
Hypotheticalslide 95
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Construction Co. enters into a contract with Smith to build a home for $200,000. The contract is expressly conditioned on Construction Co. building to Smith’s specifications. After the house is completed, Smith discovers that the house is set several feet back further than the specifications dictate.
If the condition is enforced, and thus Smith need not pay, Construction Co. will suffer a forfeiture
Oppenheimer & Co. v. Oppenheim, Appel, Dixon & Co.slide 96
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Plaintiff is leasing office space
Plaintiff decides to move offices
Plaintiff’s new landlord promises that it will pay Plaintiff if Plaintiff is unable to get out of its current lease
Parties enter into a sublease for Plaintiff’s old office space
Condition precedent: Plaintiff must deliver to Defendant the prime landlord’s written consent to certain tenant work by a specified deadline
Duty to undertake sublease does not arise until written consent is given
Plaintiff orally tells Defendant that prime landlord has consented, but fails to deliver written consent by the deadline
Defendant then claims the sublease is invalid because of the failure of the condition precedent
Oppenheimer & Co. v. Oppenheim, Appel, Dixon & Co.slide 97
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether the minor failure of the condition prevents the duties from arising
Holding: Yes. Express conditions must be performed exactly
Oppenheimer & Co. v. Oppenheim, Appel, Dixon & Co.slide 98
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule: To the extent that the non-occurrence of a condition would cause disproportionate forfeiture, a court may excuse the non-occurrence of that condition unless its occurrence was a material part of the agreed exchange
Application: Plaintiff will suffer no forfeiture, because its new landlord will pay it for any loss
J.N.A. Realty Corp. v. Cross Bay Chelsea, Inc.slide 99
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Lease for commercial property
Lease gives Chelsea option to renew for 10 years provided “that Tenant shall notify the landlord in writing by registered or certified mail six (6) months prior to the last day of the term of the lease”
Lease is assigned to Chelsea, and Chelsea is given option to renew for 24 years
Chelsea operates a restaurant for 5 years, and makes improvements to property
JNA sends letters to Chelsea, but does not notify Chelsea of need to renew
Chelsea doesn’t timely renew
JNA gives Chelsea notice that it failed to renew
J.N.A. Realty Corp. v. Cross Bay Chelsea, Inc.slide 100
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Under what circumstances may a party avoid the non-occurrence of a condition?
Rule: If the non-occurrence of a condition would cause disproportionate forfeiture, a court may excuse the non-occurrence of that condition unless its occurrence was a material part of the agreed exchange
Application:
Tenant would lose improvements made to the real estate in good faith and the good faith from the location of the restaurant
But, the record doesn’t show if JNA would be prejudiced, so don’t know if the forfeiture is disproportionate
Hypotheticalslide 101
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith dents his BMW in a parking garage. His neighbor, Jones, is an auto mechanic. Jones takes a look at the car and tells Smith that he can order a new panel from BMW. Smith and Jones enter into a contract to replace the panel at cost plus labor, but the contract is expressly conditioned on obtaining Smith’s prior approval of the price before any work is done. When Jones takes the car to his shop, he discovers a much cheaper panel from a used BMW that is in great condition. Without contacting Smith, Jones installs the used panel. If Smith refuses to pay, what is Jones’s best argument?
Smith breached the contract by refusing to pay
Jones substantially performed under the contract
Jones’s failure to obtain Smith’s approval should be excused because otherwise Jones will suffer a forfeiture
Jones’s failure to obtain Smith’s approval should be excused because the cost was much lower than contemplated

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문

Smith and Jones enter into a contract to replace the panel at cost plus labor, but the contract is expressly conditioned on obtaining Smith’s prior approval of the price before any work is done. When Jones takes the car to his shop, he discovers a much cheaper panel from a used BMW that is in great condition. Without contacting Smith, Jones installs the used panel. If Smith refuses to pay, what is Jones’s best argument?
Smith breached the contract by refusing to pay
Jones substantially performed under the contract
Jones’s failure to obtain Smith’s approval should be excused because otherwise Jones will suffer a forfeiture

Amounts of Breachslide 103
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
As we will learn, breach comes in many levels and those levels affect what happens to the breaching party and what happens to the duties of the non-breaching party.
Breach
Total
Partial
Material
What effect does breach have on a non-breaching party?slide 104
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Breach
Duty of non-breaching party to perform
Partial
Must continue to perform under the contract.
Material
Duty to perform may be suspended until breaching party cures breach.
Total
Relieves/discharges from duties under contract.
Partial Breachslide 105
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A partial breach is a non-performance of duty that is not a material breach.
The nonbreaching party must continue to perform under the contract.
Substantial Performance
Material Breachslide 106
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 241: In determining whether a failure to render or to offer performance is material, the following circumstances are significant:
the extent to which the injured party will be deprived of the benefit which he reasonably expected;
the extent to which the injured party can be adequately compensated for the part of that benefit of which he will be deprived;
the extent to which the party failing to perform or to offer to perform will suffer forfeiture;
the likelihood that the party failing to perform or to offer to perform will cure his failure, taking account of all the circumstances including any reasonable assurances;
the extent to which the behavior of the party failing to perform or to offer to perform comports with standards of good faith and fair dealing.
Material Breach: Jacob & Youngs, Inc. v. Kentslide 107
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Relevant facts?
Plaintiff had a house built ($77,000 around 1920).
Contract contained clause “All wrought-iron pipe must be well galvanized, lap welded pipe of the grade known as ‘standard pipe’ of Reading manufacture.”
Home was built with comparable pipe but not of Reading manufacture.
Contract contained express condition that final payment ($3,484.46) is to be made on provision of certificate of completeness from architect.
Architect refuses to provide such a certificate because of failure to use Reading pipe.
Homeowner refuses to make final payment
Jacob & Youngs, Inc. v. Kentslide 108
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Jacob & Youngs breached the contract
But it was not a material breach. Instead, Jacob & Youngs substantially performed
Rule: substantial performance is when:
There are minor defects or omissions (that can be remedied),
The party has performed in all material and substantive particulars, or
The contractual deviations or deficiencies do not severely impair the purpose of the contract requirements.
Application: Reading and Cohoes pipe were of equal quality. Kent got what he bargained for, which is a working house.
Jacob & Youngs, Inc. v. Kentslide 109
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What does it mean to say that Jacob & Youngs substantially performed? What is the practical significance in this case? Does Kent have to perform under the contract?
Under the doctrine of “constructive conditions,” courts imply that a party’s performance is conditional on the substantial performance of the other party (a party need not perform if the other party has materially breached). When a party “substantially performs” (the breach is not material), this constructive condition is satisfied. Thus, the non-breaching party must perform. Here, Kent must pay Jacob & Youngs the remaining $3,483.
Jacob & Youngs, Inc. v. Kentslide 110
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Does this mean that Kent is out of luck? What damages may a plaintiff receive when the defendant substantially performs?
“The owner is entitled to the money which will permit him to complete, unless the cost of completion is grossly and unfairly out of proportion to the good to be attained. When that is true, the measure is the difference in value.”
Jacob & Youngs, Inc. v. Kentslide 111
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What is the policy basis for the doctrine of substantial performance? Why do we have it?
The court references “considerations partly of justice and partly of presumable intention.”
Jacob & Youngs, Inc. v. Kentslide 112
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if Kent had really wanted Reading Pipe? What could he have done?
Kent could have made it a condition of his payment!

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문

A has breached the contract, and B need not perform
A has breached the contract, but B must still perform under the contract
A has not breached the contract, and B must perform
A has not breached the contract, but B need not perform

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Breach
Total
Partial
