Total Breach: Restatement (Second) Contracts § 242slide 116
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material breach factors
the extent to which it reasonably appears to the injured party that delay may prevent or hinder him in making reasonable substitute arrangements;
the extent to which the agreement provides for performance without delay, but a material failure to perform or to offer to perform on a stated day does not of itself discharge the other party's remaining duties unless the circumstances, including the language of the agreement, indicate that performance or an offer to perform by that day is important.
Total Breach: Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 242slide 117
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Factor Test:
Injured Party
How much will the IP be deprived of benefit of what IP reasonably expected to get?
How well can IP adequately compensated for what IP did not get?
Breaching Party
How much will BP lose if IP is excused from performance?
How likely is it that BP will cure the breach (perform)?
To what extent did BP act in good/bad faith?
Importance of Delay to Injured Party
To IP how likely would it seem that delay will impair IP’s ability to make substitute arrangements?
If the agreement gives a time for performance, if that time was not met, at the time of breach how important would it seem for the IP to be excused from the IP’s remaining duties?
Sackett v. Spindlerslide 118
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Spindler owns a newspaper
Spindler and Sackett enter into a contract to sell the newspaper for $85,000
Sackett pays about $25,000, but is unable to pay the remainder
Spindler is unable to run the paper at a profit
Spindler sells to a third party for $22,000
Sackett v. Spindlerslide 119
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether Spindler was justified in telling Sackett that he would no longer sell the newspaper. In other words, was Spindler’s termination of the contract itself a breach?
Rule: A party’s obligations under a contract are discharged when the other party’s breach is classified as a total breach
Application: The breach is total, because Spindler needed to act quickly to save the value of the newspaper. Spindler was thus justified in canceling the contract and selling to someone else
Sackett v. Spindlerslide 120
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Suppose the court had determined that Sackett’s actions constituted a material breach rather than total breach. How would the court have resolved the dispute?
Spindler would have breached, because he would not have had the right to cancel the contract. A nonbreaching party who elects to suspend performance or terminate a contract is taking a risk!

Anticipatory Repudiationslide 123
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
You have to take two steps to excuse your client from performance as a result of another party’s repudiation.
First, use the definition of repudiation to prove the other party repudiated.
Second, determine the effect of the repudiation to prove what your client may do in response.
Anticipatory Repudiationslide 124
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A repudiation is
a statement by the obligor to the obligee indicating that the obligor will commit a breach that would of itself give the obligee a claim for damages for total breach under § 243, or
a voluntary affirmative act which renders the obligor unable or apparently unable to perform without such a breach.
Anticipatory Repudiationslide 125
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 253
(1) Where an obligor repudiates a duty before he has committed a breach by non-performance and before he has received all of the agreed exchange for it, his repudiation alone gives rise to a claim for damages for total breach.
(2) Where performances are to be exchanged under an exchange of promises, one party's repudiation of a duty to render performance discharges the other party's remaining duties to render performance

Anticipatory Repudiation: Retractionslide 128
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 256
(1) The effect of a statement as constituting a repudiation under § 250 or the basis for a repudiation under § 251 is nullified by a retraction of the statement if notification of the retraction comes to the attention of the injured party before he materially changes his position in reliance on the repudiation or indicates to the other party that he considers the repudiation to be final.
(2) The effect of events other than a statement as constituting a repudiation under § 250 or the basis for a repudiation under § 251 is nullified if, to the knowledge of the injured party, those events have ceased to exist before he materially changes his position in reliance on the repudiation or indicates to the other party that he considers the repudiation to be final.

Indicated to other party considers repudiation to be final
Repudiation is nullified!

Truman L. Flatt & Sons Co. v. Schupfslide 130
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Contract for the sale of land for $160,000
Truman’s obligation to purchase is contingent on rezoning of the land
On May 21st, Truman’s attorney sends letter indicating its decision not to appeal from zoning change b/c no chance of success and offering to buy property for $142,500 under current zoning.
Schupf rejects the offer to buy for $142,500
Truman then attempts to purchase for $160,000
Schupf refuses and claims the contract is void
Truman L. Flatt & Sons Co. v. Schupfslide 131
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #1: Was there an anticipatory repudiation?
Rule: Doctrine of anticipatory repudiation requires a clear (definite and unequivocal) manifestation of intent not to perform the contract on the date of performance
Truman L. Flatt & Sons Co. v. Schupfslide 132
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application: Was the May 21st letter a clear manifestation of intent not to perform the contract on the date of performance?
No. Truman’s attorney sent letter indicating its decision not to appeal from zoning change b/c no chance of success and offering to buy property for $142,500 under current zoning. This “at most created an ambiguous implication whether performance would occur.”
Truman L. Flatt & Sons Co. v. Schupfslide 133
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What must the letter have said to constitute anticipatory repudiation?
The zoning change will not succeed, and we will not buy the property unless the price is dropped to $142,500
Truman L. Flatt & Sons Co. v. Schupfslide 134
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #2: Even if there were a repudiation, did Truman (plaintiff/buyer) validly retract it?
Yes. Why?
Schupf did not rely on the repudiation or indicate to Truman that he considered the repudiation to be final.

Right to Assuranceslide 137
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 251.
(1) Where reasonable grounds arise to believe that the obligor will commit a breach by non-performance that would of itself give the obligee a claim for damages for total breach under § 243, the obligee may demand adequate assurance of due performance and may, if reasonable, suspend any performance for which he has not already received the agreed exchange until he receives such assurance.
(2) The obligee may treat as a repudiation the obligor's failure to provide within a reasonable time such assurance of due performance as is adequate in the circumstances of the particular case.
Right to Assuranceslide 138
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
UCC § 2-609. Right to Adequate Assurance of Performance.
(1) A contract for sale imposes an obligation on each party that the other's expectation of receiving due performance will not be impaired. When reasonable grounds for insecurity arise with respect to the performance of either party the other may in writing demand adequate assurance of due performance and until he receives such assurance may if commercially reasonable suspend any performance for which he has not already received the agreed return.
(2) Between merchants the reasonableness of grounds for insecurity and the adequacy of any assurance offered shall be determined according to commercial standards.
(3) Acceptance of any improper delivery or payment does not prejudice the aggrieved party's right to demand adequate assurance of future performance.
(4) After receipt of a justified demand failure to provide within a reasonable time not exceeding thirty days such assurance of due performance as is adequate under the circumstances of the particular case is a repudiation of the contract.
Right to Assuranceslide 139
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
UCC § 2-609. Right to Adequate Assurance of Performance.
(1) A contract for sale imposes an obligation on each party that the other's expectation of receiving due performance will not be impaired. When reasonable grounds for insecurity arise with respect to the performance of either party the other may in writing demand adequate assurance of due performance and until he receives such assurance may if commercially reasonable suspend any performance for which he has not already received the agreed return.
(2) Between merchants the reasonableness of grounds for insecurity and the adequacy of any assurance offered shall be determined according to commercial standards.
(3) Acceptance of any improper delivery or payment does not prejudice the aggrieved party's right to demand adequate assurance of future performance.
(4) After receipt of a justified demand failure to provide within a reasonable time not exceeding thirty days such assurance of due performance as is adequate under the circumstances of the particular case is a repudiation of the contract.
This is essentially the same as the common law
Hornell Brewing Co. v. Spryslide 140
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Hornell grants Spry the exclusive right to purchase Arizona Tea for sale in Canada
Spry fails to timely pay invoices for products ordered
Spry claims to have a $1,500,000 line of credit
Hornell promises allow Spry a balance of $300,000 once paid in full
Spry pays in full, but then attempts to order $450,000 of product from Hornell
Hornell demands a letter confirming the existence of Spry’s line of credit and a personal guarantee
Spry does not respond
Hornell files a suit for declaratory judgment
Hornell Brewing Co. v. Spryslide 141
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #1: Did Hornell have “reasonable grounds for insecurity”?
Look to the party’s words, course of dealing or performance, nature of the contract and industry
Application: Hornell had reasonable grounds for insecurity because of his late payments, large order, and the industry rumors
Hornell Brewing Co. v. Spryslide 142
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #2: Were the assurances demanded by Hornell proper?
Yes. Given the facts and circumstances, it was reasonable for Hornell to seek documentation of a line of credit or other guarantee
What was the legal effect of Spry’s failure to reply to Hornell’s demand for assurances?
Failure to respond to a demand for assurances constitutes anticipatory repudiation.

Expectation Damages — Introduction
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Damages가 뭐냐면... 계약 위반 당했을 때 받을 수 있는 금전 보상이야. 계약법 손해배상은 "계약이 이행됐다면 당신이 있었을 상태(as-if-performed)"를 만들어주는 게 목표야. Expectation Damages 공식: 손해 = (받았어야 할 가치) - (실제 받은 가치) + (기타 손해) - (비용 절약분) - (손해 회피분) 쉽게: "계약대로 됐다면 얼마? 실제론 얼마? 그 차이." 3가지 제한: ① Foreseeability: 계약 당시 예측 가능했던 손해만 (Hadley v. Baxendale) ② Certainty: 손해 금액을 합리적으로 확정할 수 있어야 해 (추측 안 됨) ③ Mitigation: 피해자도 손해 최소화 노력해야 해
Hadley v. Baxendale — 제분소 주인이 부품을 수리점에 보냈어. 운반이 늦어져 제분소가 며칠 문 닫았어. 제분소는 문 닫은 동안 영업 손실을 청구했어. 법원: No — 운반업자는 이 부품이 제분소 유일한 부품이고 안 오면 영업이 중단된다는 걸 몰랐어. 특수 상황은 계약 시 미리 알려줘야 해.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Damagesslide 145
📝 한글
Breach of contract actionslide 146
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Promissory estoppel action
Restitution/unjust enrichment action
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 347. Measure Of Damages In Generalslide 147
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Subject to the limitations stated in §§ 350-53, the injured party has a right to damages based on his expectation interest as measured by
the loss in the value to him of the other party's performance caused by its failure or deficiency, plus
(b) any other loss, including incidental or consequential loss, caused by the breach, less
(c) any cost or other loss that he has avoided by not having to perform.
Expectation Damages
Expectation Damagesslide 148
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What do we mean by:
Loss in value,
Other Loss,
Cost Avoided, and
Loss Avoided?
Expectation Damagesslide 149
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Loss in value: The difference between value of the performance that should have been received and value of what was received.
Other loss: Incidental & Consequential damages caused by the breach
Incidental: Includes additional costs incurred after the breach in a reasonable attempt to avoid loss
Consequential: Losses beyond general damages that the plaintiff would never have incurred but for the breach.
Cost avoided: Amount saved by nonbreaching party because of not having to make expenditures that would have been incurred during performance.
Loss avoided: Amount saved by nonbreaching party by avoiding some loss.
Expectation Damagesslide 150
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Loss in value: The difference between value of the performance that should have been received and value of what was received.
Other loss: Incidental & Consequential damages
Incidental: Includes additional costs incurred after the breach in a reasonable attempt to avoid loss
Consequential: Losses beyond general damages that the plaintiff would never have incurred but for the breach.
Cost avoided: Amount saved by nonbreaching party because of not having to make expenditures that would have been incurred during performance.
Loss avoided: Amount saved by nonbreaching party by avoiding some loss.
These are only relevant with a total breach!
Expectation Damagesslide 151
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Loss in Value
Mitigation
Other Loss
Cost and Loss Avoided
The difference between what was promised and what was received
Damages that the nonbreaching party avoided or should have avoided
Must be:
Foreseeable
Reasonably Certain
Money saved because of total breach
Hawkins v. McGeeslide 152
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts:
Hawkin’s hand is disfigured in an electrical accident.
Hawkins enters into a contract with McGee, a doctor, who promises to make his hand 100% good
McGee fails to remove the scars, and his skin grafting technique makes Hawkin’s hand grow thick hair
Hawkins v. McGeeslide 153
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: What are Hawkins’ damages for the breach of contract?
Rule: Loss in Value = the difference between value of the performance that should have been received and value of what was received
Application:
McGee argues he should only have to pay the difference between the disfigured hand and the hairy hand (the hand before surgery vs. the hand after surgery)
Court holds that damages = difference between a 100% good hand and Hawkins’ actual hairy hand
Cost to find a new doctorslide 154
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Suppose Hawkins is fired from his employment because of his injuries

Hypotheticalslide 167
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
On May 5th, Smith hired Jones to make a life size statue of Smith out of steel wire. Smith agreed to pay Jones $6,000 for the statue. Jones agreed to complete the statue within 3 months (by August 5th). Two months later, Jones was two thirds complete with the work when Smith called Jones and told Jones to stop building the statue and that Smith would not pay anything for it.
Jones had spent $2,000 on building it thus far.
It would have cost another $1,000 to complete.
There are no other buyers for the statue.
Jones sold the statue for $500 for scrap (the only buyer available).
What are Jones’ damages?
$2,000
$3,000
$4,500
$6,000
Hypotheticalslide 168
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
On May 5th, Smith hired Jones to make a life size statue of Smith out of steel wire. Smith agreed to pay Jones $6,000 for the statue. Jones agreed to complete the statue within 3 months (by August 5th). Two months later, Jones was two thirds complete with the work when Smith called Jones and told Jones to stop building the statue and that Smith would not pay anything for it.
Jones had spent $2,000 on building it thus far.
It would have cost another $1,000 to complete.
There are no other buyers for the statue.
Jones sold the statue for $500 for scrap (the only buyer available).
What are Jones’ damages?
Loss in value + other loss – cost avoided – loss avoided
$6,000 + $0 - $1,000 - $500 = $4,500
Damages Casesslide 169
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
These cases help us understand what “loss in value” means in different circumstances
Loss in value = The difference between value of the performance that should have been received and value of what was received.
Real estate = difference between purchase price and fair market value
Employment = cost of obtaining other services equivalent to that promised but not performed
Construction = cost to complete or diminution in market value
Loss of Value in Real Estate Casesslide 170
📝 한글
Crabby’s Inc. v. Hamiltonslide 171
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Plaintiff enters into a contract to sell property to defendant for $290,000
Defendant failed to appear to closing and bought a different building
Plaintiff sold the property to a third party one year later for $235,000
Crabby’s Inc. v. Hamiltonslide 172
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What is the value of the performance that Crabby’s should have received?
The contract price of $290,000
What is the value of the performance that was received? In other words, how does the court put a value on Crabby’s property after the breach?
“Fair Market Value” What does that mean?
Fair market value = the price which property will bring when it is offered for sale by an owner who is willing but under no compulsion to sell and is bought by a buyer who is willing or desires to purchase but is not compelled to.
If real property is sold within a reasonable time after the breach, the price obtained is some evidence of market value.
The Jury found that fair market value was $235,000 because it was relisted immediately, and this was the best price that was offered.
Crabby’s Inc. v. Hamiltonslide 173
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
So what were Crabby’s damages?
Expectation damages = Loss in value + other loss – cost avoided – loss avoided
Loss in value =
K price ($290,000) – fair market value at time of breach ($235,000)
Other Loss =
Other costs, such as property taxes, utilities, and interest
Crabby’s Inc. v. Hamiltonslide 174
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Suppose Crabby’s had sold the property to a second buyer for $290,000. What would its damages have been in a breach of contract case against Hamilton?
Remember: expectation damages = Loss in value + other loss – cost avoided – loss avoided
Loss in value:
None! K price – fair market price = 0
Other Loss =
Other costs, such as property taxes, utilities, and interest
Loss in Value in Employment Casesslide 175
📝 한글
Handicapped Children’s Education Board v. Lukaszewskislide 176
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Defendant was hired as a speech and language therapist by plaintiff under a one year contract
Defendant received a better job offer, but plaintiff would not release her from her contract
Defendant breached the contract by resigning
Plaintiff looked for a replacement; only one qualified person applied. This person was paid $1,026 more per year under the collective bargaining agreement
Handicapped Children’s Education Board v. Lukaszewskislide 177
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Loss in value:
In employment cases, damages for breach of an employment contract include the cost of obtaining other services equivalent to that promised but not performed, plus any foreseeable consequential damages.
But didn’t the Board hire a more qualified teacher? Why should it get that benefit for free?
The Board didn’t expect to get that benefit from the bargain, so it shouldn’t have to pay for it.
Handicapped Children’s Education Board v. Lukaszewskislide 178
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Does this mean the Board could have used the breach as an excuse to hire a much more qualified person at a lower cost?
No, the employer must mitigate its damages --- it must use reasonable efforts to fill the position with a comparable person.
What if the employer can’t find a comparable employee at the same wage?
The risk that the employer cannot find a comparable person and must pay a higher salary falls on the employee
Loss in Value in Construction Casesslide 179
📝 한글
Loss in Value in Construction Casesslide 180
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Cost to complete the work is the default measure of damages
Diminution in value is the measure only when: (1) breaching party substantially performed; and (2) actually completing the work would produce economic waste
Economic waste is not the same thing as a bad bargain! Look not just to whether the cost to complete exceeds the diminution in value, but also at whether completing the work would require the breaching party to tear down what was already performed
American Standard, Inc. v. Schectmanslide 181
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Plaintiffs hired defendant to grade its property to one foot below grade lines
Defendant did not grade below the grade line, thus breaching the contract
Defendant claims the value of the property is the same as graded as if it was graded below the grade line
Plaintiff sold the property only $3,000 below market value
Cost to grade one foot below the grade line was about $90,000
American Standard, Inc. v. Schectmanslide 182
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: whether we should use the cost to complete or the decrease in market value (how much the value our bargain gone down due to the breach) to measure the loss in value
Rule:
Cost to complete is the default or normal rule. In the usual case where the contractor’s performance has been defective or incomplete, the reasonable cost of replacement or completion is the measure.
Decrease in value: When there has been a substantial performance of the contract made in good faith but defects exists, the correction of which would result in economic waste, courts have measured the damages as the difference between the value of the property as constructed and the value if performance had been properly completed.
American Standard, Inc. v. Schectmanslide 183
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
The court uses the cost to complete measure. Damages are the amount of money it would take to complete the work.
There was no substantial performance.
Grading was part of the consideration for conveying the property.
It was therefore not incidental but a central part of the bargain.
A bad bargain is not the equivalent of economic waste which is necessary to invoke the rule of Jacob and Youngs.
Measuring the loss in valueslide 184
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Cost to complete is the normal measure because:
Market value = valuation by others
Plaintiff may place a higher value on the property than others
Injured party is actually put in the same position as if the K was performed, because he/she can pay someone else to finish performance
So why do we ever use diminution in value?
Awarding cost to complete can be inefficient and a windfall to the nonbreaching party
Hypothetical 1slide 185
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith thinks that his kitchen is ugly and looks outdated. He thus forms a contract with Contractor to remodel. The contract specifies that Contractor must replace the cabinets, countertops, and tile with certain materials selected by Smith. Contractor performs his work while Smith is out of town. When Smith returns, he discovers that Smith installed the wrong cabinets, counter-tops, and tile. Contractor realizes that, in an honest mistake, he installed materials that a different customer had picked out. Contractor refuses to remove the materials he installed and put the proper materials in. He tells Smith that he is simply too busy with other projects. However, Contractor assures Smith that the materials used are of the same quality and will make Smith’s home have an equal value as if the proper materials had been installed. If Smith sues for breach, which of the follow would be true:
Smith would lose, because Contractor did not breach
Smith’s damages would be measured by the cost for Smith to hire a comparable contractor to install the proper cabinets, countertops, and tile listed in the contract
Smith’s damages would be measured by the diminution in the value of Smith’s home caused by Contractor’s failure to use the materials listed in the contract

Hypothetical 2slide 187
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Frank has always dreamed of having a brightly colored home on the beach near St. Augustine, Florida. When he finally saves up enough money, he finds the perfect home--except that it is dull brown in color. Frank buys the house anyway and contracts to have Bob paint the stucco bright green for $400. Frank pays Bob the $400 in advance. Bob isn’t the best at mixing paint, and, by mistake, the house ends up being a light, dull green color. Disappointed in the result, Frank tells Bob to repaint the house. Happy with his work and busy with other projects, Bob tells Frank that he won’t redo the work because the house looks great the way it is. Frank’s realtor advises him to follow Bob’s advice, because the house is worth more having a more normal and attractive color. If Frank sues Bob for breach of contract, which of the following is true?
Frank’s damages would be $400
Frank’s damages would be zero, because the value of his home was not diminished
Frank’s damages would be measured by how much it would cost Frank to hire someone else to paint the house bright green
Frank’s damages would be limited to the cost of the paint

UDSL 슬라이드 원문 — Class 6 — Damages
1
Expectation Damages
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Expectation Damages 핵심이 뭐냐면... "공사 완료" 계약에서 상대방이 중간에 그만뒀을 때 기준이 두 가지야 — Cost to Complete(완공 비용) vs. Diminution in Value(가치 감소분). 원칙: 기본은 Cost to Complete야. 약속대로 완공해달라는 게 당연한 권리거든. 예외 — Diminution in Value: 완공 비용이 가치 증가분보다 극도로 불균형하고, 위반이 의도적이지 않으며, 실질적 이익이 미미할 때만. Jacob & Youngs v. Kent가 대표 판례. Mitigation 의무: 손해를 합리적으로 줄일 수 있었는데 안 했으면 그 부분은 못 받아. 해고당한 직원은 유사한 일자리 구해야 해 — 근데 "열등하거나 다른 종류"의 일은 거부해도 돼.
Parker v. Fox Film — 유명 배우가 영화 계약 취소당했어. 제작사가 다른 영화 제안했는데 거절했어. 법원: 제안받은 영화가 "comparable(비슷한)" 역할이었나? 다른 장르에 주연 아닌 역할이라면 거부해도 OK — Mitigation 의무 없음. Comparable이면 거부하면 Mitigation 실패.
Lost Volume Seller: 판매자가 공급이 넘치는 경우, 구매자가 계약 취소해도 판매자가 어차피 두 건 다 팔 수 있었다면 → 그 이익을 전액 손해배상 받을 수 있어.

Loss in Valueslide 3
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
These cases help us understand what “loss in value” means in different circumstances
Loss in value = The difference between value of the performance that should have been received and value of what was received.
Real estate = difference between purchase price and fair market value
Employment = cost of obtaining other services equivalent to that promised but not performed
Construction = cost to complete or diminution in market value
Loss in Valueslide 4
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Cost to complete the work is the default measure of damages
Diminution in value is the measure only when: (1) breaching party substantially performed; and (2) actually completing the work would produce economic waste
Economic waste is not the same thing as a bad bargain! Look not just to whether the cost to complete exceeds the diminution in value, but also at whether completing the work would require the breaching party to tear down that was already performed
Restrictions on Expectation Damagesslide 5
📝 한글
Other Lossslide 6
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The basic formula for expectation damages is:
Loss in value + other loss – cost avoided – loss avoided
Other loss: Incidental & Consequential damages
Incidental: Includes additional costs incurred after the breach in a reasonable attempt to avoid loss
Consequential: Losses beyond general damages that the plaintiff would never have incurred but for the breach.
Speculationslide 7
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Expectation damages must be reasonably ascertainable.
The plaintiff has the burden to prove damages with reasonable certainty. However, damages will not be awarded if they are mere speculation, conjecture, or surmise.
Foreseeabilityslide 8
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) Contracts § 351.
(1) Damages are not recoverable for loss that the party in breach did not have reason to foresee as a probable result of the breach when the contract was made.
(2) Loss may be foreseeable as a probable result of a breach because it follows from the breach
(a) in the ordinary course of events, or
(b) as a result of special circumstances, beyond the ordinary course of events, that the party in breach had reason to know.
(3) A court may limit damages for foreseeable loss by excluding recovery for loss of profits, by allowing recovery only for loss incurred in reliance, or otherwise if it concludes that in the circumstances justice so requires in order to avoid disproportionate compensation.
Hadley v. Baxendaleslide 9
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts
Plaintiffs operate a mill. The mill was stopped when the crank shaft was broken.
Plaintiffs contract to have defendant deliver the shaft to have it repaired. Plaintiffs say the shaft must be delivered immediately.
Defendant breached the contract by delaying delivery for several days
Plaintiffs’ mill was shut down during the period of delay
Hadley v. Baxendaleslide 10
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule: Expectation damage must be reasonably foreseeable: they include those arising from special circumstances (not normally part of such a contract) only if such special circumstances were known by both parties or communicated to breaching party.
Application:
A late delivery does not normally cause lost profits from the mill being shut down.
Plaintiff did not tell defendant that the mill would be shut down if delivery was late.
So what could the plaintiffs have done to ensure full damages?
Communicate the potential damages to the defendant.
Hadley v. Baxendaleslide 11
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rationale:
When a party doesn’t know the stakes, it can’t strike a good bargain. Defendants may have charged more for the delivery if they had known about the possible damages.
Duty to Mitigateslide 12
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A plaintiff cannot hold a defendant liable for damages which need not have been incurred.
The plaintiff must mitigate damages caused by the defendant’s wrongful act.
In essence, the loss in value element will be decreased for any mitigation that the defendant should have but did not undertake.
Rockingham County v. Luten Bridge Co.slide 13
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Luten Bridge enters into a contract to build a bridge for Rockingham County
After construction began, the County repudiated the contract and told Luten to stop construction
Luten continued and finished the bridge.
Luten is suing for damages from the County’s repudiation
Rockingham County v. Luten Bridge Co.slide 14
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule:
A plaintiff cannot hold a defendant liable for damages which need not have been incurred.
The plaintiff must mitigate damages caused by the defendant’s wrongful act.
In essence, the loss in value element will be decreased for any mitigation that the defendant should have but did not undertake.
Application:
Luten cannot recover damages for any work performed on the K following the county’s repudiation
Rockingham County v. Luten Bridge Co.slide 15
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rationale:
Efficiency
Performing after the other party has repudiated (or otherwise breached) may be wasteful
Luten built a bridge “in the midst of the forest,” unconnected to any road
Fairness
Luten Bridge had to understand that the County had repudiated the contract. The non-breaching party is thus put in a difficult position.
Luten should have demanded adequate assurances!
Parker v. Twentieth Century-Fox Film Corp.slide 16
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts
Twentieth Century Fox contracted with Parker to star in “Bloomer Girl.”
Later, TCF breached but offered replacement contract to star in “Big Country.”
Bloomer Girl was relevantly different from Big Country: (Musical vs. dramatic western, LA vs. Australia).
MacLaine refused the contract.
Parker v. Twentieth Century-Fox Film Corp.slide 17
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue Should her damages be reduced by the amount she would have made in “Big Country”? In other words, did she fail to mitigate?
Rule: An employee’s failure to accept inferior or different (not substantially similar) employment is not a failure to mitigate
Meaning, employer must show (1) substantially similar work (2) employee failed to apply
Application: The work was not substantially similar, so her damages will not be reduced for any failure to mitigate
Not substantially similar because it was a different type of film with different implications for her career
Filming was in Australia instead of California
Loss in value – failure to mitigate + other loss – cost and loss avoided
Expectation Damages Formulaslide 18
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Loss in value + other loss – cost and loss avoided
How would you add the rules from Hadley, Florafax, and Luten Bridge into the formula?
Loss in value – failure to mitigate + other loss that is foreseeable and reasonably ascertainable – cost and loss avoided
Lost Volume Sellersslide 19
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule:
A replacement contract will not be subtracted from damages if the nonbreaching party is a lost volume seller
Lost volume seller = A seller who lost volume as a result of the breach. Basically, they could have entered into both the original contract and the replacement contract.
The replacement contract is an “additional” contract and NOT a “mitigating contract”
The money earned on the “additional” contract is thus not subtracted out of damages
Loss in value – mitigation + other loss – cost and loss avoided
Jetz Service Co. v. Salina Propertiesslide 20
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Jetz supplies machines for laundry services in over 2,000 locations. Jetz has an inventory of 1,500 washers and dryers that are always available.
Salina had a contract with Jetz for Jetz to supply 10 machines for a laundry at Salina’s apartment building for six years.
16 months before the end of the contract term, Salina breaches the contract and installed its own laundry equipment
Jetz recovered the machines and eventually re-leased them in another location
Jetz Service Co. v. Salina Propertiesslide 21
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Jetz re-leased the machines during the term of the breached contract.
But, the court finds that Jetz was a “lost volume seller.”
The money Jetz earned re-leasing the equipment thus will not be deducted from damages. It was an “additional” contract rather than a “mitigating” contract. Jetz will thus get the profits it lost from the breach
Hypothetical 1slide 22
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Jeff Schmitt sells Chevrolet cars in Dayton, Ohio. Assume that Jeff can get as many cars from Chevrolet as he can sell. Jeff enters into a contract to sell a new Malibu on his lot to Alex for $23,000. Jeff gets the cars from Chevy for $20,000. However, Alex breaches the contract. Jeff sells the same car to Christine a week later for $22,000. What are Jeff’s damages?
$0
$1,000
$3,000
$23,000
Loss in value – mitigation + other loss – cost and loss avoided

Limitations on Expectation Damagesslide 28
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Attorneys’ Fees
Unless otherwise required by statute, court rule, or the terms of the contract, each party pays for their own attorney fees.
Limitations on Expectation Damagesslide 29
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Punitive Damages:
Rule: No punitive damages for breach of contract, even intentional or bad faith breach
Exception: breach of duty of good faith and fair dealing in Insurance context. The whole purpose of insurance is defeated if an insurance company can refuse or fail, without justification, to pay a valid claim.
Limitations on Expectation Damagesslide 30
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rationale:
Signing a contract merely gives a party the option to perform or pay damages. No showing of wrongdoing is required to prove breach.
“The duty to keep a contract at common law means a prediction that you must pay damages if you do not keep it -- and nothing else.” Justice Holmes
The law wants to encourage efficient breach
“Contract damages are . . . not designed to ‘prevent breach’ but merely to compensate for any injury that results.” Goetz & Scott
Limitations on Expectation Damagesslide 31
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Emotional Distress
Rule: Emotional distress damages are generally only available with physical harm or when serious emotional disturbance was a likely result (Rst. 2d. 353)
Rationale: Again, breach is not necessarily culpable, we want to encourage efficient breach, and tort damages can be unpredictable, making it hard to have stable commercial expectations
Erlich v. Menezesslide 32
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts:
Plaintiffs hired the Defendant to build their dream house.
Defendant negligently builds the house. The roof leaks, the walls crack, and extensive repairs are needed. Plaintiffs are extremely upset, worried that the house could collapse, and bothered by the constant problems and repairs.
Erlich v. Menezesslide 33
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether a negligent breach of a home-building K will support an award for damages for emotional distress
Rule: In contract, emotional distress damages are only available with physical harm or when serious emotional disturbance was a likely result (Rst. 2d. 353). Otherwise, to get tort damages must show accompanying tort
Even if “tortious activity” is at issue, need something other than “economic injury” to get emotional distress damages—typically need physical injury, malice, or insurance K
Erlich v. Menezesslide 34
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
The Plaintiffs were not physically injured.
Serious emotional disturbance was not likely. Purpose of the K was not emotional well-being; distress flowed from an economic concern. “only economic injury.”
But why no tort damages, given Menezes’ negligence?
Breach of contract is tortious only when it violates a duty independent of the contract.
Erlich v. Menezesslide 35
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rationale:
Again, breach is not necessarily culpable, we want to encourage efficient breach, and tort damages can be unpredictable, making it hard to have stable commercial expectations
Court in Erlich is concerned that awarding emotional distress damages would make construction Ks difficult to predict, making such Ks more expensive
2
Reliance & Restitution Damages
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Reliance Damages가 뭐냐면... 기대이익(Expectation)을 증명하기 어려울 때 대안이야. "계약 믿고 내가 쓴 비용"을 돌려받는 거야 — 계약 전 상태(status quo ante)로 복귀. Restatement § 349: 이행이 있었다면 얻었을 이익을 반영하여 손해를 줄여야 해. 즉, 계약 자체가 손해 보는 계약이었다면 Reliance Damages도 그만큼 줄어. Restitution Damages가 뭐냐면... "내가 상대방에게 이미 준 이익"을 되찾는 거야. 계약이 파기됐을 때 내가 이미 납부한 돈이나 제공한 서비스 가치를 돌려받아. 세 가지 손해배상 비교: - Expectation: 계약대로 됐다면 내가 있었을 위치 (미래 이익) - Reliance: 계약 전 내가 있었던 위치 (과거 비용 회수) - Restitution: 상대방이 부당하게 가져간 것 (공평 회수)
예시 — 건물주가 임차인에게 "3년 임대"라고 약속해서 임차인이 건물 인테리어 공사에 $50,000 썼어. 근데 3개월 후 계약 파기됐어. Expectation(3년 임대 이익) 증명이 어려울 수 있어. 그럼 $50,000 Reliance Damages 청구 가능. 만약 임차인이 첫 달 임료 $2,000을 냈으면 그 $2,000은 Restitution으로도 청구 가능.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Other Common Law Damagesslide 36
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Reliance Damages
Measure = reliance interest – loss
Used when expectation damages or speculative or liability is based on promissory estoppel
Restitution Damages
Measure = value of the benefit conferred
Used when breaching party brings suit; plaintiff was losing money on K; or liability is based on restitution
Specific Performance
Injunction ordering performance
Used when damages are inadequate
Not used for personal services
Liquidated Damages
Used when not a penalty
Breach of contract actionslide 37
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Promissory estoppel action
Breach of contract action
Reliance Damages: Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 349slide 38
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
As an alternative to the measure of damages stated in § 347, the injured party has a right to damages based on reliance interest, including expenditures made in preparation for performance or in performance, less any loss that the party in breach can prove with any reasonable certainty the injured party would have suffered had the contract been performed.
Reliance Damagesslide 39
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Reliance damages formula: money spent in reliance – loss under the contract
Reliance Damagesslide 40
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The following rules that normally apply to limit expectation damages also apply to reliance damages:
Foreseeability: Reliance expenses are not recoverable unless the breaching party had reason to know that the loss would occur as a consequence of a breach
Mitigation: Reliance expenses are recoverable by the plaintiff only if they were wasted and if the loss could not have been avoided. If the loss or waste of expense can be avoided (by repurposing the investment or selling for salvage value), then plaintiff cannot recover those expenses.
Certainty: Reliance expenses are only recoverable if they can be proven with reasonable certainty.
Reliance Damagesslide 41
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
If you have a breach in contract claim you can choose to use the reliance interest as the measure of damages.
Why is this, in general, a bad idea?
Because the reliance damages are going to be (roughly) your cost of performance. So you just recoup that amount. But your expectation damages are going to be (roughly) your profit. Since to get you your profit we need to get you your cost of performance reliance damages generally are less than expectation damages.
Reliance Damagesslide 42
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Reliance damages are generally used:
If you have a breach of contract and the expectation damages cannot be easily calculated (perhaps they are too speculative).
If you have a promise without an exchange (so no contract formed) and the other party relied on that promise (you meet the elements of promissory estoppel).
Reliance Damagesslide 43
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Contract price: $5,000
Down payment: $1,000
Costs expended: $2,000
Cost to complete: $1,000
Expected profit: $2,000
What are expectation and reliance damages?
Which would you choose as the plaintiff?
Assume there is a contract to renovate a home. What are builder’s damages if the homeowner breaches part way through performance?

Expected profit: $2,000
What are expectation and reliance damages?
Which would you choose as the plaintiff?
Assume there is a contract to renovate a home. What are builder’s damages if the homeowner breaches part way through performance?

Wartzman v. Hightower Productions Inc.slide 50
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Hightower was a promotional venture. It was created to employ a person to break the world-record for flagpole sitting and descend on New Year’s Eve in New York as a promotional event. Hightower planned to have the individual then appear throughout the country.
The founders of Hightower hired Wartzman, an attorney, to incorporate Hightower so that stock could be sold to raise revenue.
Hightower raised money by selling stock, hired “Woody Hightower,” hired other employees, and incurred other expenses equaling about $155,000
Wartzman then told Hightower that no further stock could be issued because of a problem in the manner of incorporation
Hightower discontinued the project.
The jury awarded damages to Hightower of $170,508
Wartzman v. Hightower Productions Inc.slide 51
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: whether reliance damages were properly awarded
Rules:
Expectation damages are not recoverable when profits are too speculative
Reliance damages = monies spent in part performance, in preparation for or in reliance on the contract
Reliance damages will be reduced if the breaching party can prove a loss
Wartzman v. Hightower Productions, Inc.slide 52
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Expectation damages cannot be recovered because lost profits are too speculative
Reliance – investments in the business, liabilities of the business to others, salaries, etc.
Reliance damages are not reduced by the court because Wartzman’s argument that the project would have resulted in a loss is speculative
Wartzman v. Hightower Productions, Inc.slide 53
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The court says that Wartzman was “unable to establish that the stunt was doomed to fail.” What if Wartzman had such proof?
Such losses would need to be subtracted from Hightower’s reliance interest, making damages zero.
Walser v. Toyotaslide 54
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Walser applies to run a Lexus dealership
Toyota officials tell Walser informally that he will get the dealership
Walser buys property for the dealership
Toyota decides not to give the dealership to Walser
Walser sues Toyota, seeking $7,600,000 in damages, including lost profits.
Jury finds for Walser on a promissory estoppel claim and awards $232,131 in damages. Judge had instructed jury to limit damages to out-of-pocket expenses
Walser v. Toyotaslide 55
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether the district court erred by limiting Walser’s damages to out of pocket expenses
Rule: In a PE action, the trial court has the equitable discretion to limit damages to reliance damages if justice so requires
Application: Here, reliance damages were not a clear error in judgment because the dealership was “far from certain” and plaintiffs lost no other opportunities as a result
Note: Many courts strictly limit PE damages to reliance!
Hypotheticalslide 56
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Joe enters into a contract with Leasing Co. to lease a commercial property to start up a new restaurant. Joe spends $30,000 on equipment and $20,000 marketing his new restaurant before moving into the space. Days before he is due to move in, however, Leasing Co. breaches its contract with Joe and tells him it has leased the unit to another company. Joe then sells his recently purchased equipment for $25,000. Joe sues Leasing Co. for breach of contract. During trial, Joe presents evidence showing that he would have made a $50,000 profit, and Leasing Co. presents evidence showing that he would have lost $20,000. Assuming that the court finds that parties’ projections regarding profit and loss were speculative, Joe’s damages will equal:
$0, because Joe’s profits are speculative
$25,000, because Joe spent $50,000 in reliance on the contract and mitigated his damages by selling his equipment for $25,000
$50,000, because Joe spent $50,000 in reliance on the contract
$80,000 because Joe would have made a net profit of $30,000 and he spent $50,000 in reliance on the contract
Hypotheticalslide 57
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Joe enters into a contract with Leasing Co. to lease a commercial property to start up a new restaurant. Joe spends $30,000 on equipment and $20,000 marketing his new restaurant before moving into the space. Days before he is due to move in, however, Leasing Co. breaches its contract with Joe and tells him it has leased the unit to another company. Joe then sells his recently purchased equipment for $25,000. Joe sues Leasing Co. for breach of contract. During trial, Joe presents evidence showing that he would have made a $50,000 profit, and Leasing Co. presents evidence showing that he would have lost $20,000. Assuming that the court finds that parties’ projections regarding profit and loss were speculative, Joe’s damages will equal:
$0, because Joe’s profits are speculative
$25,000, because Joe spent $50,000 in reliance on the contract and mitigated his damages by selling his equipment for $25,000
$50,000, because Joe spent $50,000 in reliance on the contract
$80,000 because Joe would have made a net profit of $30,000 and he spent $50,000 in reliance on the contract
Breach of contract actionslide 58
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Promissory estoppel action
Restitution & unjust enrichment action
Breach of contract action
Breach of contract action
Restitution Damagesslide 59
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
When do you use restitution damages?
If the other party breached the contract, and, for some reason, the non-breaching party cannot recover its lost expectations.
If you are the breaching party, then you may seek some recovery for the value of your part performance.
If there was no contract, but one of the parties has nonetheless conferred a benefit on the other (liability in restitution).
Restitution Damagesslide 60
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
When you use restitution as the basis for your damages, you often ask the court to rescind the contract (for rescission) and for restitution.
Restitution Damagesslide 61
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The measure of damages in restitution is usually the value of the benefit conferred in the hands of the defendant.
But how do you measure that value?
If benefit is cash, get the cash back.
If benefit was a specific item (a desk Abraham Lincoln once owned), get the item back.
Market Value Restitution (majority rules)
How much it would have cost the defendant to acquire the benefit from someone else.
How much the benefit has increased the value of the defendant’s property.
Technical terms:
Quantum meruit: value of services rendered.
Quantum valebant: value of property delivered to another.
Coastal Steel Erectors v. Algernon Blairslide 62
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Blair is a general contractor
Coastal Steel is a subcontractor
Coastal Steel contracts to perform steel work for Blair
After Coastal completes 28% of the work, Blair totally breaches the contract
Amount due to Coastal under the contract was $37,000
If Coastal had fully performed, it would have lost $37,000 on the contract
Coastal brings suit
Coastal Steel Erectors v. Algernon Blairslide 63
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether expectation or restitution damages are the proper measure of recovery
What would expectation damages be in this case?
Amount due to Coastal under the K was $37,000, but Coastal would have lost $37,000.
Expectation damages = $0!
Coastal Steel Erectors v. Algernon Blairslide 64
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
So does the court award damages of $0?
No, because Coastal is entitled to restitution damages in quantum meruit
Why is this the case? Why is there liability under a theory of restitution?
Coastal provided Blair with a benefit, Blair retained the benefit w/o fully paying, and it would be inequitable to allow Blair to keep the benefit w/o paying
Coastal Steel Erectors v. Algernon Blairslide 65
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
How does the court measure restitution damages in this case?
The value of the services provided, irrespective of whether plaintiff would have lost money on the contract
This is the majority rule, though it is not universally accepted
How is the value of the services measured?
The amount for which such services could have been purchased by the defendant; while the K price is some evidence, it is not dispositive
Hypotheticalslide 66
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What if Coastal had fully performed its work under the K, and Blair breached by refusing to pay. Could Coastal elect restitution damages, claiming that his services were more valuable than the K price?
No, if the injured party has substantially or fully performed and the only performance remaining from the non-injured party is payment of a fixed amount of money, restitution is not applicable.
Lancellotti v. Thomasslide 67
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Contract to buy the name and operate a restaurant for $25,000.
Seller will still own the real estate; promises to build an addition
Buyer agrees to lease the real estate and operate the business for 5 years
Buyer pays the $25,000; Seller builds the addition
Less than 1 year later, Buyer stops paying rent and stops operating the business
Buyer files a lawsuit, demanding the $25,000 back
Lancellotti v. Thomasslide 68
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether a breaching party can recover restitution damages
Rule: Under the old common law rule, a breaching party could not recover damages
Under the modern rule, “the party who committed the breach should be entitled to recover any benefit in excess of the loss that he has caused by his own breach”
Application: The trial court must determine if the $25,000 benefit conferred on the seller exceeded the seller’s losses from breach
Hypotheticalslide 69
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
In Coastal Steel, what if Coastal had breached the contract after performing 28% of the work? Would it still have been entitled to restitution damages?
Yes. The breaching party may recover any benefit conferred in excess of the loss caused by breach. (See Restatement §357, Lancellottii). Blair hired a replacement subcontractor, so likely suffered minimal loss from the breach.
However, under the Restatement, a breaching party’s damages will be limited to a ratable portion of the total K price
Since Coastal did 28% of the work, they get 28% of the contract price
Ventura v. Titan Sportsslide 70
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts
Ventura works as a commentator for Titan
The dispute is about whether Titan must pay Ventura for using this commentary on videos
Ventura first works under an oral contract that does not include a term about videos
Ventura then signs a written contract that specifically disclaims any royalties for videos
Ventura v. Titan Sportsslide 71
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
This case involves two distinct issues.
Whether restitution damages should be awarded
If so, the appropriate measure of restitution damages
Ventura v. Titan Sportsslide 72
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #1: Liability: why should restitution be awarded?
Titan unjustly enriched by getting this benefit under the oral contract
Because the K didn’t cover using his performances in videos, such use violated Ventura’s right to publicity under state law
Titan was unjustly enriched by getting this benefit during the written contract
The written contract was obtained through fraud, and thus the court rescinds the K and awards restitution
Ventura v. Titan Sportsslide 73
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #2: The measure of damages
What is the benefit conferred on Titan?
The amount by which Ventura increased the value of Titan’s videos. This is measured by a prediction of royalty rates.
Note that, unlike in Coastal, we are not asking what it would have cost Titan to hire someone else to do Ventura’s job. The court may use either measure as justice requires.
3
Specific Performance & Liquidated Damages
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Specific Performance가 뭐냐면... 돈 말고 "그냥 약속한 거 해"라고 법원이 명령하는 거야. 법원이 이걸 발동하는 건 드물어 — 돈으로 대체가 불가능한(unique, irreplaceable) 경우에만. 언제 가능하냐: ① 부동산: 모든 토지는 Unique하다고 봐 → SP 원칙적 가능 ② 희귀/고유 물건: 명화, 골동품 등 ③ UCC: 물건이 Unique하거나 다른 구제수단으로 불충분할 때 Injunction: "하지 마"라고 법원이 금지 명령. 가수가 전속 계약 위반하고 다른 회사에서 활동하는 거 막을 때 씀. Liquidated Damages가 뭐냐면... 계약서에 미리 "위반하면 $X 내"라고 적어두는 거야. 유효하려면 두 가지 조건: ① 계약 시점에 실제 손해를 예측하기 어려웠을 것 ② 사전에 정한 금액이 예상 손해에 합리적으로 부합할 것 (Penalty가 아닌 것)
예시 — 콘서트 취소 계약금 $10,000: 공연 수익이 불확실하고 예상 손해를 미리 계산하기 어렵다면 → 합리적 Liquidated Damages. 반면, 만 원짜리 물건 계약서에 "위반하면 $1,000,000"이라고 적으면 → 터무니없어서 Penalty로 무효.
소유권 반환(Rescission): 계약 자체를 없었던 걸로 하는 거야. 착오, 사기, 강박, 능력 부족 등이 있을 때.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Specific Performanceslide 74
📝 한글
Specific Performanceslide 75
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What do we mean by “specific performance”?
An order of specific performance is intended to produce as nearly as is practicable the same effect that the performance due under a contract would have produced.
It usually, therefore, orders a party to render the performance that he promised.
Injunctionslide 76
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What is an “injunction”?
A court order by which an individual is required to perform, or is restrained from performing, a particular act.
An injunction is an equitable remedy.
It commands action or prohibits action to promote justice, etc.
Early common law courts generally did not use specific relief.slide 77
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The typical judgment at common law declared that the plaintiff recover from the defendant a sum of money.
Creating a new obligation requiring no cooperation on defendant’s part.
If defendant failed to pay, a writ of execution was issued and the sheriff could seize defendant’s property.
The enforcement of promises in equity developed along different lines.slide 78
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Decrees in equity came to take the form of a personal command to the defendant to do or not to do something.
His cooperation was assumed, and if he disobeyed he could be punished not only for criminal contempt, at the instance of the court, but also for civil contempt, at the instance of the plaintiff.
So it was said that equity acted in personam.
And law acted in rem.
Restatement 2d Contracts § 359(1)slide 79
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Specific performance or an injunction will only be ordered if damages would be inadequate to protect the expectation interest of the injured party.
Restatement 2d Contracts § 359(1)slide 80
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
In determining whether the remedy in damages would be adequate, the following circumstances are significant:
(a) the difficulty of proving damages with reasonable certainty,
(b) the difficulty of procuring a suitable substitute performance by means of money awarded as damages, and
(c) the likelihood that an award of damages could not be collected.
Sale of Landslide 81
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Specific performance is always available for a contract for the sale of land. As a matter of law, each parcel of land is deemed to be unique.

Restatement 2d Contracts § 367(1)slide 90
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A promise to render personal service will not be specifically enforced
Comment 1: “The refusal is based in part upon the undesirability of compelling the continuance of personal association after disputes have arisen and confidence and loyalty are gone and, in some instances, of imposing what might seem like involuntary servitude. . . . The refusal is also based upon the difficulty of enforcement inherent in passing judgment on the quality of performance.”
Restatement 2d Contracts § 367(1): Comment 2slide 91
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What is a contract for “personal services”?
“A performance is not a personal service . . . unless it is personal in the sense of being non-delegable.”
“However, not every non-delegable performance is properly described as a service. . . . In determining what is a personal service, the policies reflected in the more general rules on the effect of public policy and of the difficulty of enforcement are relevant. The importance of trust and confidence in the relation between the parties, the difficulty of judging the quality of the performance rendered and the length of time required for performance are significant factors.”
“Among the parties that have been held to render what are personal services within the rule stated in Subsection (1) are actors, singers and athletes, and the rule applies generally to contracts of employment that create the intimate relation traditionally known as master and servant.”
Non-Compete Agreementsslide 92
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Injunctions to enforce non-competition agreements will only be issued when damages are inadequate.
Damages are likely to be adequate to protect the employer's interest unless the employee's services are unique or extraordinary, either because of special skill that he possesses or because of special knowledge that he has acquired of the employer's business (Restatement 2d Contracts § 367, comment c)
The restrictions must also be reasonable in scope
Reier Broadcasting Co. v. Kramerslide 93
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Kramer is the head football coach at Montana State University (“MSU”)
Reier and Kramer have a contract giving Reier exclusive broadcast rights with Kramer until 2004
Reier had exclusive broadcast rights with MSU until 2002
In 2002, MSU enters into a contract with Clear Channel, giving it exclusive broadcast rights
MSU tells Kramer to broadcast with Clear Channel
Reier files this suit, seeking an injunction prohibiting Kramer from brodcasting with Clear Channel
Reier Broadcasting Co. v. Kramerslide 94
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether the contractual agreement not to perform personal services for a competitor could be enforced through specific performance?
Reier Broadcasting Co. v. Kramerslide 95
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule: A promise to render personal services will not be specifically enforced
Application
The court will not issue an injunction enforcing the non-competition provision
Kramer’s services are unique, and therefore damage would be inadequate
However, enforcing the non-compete would amount to indirect enforcement of the personal services contract
Liquidated Damagesslide 96
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Liquidated damages = Stipulated damages that are a specified sum (monetary compensation)
Rule: A liquidated damages provision will not be enforced if it is deemed to be a penalty provision. Courts consider two factors:
The reasonableness of the amount
The difficulty in proving loss
Sliding scale:
“If the difficulty of proof of loss is great, considerable latitude is allowed in the approximation of anticipated or actual harm. If, on the other hand, the difficulty of proof of loss is slight, less latitude is allowed in that approximation.”
Restatement 2d Contracts § 356, Comment 2
Liquidated Damagesslide 97
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Why not allow the parties to agree to a penalty?
“The central objective behind the system of contract remedies is compensatory, not punitive. Punishment of a promisor for having broken his promise has no justification on either economic or other grounds and a term providing such a penalty is unenforceable on grounds of public policy.”
Restatement 2d Contracts § 356, Comment 1
Barrie School v. Patchslide 98
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Patches enter into a contract to send their child to Barrie School
The contract states that if the Patches withdrew their child after a certain date, they would pay full tuition for the entire year as liquidated damages
The Patches withdrew their child after the specified date, but refuse to pay tuition
Barrie School files suit for breach of contract
Barrie School made no attempt to enroll a replacement student; in fact, enrollment exceeded expectations
Barrie School v. Patchslide 99
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether the liquated damages provision is enforceable
Rules:
The party seeking to have the court set aside the award must prove that the amount is a penalty, based on the reasonableness of the amount and the difficulty in proving loss
The party seeking to set aside the liquidated damages provision has the burden of proof
In trying to decide whether a liquidated damages provision is a penalty, you have to to ascertain whether it is a reasonable estimate at the time of contracting. You don’t look at post-formation information
Barrie School v. Patchslide 100
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Patches argue the amount is excessive because the school did not suffer any actual damages
Court holds that the liquidated amount is enforceable because:
The amount was not grossly excessive at the time of formation, and
Damages for losing a student would have been difficult to predict at the time the K was signed
Barrie School v. Patchslide 101
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The Patches argued that damages should be reduced because Barrie School did not attempt to find a replacement student. Barrie School did not mitigate its damages.
Court rejects this argument. It holds that once a court determines that a liquidated damages provision is valid, it need make no further inquiry into actual damages. The mitigation principle is used to determine actual damages. Actual ex post damages are irrelevant if the court is applying the parties’ ex ante damages prediction. Reducing the liquated amount would violate the parties’ agreement and expectations.
Hypotheticalslide 102
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Recall the facts of Hightower. Assume that Hightower had a liquidated damages provision in its contract with Wartzman setting damages at $200,000. Would this be enforceable?
What if it set damages at $1,000,000?
What if it set damages at $2,000,000?
Rule: A liquidated damages provision will not be enforced if it is deemed to be a penalty provision. Courts consider two factors:
The reasonableness of the amount
The difficulty in proving loss
UDSL 슬라이드 원문 — Class 7 — Defenses
1
Unconscionability, Undue Influence & Infancy
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Unconscionability가 뭐냐면... 계약이 너무 불공평해서 양심에 반할 때 법원이 집행을 거부해. 단, 두 가지가 모두 있어야 해 — Procedural(과정 불공정) + Substantive(내용 불공정). Procedural Unconscionability (과정): 협상력 차이(bargaining power), 세밀한 글씨 숨김, 이해하기 어려운 언어, 선택 여지 없음(take-it-or-leave-it). "알아도 못 피했어." Substantive Unconscionability (내용): 조건 자체가 충격적으로 일방적이야. 시장 가격의 3~4배, 완전히 일방적인 면책 조항 등. UCC § 2-302: 법원이 Unconscionable 조항을 거부, 수정, 혹은 일부만 집행할 수 있어.
판례 — In re Checking Account Overdraft: 은행이 고객 계좌에서 큰 금액을 먼저 처리해서 초과인출 수수료를 최대화했어. 고객에겐 불리한 방향으로. 법원: 약관(fine print) + 선택권 없음(모든 은행이 비슷함) + 극도로 불리한 결과 → Unconscionable. 은행의 처리 순서 변경 관행을 집행 거부.
Infancy (미성년자): 18세 미만이 맺은 계약은 Voidable — 미성년자가 파기(disaffirm) 선택 가능. 단, 성인 되고 나서 계속 이행하면 Ratification(추인). 생필품(necessaries)은 예외.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Defenses to Contract Enforcementslide 1
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문

Unconscionabilityslide 2
📝 한글
Rule: Most courts require a showing of both procedural unconscionability and substantive unconscionabilityslide 3
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Procedural = lack of meaningful choice in the contract provision
Term is hidden (often in small print), or lack of bargaining power (form contract)
Substantive = unfair, harsh, or oppressive term
Term benefits only one party in an unfair way
Unconscionability
U.C.C. § 2-302.slide 4
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Unconscionable Actions Court May Take
If term/contract was unconscionable at time of contracting
Court may refuse to enforce K in its entirety
Court may enforce K without unconscionable clause
Court may limit application of unconscionable clause to avoid unconscionable result
In re Checking Account Overdraft Litigationslide 5
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Facts:
Plaintiffs bring a class action lawsuit against a number of banks. They allege the bank’s practice of ordering checking withdraws is unconscionable.
Buried in the fine print of each contract customers have with the bank is a provision that says that, when a customer has multiple withdraws within one day, the bank will order them from largest to smallest.
This provision has the effect of maximizing overdraft fees.
In re Checking Account Overdraft Litigationslide 6
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Example:
Customer has $100 in her checking account
She has 3 withdraws in one day: $15, $15, $90
If left in that order, she is charged one overdraft fee
If reordered from largest to smallest, as the contract requires, she is charged 2 overdraft fees
In re Checking Account Overdraft Litigationslide 7
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Held: Provision is unconscionable
It is procedurally unconscionable because of the disparity in sophistication and bargaining power; terms were contained in voluminous boilerplate language drafted by the banks; no ability to negotiate; no notification re opt-out
It is substantively unconscionable because the only reason for re-ordering is to maximize fees; fees bear no relation to cost to bank
Hypothetical 1slide 8
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith owns an electronics store. He provides financing for his goods for customers that cannot afford them. In exchange for such financing, Smith charges prices that are 20% higher than the market price and includes a term in the contract allowing him to repossess all goods purchased from his store if any payment is made late. In fact, Smith will have the right to repossess all goods ever purchased from Smith if a payment on any one good is late. However, Smith sits down with all of his customers and explains these terms and that this is the only way he can sell his goods to people who could not otherwise afford them. Jones purchases 5 goods from Smith over 5 years. He then misses one payment on one good, and Smith repossesses all 5 goods. Does Joe have a valid defense in unconscionability?
Yes, because the terms the terms are substantively and procedurally unconscionable
Yes, because the terms are complex and confusing
No, because the terms are substantively fair
No, because although the terms may be substantively unconscionable, there is no procedural unconscionability

Undue Influenceslide 12
📝 한글
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 177. Undue Influenceslide 13
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Undue influence is unfair persuasion of a party:
who is under the domination of the person exercising the persuasion; or
who by virtue of the relation between them is justified in assuming that that person will not act in a manner inconsistent with his welfare.
Comment a: Relations that often fall within the rule include those of parent and child, husband and wife, clergyman and parishioner, and physician and patient. In each case it is a question of fact whether the relation is such as to give undue weight to the other's attempts at persuasion. The required relation may be found in situations other than those enumerated. However, the mere fact that a party is weak, infirm or aged does not of itself suffice, although it may be a factor in determining whether the required relation existed
Undue Influence
Undue Influenceslide 14
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 177, Cmt. b
The ultimate question is whether the result was produced by means that seriously impaired the free and competent exercise of judgment. Such factors as the unfairness of the resulting bargain, the unavailability of independent advice, and the susceptibility of the person persuaded are circumstances to be taken into account in determining whether there was unfair persuasion, but they are not in themselves controlling.
Hypothetical 1slide 15
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith is not experienced in business and has, for years, been accustomed to rely in business matters on the advice of his friend Jones who is experienced in business. Jones constantly urges Smith to make a contract to sell to McIntyre, (Jones’s friend), a tract of land at a price that is well below its fair value. One day, Jones tells Smith that he must agree to sell now, or McIntyre will buy a different tract of land. Smith is thereby induced to make the contract.
Can Smith avoid this contract as arising out of undue influence?
Yes
No
Undue Influence
Hypothetical 1slide 16
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith is not experienced in business and has, for years, been accustomed to rely in business matters on the advice of his friend Jones who is experienced in business. Jones constantly urges Smith to make a contract to sell to McIntyre, (Jones’s friend), a tract of land at a price that is well below its fair value. One day, Jones tells Smith that he must agree to sell now, or McIntyre will buy a different tract of land. Smith is thereby induced to make the contract.
Can Smith avoid this contract as arising out of undue influence?
Yes, because Jones used unfair persuasion and Smith is justified in assuming that Jones will not act in a manner inconsistent with his welfare.
Undue Influence

Smith, an elderly and illiterate man, lives with and depends for his support on Jones, his nephew. Jones asks Smith if he would be willing to sell him a tract of land. Smith offers to sell the land to Jones for $10,000, the price he paid for it 20 years ago. The land is now worth close to $100,000. Jones accepts.
Can Smith avoid this contract as arising out of undue influence?

Hypothetical 2slide 18
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith, an elderly and illiterate man, lives with and depends for his support on Jones, his nephew. Jones asks Smith if he would be willing to sell him a tract of land. Smith offers to sell the land to Jones for $10,000, the price he paid for it 20 years ago. The land is now worth close to $100,000. Jones accepts.
Can Smith avoid this contract as arising out of undue influence?
No. Jones has exerted no “excessive pressure” or “unfair persuasion.” The fact of old age or infirmity is not sufficient.
Undue Influence

Hypothetical 3slide 20
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith, an elderly and illiterate man, lives with and depends for his support on Jones, his nephew. Jones asks Smith to sell him a tract of land for $1,000. This tract of land is worth $100,000. When Smith objects, Jones tells Smith that he will no longer support him if he does not agree. When Smith asks for time to find a replacement caregiver, Jones says he will leave at that instant if Smith does not agree to the sale. Smith is thereby induced to make the proposed contract.
Can Smith avoid this contract as arising out of undue influence?
Yes because Smith is under the domination of Jones.

Infancyslide 21
📝 한글
Infancyslide 22
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Sometimes people who are younger than 18 (“infants”) enter into contracts with adults.
The danger in such circumstances is that the adult takes advantage of the infant.
As a result, the law has devised a protective doctrine call “infancy.”
Traditional Rule:slide 23
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract entered into between an infant and an adult is voidable unless it is a contract for necessities (like food) for the infant.
If the infant voids the contract, then the infant receives all of the consideration the infant gave to the adult regardless of the condition of what was given to the infant. The infant must then give back whatever consideration he/she received.
Infancy
Facts:slide 24
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Dobson, 16 yo, bought used pickup truck for $4,900.
Pickup developed mechanical problems (likely a burnt valve) 9 months later.
One month later engine “blew up” making the truck inoperable.
Shraders refused to accept tender of the truck or give a refund.
Dobson parked the car in his parent’s front yard where it was subsequently hit, damaging the left front fender.
Dobson v. Shrader
Dobson v. Shraderslide 25
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue:
Whether a minor is entitled to a full refund of the price paid under a contract for a pickup truck?
Traditional Rule:slide 26
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract entered into between an infant and an adult is voidable unless it is a contract for necessities (like food) for the infant.
If the infant voids the contract, then the infant receives all of the consideration the infant gave to the adult regardless of the condition of what was given to the infant. The infant must then give back whatever consideration he/she received.
Application
Dobson gets back $4,900 (the full purchase price), and he must give back the truck (in its broken condition)
Dobson v. Shrader
Infancyslide 27
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
As the Dobson case shows, a contract between an adult and an infant is binding on the adult!
The minor can choose to affirm the contract when reaching the age of majority
Careful! The minor may implicitly affirm the contract through his conduct after reaching the age of majority
Example: If Dobson had continued to pay for the truck for a reasonable period of time after reaching 18 years old, he would implicitly affirm the contract and thus be bound
Incapacity/Insanityslide 28
📝 한글
Incapacityslide 29
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A person incurs only voidable contractual duties by entering into a transaction if he is unable to understand in a reasonable manner the nature and consequences of the transaction.
During a period of competency, or through a legal representative, the person can void or affirm the contract
But, incompetents are liable under restitution for necessities like food or medicine.
Intoxicationslide 30
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
In extreme cases, this defense can apply to intoxicated individuals as well. The person must be so drunk that they do not understand what they are agreeing to, and the other person must have reason to know of the intoxication.
A person can always affirm the contract when lucid
Hypotheticalslide 31
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Smith is a billionaire who suffers from a mental illness and is unable to understand the consequences of her actions. Smith enters into a contract to buy a yacht from Jones for $1 million. Smith thinks that she is merely buying a trip on the yacht. Can Smith rescind the contract?
Yes, because she can use the incompetency defense
Yes, but only if Jones knew that Smith was not able to understand the transaction
No, if the contract was made on fair terms
No, because no contract was formed

2
Duress & Public Policy
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Duress가 뭐냐면... 강압적인 위협으로 계약에 서명하게 만든 거야. 단순히 불리한 협상이 아니라, 선택의 여지가 없는 위협이어야 해. 요건: ① 부당한/불법적인 위협 (Wrongful Threat) ② 그 위협 때문에 동의한 것 ③ 합리적인 다른 대안이 없었을 것 Economic Duress: 물리적 힘이 아닌 경제적 압박도 Duress 될 수 있어. "계약서 바꾸지 않으면 납품 안 해" — 하지만 일반적인 협상 압박은 Duress 아님.
판례 — Totem Marine Tug & Barge: Totem이 Alaska와 계약을 완수했는데 Alyeska가 돈을 안 줬어. Totem은 자금난에 빠졌고, Alyeska는 이 상황을 이용해 훨씬 낮은 금액으로 합의를 압박했어. 법원: Economic Duress 인정 — Totem에겐 합리적 대안이 없었고, Alyeska는 고의로 이 상황을 활용했어.
Public Policy (공공 정책): 법에 위반하거나 공공 정책에 반하는 계약은 Void. 예: 경쟁금지 약정(Non-compete)은 합리적 범위(지역, 기간, 업종)를 넘으면 집행 불가. Exculpatory Clause(면책 조항)도 공공 이익 관련 서비스에서 지나치면 무효.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Duressslide 33
📝 한글
Duressslide 34
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract may be voided on grounds of economic duress if there is:
A wrongful or improper threat,
A lack of reasonable alternatives, and
Actual inducement of the contract by threat.
See Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 175
When is a threat wrongful or improper?slide 35
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 176
(1) A threat is improper if
(a) what is threatened is a crime or a tort, or the threat itself would be a crime or a tort if it resulted in obtaining property,
(b) what is threatened is a criminal prosecution,
(c) what is threatened is the use of civil process and the threat is made in bad faith, or
(d) the threat is a breach of the duty of good faith and fair dealing under a contract with the recipient.
Duress
Duressslide 36
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
When does a party have no reasonably available alternatives? Can’t the party always file a lawsuit for breach?
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 175, Comment b
The alternative may take the form of a legal remedy. . . . This alternative may not, however, be reasonable if the threat involves, for instance, the seizure of property, the use of oppressive tactics, or the possibility of emotional consequences. The standard is a practical one under which account must be taken of the exigencies in which the victim finds himself, and the mere availability of a legal remedy is not controlling if it will not afford effective relief to one in the victim's circumstances.
Totem Marine Tug & Barge, Inc.slide 37
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Totem has a contract to transport materials by ship for Alyeska
Problems arose making shipping more expensive
Totem submitted invoices of about $300,000
Totem was in urgent need of the money; without the money, it would go bankrupt
Alyeka offered to settle the claim for $97,500, and Totem accepted
Totem filed this suit to rescind the settlement contract and recover under the original contract
Totem Marine Tug & Barge, Inc.slide 38
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: whether Totem can avoid the binding release agreement on grounds of economic duress
Rule:
A contract may be avoided on grounds of economic duress if there is:
A wrongful or improper threat,
A lack of reasonable alternatives, and
Actual inducement of the contract by threat.
See Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 175
Application:slide 39
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Totem Marine Tug & Barge, Inc.
Rule
Evidence?
A wrongful or improper threat,
Alyeska threatens not to perform in bad faith, knowing that it owed substantially more than its settlement offer
A lack of reasonable alternatives, and
Totem was faced with impending bankruptcy, unable to meet debts w/o immediate cash
Actual inducement of the contract by threat
Totem accepted the settlement only because a failure in payment would have thrown Totem into bankruptcy
Now assume that Totem is owned by Bill Gates (one of the most wealthy people in the country), but the facts of Totem Marine are otherwise the same. Will the court find that the contract is voidable due to economic duress?slide 40
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Duress Hypo 1
Now assume that Totem is owned by Bill Gates (one of the most wealthy people in the country), but the facts of Totem Marine are otherwise the same. Will the court find that the contract is voidable due to economic duress?slide 41
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
No. Totem has the reasonably available alternative of filing a lawsuit against Alyeska for breach of contract.
Duress Hypo 1
Smith loses his job. As a result, he desperately needs money to pay for his insurance and medical care. He thus lists his home for $100,000, which is a reasonable price. Jones, who knows that Smith has lost his job and needs the money, offers Smith $70,000, hoping to take advantage of Smith’s situation. Jones tells Smith that it will likely take him months to find a buyer who is willing to pay $100,000. Smith reluctantly agrees. Is this contract voidable due to economic duress?slide 42
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Yes
No
Duress Hypo 2
Smith loses his job. As a result, he desperately needs money to pay for his insurance and medical care. He thus lists his home for $100,000, which is a reasonable price. Jones, who knows that Smith has lost his job and needs the money, offers Smith $70,000, hoping to take advantage of Smith’s situation. Jones tells Smith that it will likely take him months to find a buyer who is willing to pay $100,000. Smith reluctantly agrees. Is this contract voidable due to economic duress?slide 43
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
No, Jones has not made a wrongful or improper threat
