Public Policyslide 44
📝 한글
Public Policyslide 45
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What is public policy?
“Public policy” is that principle of the law which holds that no subject can lawfully do that which has a tendency to be injurious to the public or against the public good.
Public policy presents the principles under which the freedom of contract or private dealings are restricted by law for the good of the community
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 186. Promise In Restraint Of Tradeslide 46
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A promise is unenforceable on grounds of public policy if it is unreasonably in restraint of trade.
A promise is in restraint of trade if its performance would limit competition in any business or restrict the promisor in the exercise of a gainful occupation.
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 186. Illustrationsslide 47
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A, B and C, competing manufacturers, promise each other not to sell goods in which they deal at prices below fixed minimums.
Their promises are unreasonably in restraint of trade and are unenforceable on grounds of public policy.
A, B and C, who are competing merchants in a city where there are many competitors, promise to become partners in order to reduce the expense of doing business. The economic situation of A, B and C is such as to make the partnership reasonable.
Their implied promises not to compete individually in the same market are not unreasonably in restraint of trade and enforcement is not precluded on grounds of public policy.
Valley Medical Specialists v. Farberslide 48
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
VMS hires Dr. Farber, a pulmonologist who treats AIDS and HIV-positive patients
The employment agreement contains a restrictive covenant, preventing him from performing “medical care” within 5 miles of any VMS location for 3 years
Dr. Farber left VMS and began practicing in the covered location. VMS filed this suit.
Valley Medical Specialists v. Farberslide 49
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether the restrictive covenant between Farber and VMS is enforceable?
Valley Medical Specialists v. Farberslide 50
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rules:
A covenant not to compete is valid only if it protects some legitimate interest beyond the employer’s desire to protect itself from competition
After identifying a legitimate interest, the court must ask where the restriction is “reasonable” by determining whether:
The restraint is greater in scope (area, activity, duration) than necessary to protect the employer’s legitimate interest; and
That interest is outweighed by the hardship to the employee and the likely injury to the public.
Valley Medical Specialists v. Farberslide 51
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Valley Medical is seeking to protect its legitimate interest in Farber’s patient base and patient referrals
Is the scope (activity, duration, area) of this restriction greater than necessary to protect Valley’s interest?
Applies to medical services beyond those performed at VMS
3 years is longer than needed to protect patient referrals
Area covers 235 square miles
Valley Medical Specialists v. Farberslide 52
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application:
Is Valley Medical ‘s interest outweighed by the hardship to the employee and the likely injury to the public?
The court states that, because he is a doctor, the K will be “strictly construed for reasonableness”. The court is saying that the injury to the public is especially large.
VMS’s interests are outweighed by the harm to Dr. Farber and his patients.

Mutual & Unilateral Mistake
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Mutual Mistake가 뭐냐면... 계약 당시 양쪽 다 사실(fact)에 대해 잘못 알고 있었던 거야. 그 잘못된 사실이 계약의 핵심(material basis)이면 계약을 취소(void/voidable)할 수 있어. Mutual Mistake 요건 3가지: ① 계약 시점에 이미 존재하는 사실의 착오 ② 계약의 기본 전제에 관한 것 ③ 위험을 한 쪽이 부담하기로 합의하지 않은 것
판례 — Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly: 부부가 아파트용 토지를 매수했어. 계약서엔 "As-Is" 조항이 있었어. 근데 나중에 그 땅에 불법 정화조가 있어서 주거 불가 판정 났어. 쌍방 다 이 사실을 계약 시점에 몰랐어. 법원: Mutual Mistake 맞아. 하지만 As-Is 조항 때문에 위험을 매수인이 부담하기로 한 거라고 봐 → 취소 불가. "As-Is"는 위험 배분 계약이야.
Unilateral Mistake: 한쪽만 틀렸을 때. 원칙적으로 취소 불가. 단, 상대방이 그 착오를 알았거나 착오가 너무 명백해서 집행하는 게 비양심적일 때만 예외. Mutual Mistake vs. Frustration of Purpose: Mistake는 계약 당시부터 사실이 달랐던 것. Frustration은 계약 후 상황이 바뀐 것.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Mistakeslide 55
📝 한글
Mutual Mistakeslide 56
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
What is a mistake?
A contractual mistake is a belief that is not in accord with the facts.
For the doctrine of mistake to apply, the erroneous belief must relate to a fact in existence at the time the contract is executed.
When will a mistake support rescission of a contract?
A mutual mistake supports rescission when the mistaken belief relates to a basic assumption of the parties upon which the contract is made and which materially affects the agreed performances of the parties.
Rescission is not available to a party that has assumed the risk of loss in connection with the mistake.
Mutual Mistakeslide 57
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Elements:
Mistake of both parties (mutual)
At the time of contracting (mistake)
Concerns a basic assumption
Has a material effect on performances
Party asserting defense did not assume the risk
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerlyslide 58
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
The Pickles bought rental property
Clause in Contract:
“Purchaser has examined this property and agrees to accept same in its present condition. There are no other or additional written or oral understandings.”
The septic system is too small
The house was condemned as a result.
The Pickles sought rescission
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerlyslide 59
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue:
Whether the contract could be rescinded on the basis of mistake?
Rule:slide 60
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract will be rescinded on the basis of mistake if all of the following are true:
Mistake of both parties (mutual)
At the time of contracting (mistake)
Concerns a basic assumption
Has a material effect on performances
Party asserting defense did not assume the risk
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly
What was the mistake?slide 61
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contractual mistake is a belief that is not in accord with the facts.
Both the seller and buyer mistakenly believed that the property transferred could be utilized as income generating rental property.
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly
Does the mistake relate to a fact in existence at the time the contract was executed?slide 62
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
For the doctrine of mistake to apply, the erroneous belief must relate to a fact in existence at the time the contract is executed.
Yes. Despite no problems at the time, the septic system as installed was too small for the property at the time the contract was executed.
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly
Did the mistake go to a basic assumption of the contract?slide 63
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A mutual mistake supports rescission when the mistaken belief relates to a basic assumption of the parties upon which the contract is made and which materially affects the agreed performances of the parties.
Yes. A basic assumption of the contract was that that the building was suitable for human habitation and could be utilized to generate income.
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly
Did the mistake materially affect the agreed performances of the parties?slide 64
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A mutual mistake supports rescission when the mistaken belief relates to a basic assumption of the parties upon which the contract is made and which materially affects the agreed performances of the parties.
Yes. The invalidity of the assumption changes the character of the property transferred and thereby frustrates the intended use of the property.
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly
Who bore the risk of mistake?slide 65
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rescission is not available to a party that has assumed the risk of loss in connection with the mistake.
Mr. and Mrs. Pickles (purchasers)
Clause in K: “Purchaser has examined this property and agrees to accept same in its present condition. There are no other or additional written or oral understandings.”
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly
So what is the result? Can the Pickles rescind the contract under the mistake defense?slide 66
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
No. They assumed the risk of loss is case of mistake. One of the elements of the rule is missing.
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly
When does a party assume the risk?slide 67
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The risk is allocated to him by the court
The party is aware at time the contract is made that he has limited knowledge regarding facts relating to mistake but treats knowledge as sufficient
The risk is allocated to him by agreement
Lenawee County Board of Health v. Messerly
Restatement (Second) Contracts § 154

Smith purchases the motor, and finds that it cannot shift out of neutral, making it worthless.

No

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문

Owner and Builder believe that all of the gravel and earth is above water level and can be removed by ordinary means, but in fact about one quarter of it is below water level, so that removal will require special equipment at an additional cost of about twenty percent.
Does Builder have a defense to performing the Contract?
Yes
No
Hypothetical 2slide 71
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Owner of land and Builder make a contract under which Builder is to take from Owner’s land, at a stated rate per cubic yard, all the gravel and earth necessary for the construction of a bridge, an amount estimated to be 114,000 cubic yards. Owner and Builder believe that all of the gravel and earth is above water level and can be removed by ordinary means, but in fact about one quarter of it is below water level, so that removal will require special equipment at an additional cost of about twenty percent.
Does Builder have a defense to performing the Contract?
Elements:
Mistake of both parties (mutual)
At the time of contracting (mistake)
Concerns a basic assumption
Has a material effect on performances
Party asserting defense did not assume the risk
No. The contract is not voidable by Builder, because the court will allocate to Builder the risk of the mistake because Builder can best bear and prevent this risk
Hypothetical 3slide 72
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Joe inherits a box of jewelry when his grandmother passes away. Joe doesn’t know exactly what type of jewelry is in the box, but he thinks that his grandmother probably wouldn’t have anything too expensive and doesn’t want to go through the hassle of getting it appraised. Joe thus sells the box and all jewelry to Kim, a friend who collects antiques, for $500. Kim also has no idea what the jewelry is worth. After the purchase, Kim takes the jewelry to an appraiser and learns that it is worth $50,000. If Joe seeks to rescind the contract under mistake, what will be the result?
Kim will win, because she had no idea what the jewelry was worth at the time of formation
Joe will win, because it would be unconscionable for Kim to keep the jewelry
Joe will win, because both parties made a mistake as to a basic assumption at the time of contracting that had a material affect on the parties’ performances
Kim will win, because Joe assumed the risk that the jewelry would be more valuable than he anticipated

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Joe inherits a box of jewelry when his grandmother passes away. Joe doesn’t know exactly what type of jewelry is in the box, but he thinks that his grandmother probably wouldn’t have anything too expensive and doesn’t want to go through the hassle of getting it appraised. Joe thus sells the box and all jewelry to Kim, a friend who collects antiques, for $500. Kim also has no idea what the jewelry is worth. After the purchase, Kim takes the jewelry to an appraiser and learns that it is worth $50,000. If Joe seeks to rescind the contract under mistake, what will be the result?
Kim will win, because she had no idea what the jewelry was worth at the time of formation
Joe will win, because it would be unconscionable for Kim to keep the jewelry
Joe will win, because both parties made a mistake as to a basic assumption at the time of contracting that had a material affect on the parties’ performances
Kim will win, because Joe assumed the risk that the jewelry would be more valuable than he anticipated
Unilateral Mistakeslide 74
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule
A contract based upon a unilateral mistake may be rescinded if the mutual mistake factors are met; and either
Effect of mistake would make enforcement unconscionable
Other party had reason to know of the mistake or his fault caused it.
Material Facts:slide 75
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Wil-Fred’s submitted a bid for a city project
Wil-Fred’s bid was the lowest bid, because it was based on the mistaken estimate of a subcontractor
Subcontractor’s bid was mistaken because he erroneously believed heavy equipment could be used on the project
The subcontractor’s bid was $150,000 less than the cost with the proper equipment
Wil-Fred’s attempts to rescind its bid based on mistake
Wil-Fred’s Inc. v. Metropolitan Sanitary District
Issue:slide 76
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Under what circumstances may a contract be rescinded for unilateral mistake?
Wil-Fred’s Inc. v. Metropolitan Sanitary District
Ruleslide 77
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문

Other party had reason to know of the mistake or his fault caused it.

Application:slide 78
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Mistake of one party at the time of contracting;
Mistaken bid
Concerns a basic assumption
Ability to use normal equipment
Has a material effect on performances
$150,000
Party asserting defense did not assume the risk
City was not harmed by withdrawing bid; city’s actions induced mistake; Wil-Fred’s exercised reasonable care
Effect of mistake would make enforcement unconscionable
Burden on Wil-Fred’s too great
Other party had reason to know of the mistake or his fault caused it
City gave conflicting and ambiguous statements

4
Changed Circumstances (Impossibility/Frustration)
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Changed Circumstances가 뭐냐면... 계약 후 예상치 못한 사건이 생겨서 이행이 불가능하거나 무의미해진 경우야. 법원이 의무를 면제해줄 수 있어. 3가지 법리: ① Impossibility: 이행 자체가 물리적으로 불가능해짐. 예: 계약한 건물이 화재로 소실. ② Commercial Impracticability: 이행이 가능하긴 한데, 계약의 기본 전제였던 상황이 바뀌어 극도로 어려워짐. UCC § 2-615. ③ Frustration of Purpose: 이행은 가능하지만, 계약 목적 자체가 사라졌을 때. 공통 요건: ① 예상치 못한 사건 발생 ② 그 사건의 리스크를 계약으로 어느 쪽이 부담할지 정하지 않았을 것 ③ 이행이 불가/무의미
판례 — Taylor v. Caldwell: 음악당을 임대했어. 콘서트 직전 화재로 소실. 법원: Impossibility 인정 — 계약의 기반이 된 건물이 사라졌으니 양쪽 다 의무 소멸. / Krell v. Henry: 에드워드 7세 대관식 행렬을 보려고 창문 임대. 대관식이 갑자기 취소됐어. 건물은 멀쩡해 — 하지만 창문 임대의 목적(행렬 관람)이 사라졌어 → Frustration of Purpose.
부분적 이행 불능(Partial Impracticability): 전체 아닌 일부만 불능이면 가능한 부분은 이행하고, 합리적으로 배분해야 해. (UCC § 2-615)
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Changed Circumstancesslide 81
📝 한글
Impossibility, Impracticability & Frustrationslide 82
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Mistake dealt with events that occurred before K formation.
Impossibility, impracticability and FOP result from events occurring after K formation.
Impracticability, Impossibility and Frustrationslide 83
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Elements:
The non-occurrence of something was basic assumption of the contract
That “something” occurs and makes performance or purpose impossible/impracticable/substantially frustrated
Due to no fault of one claiming excuse; AND
The parties didn’t assume the risk
Impossibility, Impracticability & Frustrationslide 84
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Assumption of the risk applies to both mistake and changed circumstances
Changed circumstances will provide a defense only when the parties themselves did not allocate the risk of the events which have rendered performance impossible or impracticable, or which have frustrated the purpose of the K
Basic Assumptionslide 85
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 261, cmt b
Its application is simple enough in the cases of the death of a person or destruction of a specific thing necessary for performance. The continued existence of the person or thing (the non-occurrence of the death of destruction) is ordinarily a basic assumption on which the contract was made, so that death or destruction effects a discharge.
Its application is also simple enough in the cases of market shifts or the financial inability of one of the parties. The continuation of existing market conditions and of the financial situation of the parties are ordinarily not such assumptions, so that mere market shifts or financial inability do not usually effect discharge under the rule stated in this Section.
In borderline cases this criterion is sufficiently flexible to take account of factors that bear on a just allocation of risk. The fact that the event was foreseeable, or even foreseen, does not necessarily compel a conclusion that its non-occurrence was not a basic assumption.
Assuming the Riskslide 86
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 261, cmt c
Even absent an express agreement, a court may decide, after considering all the circumstances, that a party impliedly assumed such a greater obligation. . . . Circumstances relevant in deciding whether a party has assumed a greater obligation include:
His ability to have inserted a provision in the contract expressly shifting the risk of impracticability to the other party. . . .
A commercial practice under which a party might be expected to insure or otherwise secure himself against a risk also militates against shifting it to the other party.
Foreseeability: If the supervening event was not reasonably foreseeable when the contract was made, the party claiming discharge can hardly be expected to have provided against its occurrence. However, if it was reasonably foreseeable, or even foreseen, the opposite conclusion does not necessarily follow.
Impracticabilityslide 87
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 261, cmt d
Performance may be impracticable because extreme and unreasonable difficulty, expense, injury, or loss to one of the parties will be involved.
Performance may also be impracticable because it will involve a risk of injury that is disproportionate to the ends to be attained by performance.
However, “impracticability” means more than “impracticality.” A mere change in the degree of difficulty or expense due to such causes as increased wages, prices of raw materials, or costs of construction, unless well beyond the normal range, does not amount to impracticability since it is this sort of risk that a fixed-price contract is intended to cover.
Frustration of Purposeslide 88
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 261, cmt a
circumstances makes one party's performance virtually worthless to the other, frustrating his purpose in making the contract.
the frustration must be substantial. It is not enough that the transaction has become less profitable for the affected party or even that he will sustain a loss. The frustration must be so severe that it is not fairly to be regarded as within the risks that he assumed under the contract.
It is distinct from the problem of impracticability . . . because there is no impediment to performance by either party.
Karl Wendt Farm Equipment Co. v. International Harvester Co.slide 89
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Wendt is a dealer of IH farm equipment under a Dealer Agreement
The Dealer Agreement can only be terminated upon certain specified conditions
IH’s farm equipment division is losing the company millions
IH thus sells its farm equipment division to Tenneco
Wendt is not offered a Tenneco franchise
Wendt sues IH for breach of the Dealer Agreement
Karl Wendt Farm Equipment Co. v. International Harvester Co.slide 90
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #1 : Whether impracticability was a valid defense for IH’s breach of the franchise agreement
Rule Elements:
The non-occurrence of something was basic assumption of the contract
That “something” occurs and makes performance or purpose impossible/impracticable/substantially frustrated
Due to no fault of one claiming excuse
And parties didn’t assume the risk
Application:
Economic stability is not a basic assumption
Mere unprofitability is not impracticability
Karl Wendt Farm Equipment Co. v. International Harvester Co.slide 91
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue #2: Whether the doctrine of frustration of purpose was applicable?
Defendant’s argument: the primary purpose of the contract was mutual profitability.
Court rejects this argument, holding that the primary purpose was to establish a dealership
Court suggests that profitability cannot be the “purpose,” because the defense is not a way for parties to avoid a contract simply because it is unprofitable
Frustration of purpose is about allocating risk in light of unforeseen circumstances, and here IH should bear the risk of a market downturn making its K unprofitable
Mel Frank Tool & Supply v. Di-Chemslide 92
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Material Facts:
Di-Chem enters into a lease with Mel Frank for a storage and distribution facility
After the lease is formed, the chemicals Di-Chem is using at the premises are labeled as hazardous by the city
Di-Chem vacated the premises, because the city’s action made the property useless to the company
Mel Frank sued for breach of the lease and Di-Chem defended in part on the basis of frustration of purpose
Mel Frank Tool & Supply v. Di-Chemslide 93
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Issue: Whether Di-Chem’s performance under the lease can be excused under frustration of purpose
Why aren’t we talking about impracticability?
Di-Chem isn’t saying that performance is difficult or impracticable; rather it is saying that Mel Frank’s performance is much less valuable to it
Mel Frank Tool & Supply v. Di-Chemslide 94
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Rule: Frustration of purpose = circumstances make one party's performance virtually worthless to the other, frustrating his purpose in making the contract.
The frustration must be substantial. It is not enough that the transaction has become less profitable for the affected party or even that he will sustain a loss. The frustration must be so severe that it is not fairly to be regarded as within the risks that he assumed under the contract
Application:
The purpose of the contract was to store the chemicals. The lease is worthless to Di-Chem now, so the defense applies.
Hypothetical 1slide 95
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Taylor contracts to renovate Caldwell’s concert hall. While Taylor is engaged in making repairs, a fire destroys the concert hall, and Taylor does not finish the repairs.
Taylor’s duty to renovate the concert hall is discharged, and Taylor is not liable to Caldwell for breach of contract.
Performance is impossible, existence of the concert hall was a basic assumption of the contract, and there is no express of implied term allocating the risk (we can assume Caldwell is more likely to have fire insurance on the concert hall and can thus best bear the risk)

Builder abandons the site and goes off to build something else more profitable, and does not get or request any money from Caldwell. Caldwell sues Builder for breach. Builder claims that her non-performance is excused due to impossibility. Who wins?
Builder
Caldwell

Fraudulent Misrepresentationslide 102
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contract is voidable by the innocent party if:
Fraudulent or material misrepresentation;
Fraudulent = the party makes a statement of fact that he knows is not true
Hiding/concealing a fact is the same as saying it doesn’t exist
Material = important enough to induce the agreement
The innocent agreed to the contract because of the fraud; and
Reliance on the fraudulent statement was reasonable

Yes
No

Plaintiff purchases a home from Defendant. The home had serious water damage in the past. The Defendant hired someone to paint over the water damage so that it would not be visible. Defendant is not asked about water damage and does not disclose it.
5/13/2026
Yes. Defendant’s concealment of the water damage is equivalent to a fraudulent misrepresentation

UDSL 슬라이드 원문 — Class 8 — Modification & Waiver
1
Modification & Waiver
0회독 — 처음 읽는 사람을 위한 설명
Modification이 뭐냐면... 이미 체결된 계약을 나중에 바꾸는 거야. 바꾸는 게 유효하려면 어떤 조건이? Common Law: 변경에도 새로운 Consideration이 필요해. 이미 하기로 된 걸 "해줄게" 하는 건 Consideration 아님(Pre-Existing Duty Rule). Pre-Existing Duty Rule 예외 2가지: ① 예상 못 한 사정으로 인한 공정한 변경 (unforeseen circumstances) ② 계약 취소 후 새로 체결 (rescission + new contract) UCC: Goods 계약 변경은 Consideration 없어도 돼 — 단, Good Faith(성실)만 있으면 유효. "협박해서 올린 가격"은 Good Faith 아님.
판례 — Kelsey-Hayes: 자동차 부품 공급자가 납기 중에 "가격 올려줘, 안 그러면 납품 중단"이라고 협박했어. 자동차 회사는 어쩔 수 없이 동의했어. 법원: UCC에서도 변경은 Good Faith 필요. 이건 Economic Duress + Bad Faith → 변경 무효. 단순히 원자재 값이 올라서 가격 올려달라는 요청은 Good Faith 변경이 될 수 있어.
Waiver: "계약 조건을 포기할게"라는 의사표시. Consideration 없이도 가능. 단, 중요 조건(material term)의 포기는 나중에 철회 가능 (Retraction) — 상대방이 그에 의존하기 전에. No Oral Modification (NOM) 조항: "변경은 서면으로만" 조항 있어도, 구두 변경 후 이행했으면 법원이 유효로 볼 수 있어.
📖 UDSL 슬라이드 원문1회독
Agendaslide 1
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Modification
Final Exam
Review
Practice Problems
Modificationslide 2
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A modification is a change in one or more respects which leaves the general purpose and effect of the contract undisturbed.
A modification is permanent. The original agreement merges into the new (modified) agreement and is extinguished.
Modificationslide 3
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Pre-existing duty rule:
Under the common law, a modification is effective only with additional consideration
Promising to do what you are already obligated to do under a contract is not consideration for a modification to that contract.
There are two exceptions to the pre-existing duty rule:slide 4
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A fair modification due to unforeseen circumstances; or
Reliance on a promised modification
Restatement (Second) of Contracts § 89
A fair modification due to unforeseen circumstances:slide 5
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The limitation to a modification which is “fair and equitable” goes beyond absence of coercion and requires an objectively demonstrable reason for seeking a modification.
The reason for modification must rest in circumstances not “anticipated” as part of the context in which the contract was made, but a frustrating event may be unanticipated for this purpose if it was not adequately covered, even though it was foreseen as a remote possibility.
In these circumstances, we are not concerned about a party taking unfair advantage of the other side in bad faith
Material facts:slide 6
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Group of sailors/fishermen entered into contract under which they would receive $50 or $60 for season’s work plus two cents for each salmon the catching of which he took part.
When they arrive in Alaska they stopped work and demanded that the company’s superintendent alter the contract so that they received $100.
Superintendent made the change but stated that he did not have the power to alter the contract.
Company refused to pay
Alaska Packers’ Association v. Domenico
Pre-existing duty rule: Promising to do what you are already obligated to do under a contract is not consideration for a modification to that contract.slide 7
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Application: The modification is not enforceable because the fishermen had a preexisting duty to catch the fish. They provided no new consideration
Alaska Packers’ Association v. Domenico
Rationale:slide 8
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Although Domenico signed, the court is concerned that APA took unfair advantage of Domenico by acting in bad faith under the K
The pre-existing duty rule is meant to protect parties from such bad faith
Alaska Packers’ Association v. Domenico
What if the fisherman in APA discovered that the nets provided by Domenico were in disrepair, making the job more dangerous and difficult?slide 9
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Now there are unforeseen circumstances that were not anticipated at the time of formation
Alaska Packers’ Association v. Domenico
Hypothetical 1slide 10
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
By a written contract Smith agrees to excavate a cellar for Jones for a stated price. Solid rock is unexpectedly encountered and Smith so notifies Jones. They then orally agree that Smith will remove the rock at a unit price which is reasonable but nine times that used in computing the original price, and Smith completes the job. Is Jones bound to pay the increased amount?
Yes
No

🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
By a written contract Smith agrees to excavate a cellar for Jones for a stated price. Solid rock is unexpectedly encountered and Smith so notifies Jones. They then orally agree that Smith will remove the rock at a unit price which is reasonable but nine times that used in computing the original price, and Smith completes the job. Is Jones bound to pay the increased amount?
Yes, the unforeseen circumstances exception applies

B agrees to shipment under ventilation but later changes his mind. A receives notification of the change after leaving the first port. Is the modification effective?

A has relied on the modification and thus may ship under ventilation

Hypothetical 3slide 15
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
A contracts with B to carry a shipment of fish under refrigeration. During the short first leg of the voyage the refrigeration equipment on the ship breaks down, and A offers either to continue under ventilation or to hold the cargo at the first port for later shipment. B agrees to shipment under ventilation but later changes his mind. A receives notification of the change before reaching the first port. What result?
A is bound to ship under refrigeration, because A has not relied on the modification
UCC Modificationslide 16
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Under Article 2 of the Uniform Commercial Code, an agreement modifying a contract needs no consideration to be binding.
Accordingly, courts have held that a post sale assurance of repair is an express warranty and is binding as a modification of the contract, even though not supported by consideration
Modification and conductslide 17
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
The conduct of the parties to a sales contract may constitute a modification of their agreement:
acceptance of nonconforming goods, especially when they are retained, used, and resold, or when the buyer orally agrees to pay for them at the contract rate, may be conduct evidencing a modification of the contract
acceptance of goods at a modified price is conduct that demonstrates a modification of the contract, despite prohibitions on non-written modifications in the contract, and the statute of frauds
Later conduct may also show that parties did not intend a modification.
Waiverslide 18
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Sometimes there is not a modification (change to the contract) but instead a waiver.
A waiver is the intentional relinquishment of a known right.
Hypotheticalslide 19
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Wallace enters into a contract to sell Robert 1200 pallets of bagged fertilizer in lots of 100 to be delivered each month for twelve months no later than the 5th of that month. In May, Wallace tells Robert that the May delivery will be delayed by two days. Robert says that this is not a problem. Is this a modification or a waiver?
Waiverslide 20
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
Think about what happens if Wallace simply makes the next (the June) delivery on the 7th.
This would be two days late under the original contract.
If Robert only waived the delivery requirement for May, then Wallace has breached the (original and only) contract in June.
If Robert agreed to a modification altering the delivery date, then Wallace has not breached the modified contract.
No Oral Modification (“NOM”) Clausesslide 21
🇺🇸 UDSL 원문
UCC § 2-209:
(2) NOM clauses are enforceable
(3) The requirements of the statute of frauds section of this Article (Section 2-201) must be satisfied if the contract as modified is within its provisions.
(4) Although an attempt at modification or rescission does not satisfy the requirements of subsection (2) or (3) it can operate as a waiver.
(5) A party who has made a waiver affecting an executory portion of the contract may retract the waiver by reasonable notification received by the other party that strict performance will be required of any term waived, unless the retraction would be unjust in view of a material change of position in reliance on the waive
KTK 문제풀이 (17문제) — 팩트패턴 분석 후 ↓ 버튼으로 정답·해설 확인
Applicable Law & Formation
📝 핵심 이론
Common Law vs UCC 구분 → 물건(Goods) 매매면 UCC, 서비스·부동산은 Common Law.
혼합계약: Predominant Purpose Test (주된 목적 기준).
UCC: 상인(Merchant) 개념 중요 — 그 종류 물건 거래하는 자.
Output/Requirements 계약: Best Efforts 묵시적 의무 포함 (UCC §2-306).
🇺🇸 Key Rules
UCC Article 2 governs sale of goods (moveable, tangible, identified at contracting). All else — services, real property — is Common Law.
Mixed contracts: Predominant Purpose Test — which purpose is primary?
Merchant: one who deals in goods of the kind or holds themselves out as having special knowledge.
Output/Requirements contracts: imply best efforts obligation (UCC §2-306).
Q1 — Applicable Law
A buyer contacts a seller to purchase 500 custom-designed metal widgets to be incorporated into the buyer's manufacturing machinery. The seller agrees by email. No written contract is signed. Which body of law governs this transaction?
(A) Common Law, because the contract involves manufacturing services.
(B) UCC Article 2, because the primary subject matter is the sale of goods.
(C) Neither, because there is no signed written contract.
(D) Both equally, under the Predominant Purpose Test.
정답: B
UCC Article 2 governs contracts for the sale of goods — moveable, tangible things identified at the time of contracting. Custom-manufactured widgets are goods. Although manufacturing services are involved, the Predominant Purpose Test looks to the primary purpose of the contract: here, the delivery of the widgets. The lack of a signed writing is relevant to the Statute of Frauds, not to which body of law governs.
Q2 — UCC Merchant
Darla owns a bookstore that sells new and used books. She posts a notice in her store window offering to sell a set of used law school textbooks for $500, and adds: 'This offer will remain open for 30 days.' Bob, a law student, sees the notice but does not respond for 35 days. When Bob arrives to buy the books, Darla has already sold them. Bob sues, claiming Darla breached a firm offer. Who prevails?
(A) Bob, because Darla's written promise to hold the offer open for 30 days is binding under UCC § 2-205.
(B) Bob, because the offer remained open for a reasonable time beyond 30 days.
(C) No, because Darla gave written assurance that the offer would remain open until November 15.
(D) Darla, because Bob failed to accept within the 30-day period stated in the offer.
정답: D
The UCC Firm Offer rule (§2-205) applies only to merchants. Darla was not a merchant with respect to law books or bookshelves. Under Common Law, a promise to hold an offer open is not binding without consideration. The $10,000 book sale did not constitute consideration for the promise to hold the stack offer open. Therefore, without consideration, Darla's promise was not binding, and the offer was freely revocable.
Q3 — Output Contract
Bestbake Co. and Today's Pastry Inc. entered into a one-year output contract under which Today's Pastry agreed to purchase all of Bestbake's output of baked buns. After six months, Today's Pastry stopped ordering. Bestbake sues. What is the most likely outcome?
(A) Today's Pastry wins, because Bestbake was not bound to sell a fixed number of units.
(B) Today's Pastry wins, because the UCC Statute of Frauds requires a specific quantity term.
(C) Bestbake wins, because Today's Pastry had a best-efforts obligation to purchase Bestbake's output.
(D) Bestbake wins, because Today's Pastry's conduct constituted anticipatory repudiation.
정답: C
Because the contract involves the sale of goods, the UCC controls. Under the UCC, output contracts are ones in which the buyer agrees to purchase all of a seller's output for a particular good. For such contracts, sellers and buyers have an obligation to act in good faith — to use their best efforts to supply and purchase the goods respectively. Therefore, Today's Pastry Inc. was under an implied obligation to use its best efforts to purchase Bestbake's one-year output of baked buns.
Offer / Acceptance / Firm Offer
📝 핵심 이론
Mirror Image Rule (Common Law): Acceptance는 Offer 조건 그대로여야. 조건 변경 = Counteroffer → 원래 Offer 소멸.
UCC §2-207 Battle of the Forms: 추가·다른 조건 있어도 Acceptance 성립. 추가 조건은 상인간 자동 포함(중요 변경 아닌 경우).
Firm Offer (UCC §2-205): 상인이 서면으로 offer open → Consideration 없이 최대 3개월 철회 불가.
Mailbox Rule: 수락 편지는 보내는 순간 효력 발생. Option Contract·지정 방법은 도착해야.
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Mirror Image Rule (CL): Acceptance must match offer exactly — any change = Counteroffer, killing the original offer.
UCC §2-207 (Battle of the Forms): Different/additional terms don't prevent acceptance. Between merchants, additional terms become part of contract unless material alteration or objection.
Firm Offer (UCC §2-205): Merchant's signed written assurance to keep offer open — irrevocable up to 3 months without consideration.
Mailbox Rule: Acceptance effective on dispatch. Exception: option contracts require receipt.
Q21 — Parol Evidence — Course of Performance
Wavelaster Inc. and Wetailers Co. signed a three-year agreement for Wavelaster to sell all radio equipment to Wetailers at $50 per unit. The written agreement allowed the buyer to return defective radios for a refund but was silent on non-defective returns. Wetailers seeks to introduce evidence that during the contract's three-year term, it returned 125 non-defective radios which Wavelaster refused to credit. The trial court should rule the evidence is:
(A) Inadmissible, because it is barred by the parol evidence rule.
(B) Inadmissible because the express terms of the agreement contradict the course of performance.
(C) Admissible, because it supports an agreement not within the statute of frauds.
(D) Admissible, because course-of-performance evidence is considered the best indication of what the parties intended the writing to mean.
정답: D
Course-of-performance evidence — the conduct of the parties during the life of the contract — is generally admissible as the best evidence of the parties' intent. Under the UCC, courts look to course of performance, course of dealing, and trade usage to supplement or explain contract terms. Because the written agreement was silent on non-defective returns (not contradictory), the course-of-performance evidence is admissible to show what the parties intended.
Q22 — Accord & Satisfaction
In the same Wavelaster/Wetailers dispute, Wetailers returned 25 radios and included a check marked 'Payment in full for all goods sold to Wetailers Co. to date.' Wavelaster's clerk, knowing about the 25 returned radios, deposited the check without protest. Wavelaster later sues for the value of the 25 radios. Wetailers' best defense is:
(A) Wavelaster's deposit estopped it from claiming Wetailers owed any additional amount.
(B) By depositing the check with knowledge of its notation, Wavelaster discharged the disputed debt by accord and satisfaction.
(C) The check constituted a unilateral contract that Wavelaster accepted by depositing it.
(D) Wetailers had a statutory right under the UCC to return non-defective goods.
정답: B
Accord and satisfaction requires (1) a bona fide dispute about the amount owed, (2) an offer of a specific sum in full settlement, and (3) acceptance of that offer. When Wavelaster's clerk deposited the check that was conspicuously marked 'payment in full,' knowing about the disputed 25 radios, this constituted acceptance of the accord. The satisfaction (depositing the check) discharged the disputed debt. This is a classic accord and satisfaction scenario.
Capacity
📝 핵심 이론
미성년자(Infancy): 계약 voidable — 미성년자 단독으로 성년 전후 disaffirm 가능. 성년 후 합리적 시간 내 취소 없으면 ratify 간주 가능.
Necessities 예외: 음식·의복·주거·의료는 미성년자도 quasi-contract 책임 (실제 가치 기준, 계약가 아님).
Mental Incapacity: 계약 시점에 행위 성질·결과 이해 불가 = voidable. 법원 adjudication 있으면 void.
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Infancy: Contract is voidable at minor's election — may disaffirm before or within reasonable time after majority. Upon disaffirmance, must return consideration received.
Necessities exception: Minor liable in quasi-contract for food, clothing, shelter, medical care (measured by reasonable value, not contract price).
Mental Incapacity: Voidable if party could not understand nature/consequences at time of contracting. Void if subject to prior adjudication.
Q_cap1 — Infancy / Disaffirmance
A 16-year-old purchased a used car from a dealer for $8,000, paying cash. Two months later, after using the car regularly, the minor seeks to disaffirm the contract and recover the $8,000. The car has depreciated to $5,500. Under the traditional common law rule, what result?
(A) The minor may disaffirm and recover the full $8,000, because the contract is voidable.
(B) The minor may disaffirm but can only recover $5,500, the current value of the car.
(C) The minor may not disaffirm because a car is a necessity.
(D) The minor may not disaffirm because two months have passed.
정답: A
Under the traditional (majority) common law rule, a contract entered into by a minor is voidable at the minor's election. Upon disaffirmance, the minor may recover the full consideration paid, regardless of depreciation or use. The minor must return the car (or whatever remains), but is entitled to the full $8,000 back. A car is generally not classified as a necessity (food, clothing, shelter, medical care). The two-month delay does not prevent disaffirmance before reaching majority.
Parol Evidence
📝 핵심 이론
완전 통합(Total Integration): 서면이 최종·완전 합의 → prior/contemporaneous 구두 합의 모두 배제.
부분 통합(Partial Integration): 추가 조건 배제, 모순 조건 배제, 설명·해석은 가능.
PER 예외: 사기·강박(fraud/duress), Condition Precedent, 서명 후 수정(Modification), 모호성(Ambiguity) 해석 — 이 경우엔 외부 증거 허용.
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Total Integration: Writing is final and complete expression — bars all prior/contemporaneous agreements that add or contradict.
Partial Integration: Writing is final but incomplete — bars contradictions, allows consistent additional terms.
PER Exceptions: fraud, duress, condition precedent to effectiveness, post-signing modification, and ambiguity — extrinsic evidence admissible for all.
Q_per1 — PER — Totally Integrated
Buyer and Seller signed a detailed written contract for the sale of a house, including a merger clause stating 'This agreement constitutes the entire agreement between the parties.' Buyer now seeks to introduce evidence of an oral promise made before signing that Seller would repaint the exterior. Under the classical (four corners) approach, this evidence is:
(A) Admissible, because it concerns a collateral matter.
(B) Admissible, because it is consistent with the written terms.
(C) Inadmissible, because the writing is a total integration and the oral promise adds a term.
(D) Inadmissible, because real estate contracts must be in writing.
정답: C
When a written agreement is totally integrated (a complete and final expression of the parties' agreement — evidenced here by the merger clause), the parol evidence rule bars evidence of any prior or contemporaneous agreement that would add to or contradict the writing. Under the classical four-corners approach, courts look only to the writing itself to determine integration. The oral promise to repaint adds a new term and is therefore inadmissible.
Q_per2 — PER — Fraud Exception
Owner and Buyer signed a written loan modification agreement. Before signing, Lender orally promised to restructure the loan on two properties. The written agreement only addressed one property. Owner seeks to introduce evidence of the oral promise about the second property. The trial court should:
(A) Exclude the evidence under the parol evidence rule, because the written agreement is integrated.
(B) Admit the evidence, because it concerns fraud in the inducement.
(C) Admit the evidence, because the oral promise addresses a separate collateral agreement.
(D) Exclude the evidence, because the Statute of Frauds requires real property agreements to be written.
정답: B
The parol evidence rule does not bar evidence of fraud in the inducement. If a party was induced to sign a written agreement based on a fraudulent misrepresentation, extrinsic evidence of that misrepresentation is admissible regardless of the integration. Here, if the lender fraudulently promised to restructure the second property to induce signing, that evidence goes to fraud — a recognized exception to the parol evidence rule (see Riverisland Cold Storage v. Fresno-Madera Production Credit Assn.).
Conditions & Waiver
📝 핵심 이론
Express Condition: 엄격 충족(Strict Compliance) 필수 — 하루 늦어도 조건 미충족. Substantial Performance는 Promise에만 적용.
Waiver: 조건 포기 가능. 중요(material) 조건 포기는 Consideration 필요. 반복 행동으로 묵시적 포기(Waiver by Conduct) 성립 가능.
Constructive Condition: 순서 있는 이행에서 선행 의무가 후행 의무의 묵시적 조건 — 먼저 이행 안 하면 상대 의무 미발생.
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Express Condition: Must be strictly/literally satisfied — no substantial performance excuse. One day late = condition not met.
Waiver: Party may waive a condition; waiver of material condition requires consideration. Repeated conduct may create waiver by estoppel.
Constructive Condition: In sequential performance, the first party's performance is an implied condition to the other's duty to perform.
Q_cond1 — Express Condition — Strict Compliance
A tenant had a lease option to renew if written notice was provided 'by September 1.' The tenant sent written notice on September 2. The landlord refused to honor the option. The tenant argues the one-day delay was immaterial. Under the common law rule on express conditions, what result?
(A) The tenant prevails, because the one-day delay was immaterial.
(B) The tenant prevails, because the landlord waived the condition by not immediately objecting.
(C) The landlord prevails, because express conditions must be strictly satisfied.
(D) The landlord prevails, because the tenant's conduct constituted anticipatory repudiation.
정답: C
Express conditions must be strictly, literally satisfied — not merely substantially. This is a critical distinction from the substantial performance doctrine, which applies to promises. Because the tenant failed to give notice by September 1 as expressly required, the condition was not met and the tenant lost the right to exercise the option. See Oppenheimer & Co. v. Oppenheim, Appel, Dixon & Co. There is no evidence of waiver on the landlord's part.
Impracticability
📝 핵심 이론
Impossibility (Common Law): 이행이 객관적으로 불가능 — 이행 대상 물건 멸실, 법령 변경, 지정 인물 사망.
Commercial Impracticability (UCC §2-615): 예측 불가 사태로 이행이 극단적 부담 → 가능한 만큼만 이행 후 합리적 배분 의무.
Frustration of Purpose: 이행은 가능하지만 계약 목적 자체 소멸. 양측이 예측 불가했어야 적용 (Coronation Cases).
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Impossibility (CL): Performance excused if objectively impossible — destruction of subject matter, death of specified person, supervening illegality.
Commercial Impracticability (UCC §2-615): Unforeseen contingency makes performance commercially impracticable — seller must allocate available supply proportionally.
Frustration of Purpose: Performance possible but principal purpose destroyed by unforeseen event. Both parties must not have assumed the risk.
Q_imp1 — Commercial Impracticability
A farmer contracted to sell 1,000 bushels of wheat to a buyer at $5 per bushel. An unexpected drought destroyed 80% of the farmer's crop. The farmer can only harvest 200 bushels. The farmer seeks to be excused from delivering the remaining 800 bushels. Under the UCC commercial impracticability doctrine, what is the most likely result?
(A) The farmer is fully excused because the drought was unforeseeable.
(B) The farmer must deliver only the 200 available bushels and allocate them fairly if there are multiple buyers.
(C) The farmer is not excused because price fluctuation is a normal commercial risk.
(D) The farmer is excused only if the drought was caused by an act of God.
정답: B
Under UCC § 2-615, a seller is excused from delivery to the extent performance has been made impracticable by an unforeseen contingency. When only partial performance remains possible, the seller must allocate the available supply among buyers in a fair and reasonable manner. The farmer can deliver the 200 bushels available but need not obtain wheat elsewhere. The buyer must be notified and may choose to terminate or accept the partial delivery.
Breach & Remedies
📝 핵심 이론
기대이익(Expectation): 계약 이행 시 있었을 위치 = 이행이익. 예견 가능·확실성·회피 불가 요건 충족 시 회복.
Hadley v. Baxendale: 결과손해(Consequential)는 계약 체결 시 양측이 예견 가능한 것만. 특수 사정은 사전 고지 필요.
Mitigation: 비위반 당사자는 합리적 조치로 손해 최소화 의무. 유사 대체 기회 거부 시 그 부분 회복 불가.
Jacob & Youngs: 실질적 이행 후 경미 breach → 교체비용 아닌 시장가치 차이(diminution in value).
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Expectation Damages: Put non-breaching party in position had contract been performed. Must be foreseeable, certain, and unavoidable.
Hadley v. Baxendale: Consequential damages recoverable only if within reasonable contemplation of both parties at time of contracting.
Mitigation: Non-breaching party must take reasonable steps to minimize loss. Refusal of comparable substitute = no recovery for that portion.
Jacob & Youngs: Substantial performance + trivial breach → diminution in market value, not cost of replacement.
Q_br1 — Expectation Damages
A homeowner hired a contractor to build an addition for $100,000. The contractor completed the work but used Reading pipe instead of the contractually specified Cohoes pipe. The pipes are functionally identical and the cost to replace them would be $29,000 — nearly 30% of the contract price — while the market value of the house increased by the same amount with either pipe. Under Jacob & Youngs v. Kent, what damages should the homeowner recover?
(A) $29,000 — the cost of replacement to enforce the contract strictly.
(B) Nothing — the contractor substantially performed.
(C) The difference in market value between a house with Reading pipe and Cohoes pipe.
(D) $100,000 — the full contract price withheld as a penalty for breach.
정답: C
In Jacob & Youngs v. Kent, Judge Cardozo held that when a contractor has substantially performed and the breach is unintentional, damages are measured by the diminution in market value — not the cost of replacement — when the cost of completion would be grossly disproportionate to the good to be attained. Since the Reading and Cohoes pipes are functionally equivalent, the difference in market value is likely zero or nominal. The cost-of-replacement measure would result in economic waste.
Q_br2 — Hadley v. Baxendale — Foreseeability
A mill owner sent a broken crankshaft to a carrier for repair with no mention of the urgent nature. The carrier delayed delivery, causing the mill to shut down for extra days and lose profits. The mill owner sues for lost profits. Under the rule of Hadley v. Baxendale, the lost profits are:
(A) Recoverable, because they were the direct result of the carrier's breach.
(B) Recoverable, because the carrier should have foreseen any delay would cause harm.
(C) Not recoverable, because special circumstances were not communicated to the carrier at the time of contracting.
(D) Not recoverable, because lost profits are always too speculative.
정답: C
Under Hadley v. Baxendale, consequential damages are recoverable only if they were within the reasonable contemplation of both parties at the time of contracting. Lost profits from mill shutdown are special/consequential damages. Since the mill owner did not inform the carrier that the crankshaft was the only one and the mill would shut down without it, the carrier could not have foreseen these losses. The rule limits recovery to damages that arise naturally from the breach or were specifically communicated.
Q_br3 — Mitigation
A director under a two-year contract at $100,000/year was wrongfully terminated after six months. She was offered a comparable director position at another studio for the same salary, but declined because she preferred not to work for that studio. She sues for the remaining 18 months of salary. She may recover:
(A) The full 18 months salary, because she is entitled to the benefit of her bargain.
(B) Nothing, because she failed to mitigate damages by accepting the comparable offer.
(C) 6 months salary only, representing the period before she could reasonably have found work.
(D) The full amount minus the salary she actually earned elsewhere.
정답: B
Under Parker v. Twentieth Century-Fox Film Corp., the duty to mitigate requires the non-breaching party to accept substitute employment that is comparable — not different or inferior. Here, the offered position was comparable (same title, same salary, same industry). The director's personal preference for not working at that studio does not excuse her failure to mitigate. By refusing comparable employment, she cannot recover the lost salary she could have earned.
Accord & Satisfaction
📝 핵심 이론
Accord: 기존 의무 대신 다른 이행을 하기로 하는 새 합의. Satisfaction 전까지 기존 의무는 존속.
Satisfaction: 합의된 이행 완료 → 기존 의무 소멸. Accord만 있고 Satisfaction 없으면 원래 의무 + breach 청구 가능.
Full-Payment Check (UCC §3-311): 분쟁 있는 채권에 'Full Payment' 명시 수표를 상대방이 입금하면 자동 accord & satisfaction.
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Accord: New agreement to accept different performance in satisfaction of existing duty. Original duty suspended, not discharged, until satisfaction.
Satisfaction: Performance of the accord discharges both the accord and the original duty. Breach of accord revives original claim.
Full-Payment Check (UCC §3-311): Cashing a check conspicuously marked 'full payment' on a disputed claim = accord and satisfaction.
Q_as1 — Accord & Satisfaction — UCC
A buyer owed $10,000 for goods delivered. The buyer disputed $2,000 in charges, claiming defective delivery. The buyer mailed a check for $8,000 clearly marked 'Full and final payment for all amounts owed.' The seller deposited the check and then sued for the remaining $2,000. Under the UCC, what is the most likely result?
(A) The seller may recover $2,000, because cashing a check does not waive disputed claims under the UCC.
(B) The seller may recover $2,000, because the dispute must be resolved by agreement, not unilateral action.
(C) The seller cannot recover, because depositing the check constituted accord and satisfaction of the disputed amount.
(D) The seller cannot recover, because the check's notation created a binding novation.
정답: C
Under UCC § 3-311, if a check is tendered as full satisfaction of a disputed claim and the check contains a conspicuous statement that it is in full satisfaction, cashing the check constitutes accord and satisfaction. The key elements are: (1) a good-faith dispute, (2) a conspicuous full-payment notation, and (3) the creditor cashes the check. The seller knew of the dispute and the notation — depositing the check binds them to the accord. The seller's remedy was to return the check uncashed.
Third-Party Beneficiary
📝 핵심 이론
Intended Beneficiary: 계약 당사자들이 직접 이익을 주려 했던 제3자 → 독립 청구권 보유.
Incidental Beneficiary: 부수적으로 이익 받는 자 → 청구권 없음 (도서관 건축·고용 예시).
Vesting: 수익자가 신뢰해 행동하거나 소송 제기 시 당사자들 단독 수정·취소 불가.
Creditor Beneficiary: 채권자 지위 제3자도 Intended Beneficiary로 직접 소송 가능.
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Intended Beneficiary: Parties intended to directly benefit the third party — has independent enforcement rights against promisor.
Incidental Beneficiary: Merely benefits as a side effect — no enforceable rights (library construction, hiring provisions).
Vesting: Once beneficiary relies, changes position, or brings suit — parties cannot modify or discharge without consent.
Creditor Beneficiary: Third party to whom promisee owes a debt — can enforce as intended beneficiary.
Q_tpb1 — Intended vs. Incidental Beneficiary
City contracted with Builder to construct a public library. The contract specified that Builder would hire local workers. Smith, an unemployed local resident, was not hired. Smith sues Builder as a third-party beneficiary of the contract. What result?
(A) Smith prevails, because he is a member of the class the contract was designed to benefit.
(B) Smith prevails, because City intended to benefit local workers like Smith.
(C) Smith does not prevail, because he is only an incidental beneficiary — the primary purpose was building the library.
(D) Smith does not prevail, because only government entities can enforce public contracts.
정답: C
An intended beneficiary has enforceable rights under the contract; an incidental beneficiary does not. To be an intended beneficiary, the contracting parties must have intended to confer a direct benefit on that person. Here, the purpose of the contract was to build a library for the public. The hiring provision, while it may benefit local workers incidentally, was not the primary intent of the contract. Smith is an incidental beneficiary and cannot enforce the contract.
Assignment & Delegation
📝 핵심 이론
Assignment (권리 이전): 원칙적으로 가능. Anti-Assignment Clause 위반 = breach지 void 아님 ('shall be void' 명시 시에만 void).
Delegation (의무 이전): Delegatee가 이행해도 Delegator는 여전히 보증인으로 책임. 개인 서비스 의무는 동의 없이 위임 불가.
Novation: 원 당사자를 새 당사자로 완전 대체 → 원 당사자 의무 소멸 (상대방 동의 필수).
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Assignment: Transfer of rights — generally permitted. Anti-assignment clause = breach if violated, NOT void (unless clause says 'void'). Assignor warrants rights exist.
Delegation: Transfer of duties — delegator remains secondarily liable. Personal service obligations cannot be delegated without consent.
Novation: Substitution of new party releases original party — requires obligee's consent. Distinguishable from mere delegation.
Q_ad1 — Anti-Assignment Clause
A contract for consulting services stated 'This contract may not be assigned without the other party's written consent.' The consultant assigned the contract without consent to a qualified sub-consultant. The client seeks to void the assignment. What result?
(A) The assignment is void, because the anti-assignment clause is enforceable.
(B) The assignment is effective, but the assignor is in breach of the anti-assignment clause.
(C) The assignment is void only if the client can show material prejudice.
(D) Anti-assignment clauses are unenforceable as a matter of public policy.
정답: B
Under the Restatement and majority rule, an anti-assignment clause that prohibits assignment without consent does not make the assignment void — it makes the assignment a breach of contract. The assignment is still effective to transfer rights, but the assigning party is liable for breach of the no-assignment covenant. Only language expressly stating the assignment is 'void' or 'invalid' will render it ineffective. The distinction between 'you cannot assign' (breach) and 'any assignment shall be void' (void) is critical on the MBE.
Implied Contract
📝 핵심 이론
Implied-in-Fact Contract: 행위로부터 묵시적 합의 추론 — 말 없어도 행동으로 Mutual Assent 성립 (의식 있는 상태여야).
Quasi-Contract (Implied-in-Law): 합의 없어도 부당이득(Unjust Enrichment) 방지 위해 법이 부과. Restitution interest 측정.
Promissory Estoppel: 약속 + 합리적 신뢰 + 불이익 발생 → Consideration 없어도 약속 집행 (주로 reliance damages).
🇺🇸 Key Rules
Implied-in-Fact Contract: Agreement inferred from conduct — mutual assent established through behavior, not words. Party must be conscious and able to assent.
Quasi-Contract (Implied-in-Law): No agreement required — law imposes obligation to prevent unjust enrichment. Recovery = reasonable value of benefit conferred.
Promissory Estoppel: Promise + reasonable reliance + detrimental change of position → promise enforceable without consideration (reliance damages).
Q_imp_c1 — Implied-in-Fact Contract
Which of the following scenarios most likely creates an implied-in-fact contract?
(A) Ryder is rushed to a hospital emergency room while unconscious. The hospital provides treatment.
(B) A homeowner regularly allows her neighbor to park in her driveway with no discussion of payment.
(C) Neighbor watches Doctor fix his driveway and, when asked afterward, agrees to pay for the work.
(D) Contractor performs landscaping on the wrong house while the owner is away on vacation and unaware.
정답: C
An implied-in-fact contract arises from conduct rather than words — courts infer an agreement from the parties' behavior. The key element is that both parties manifested mutual assent through conduct. In (C), Neighbor observed Doctor fixing the driveway and did not object — this creates a reasonable inference that Neighbor agreed to pay for the benefit received. Contrast (B): Ryder was unconscious, so he could not manifest assent; (A) and (D) also lack the mutual assent element.
